MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 1
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 1

1. A client reports low mood, insomnia, loss of appetite, and fatigue for 3 weeks. Two years
earlier, she had a 10-day period of elevated mood, decreased need for sleep, pressured
speech, and impulsive spending that caused major impairment. Which diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Major depressive disorder
  B. Bipolar I disorder
  C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Bipolar I disorder
  Rationale: A past manic episode causing marked impairment is sufficient for Bipolar I disorder,
even if the current presentation is depressive.

2. A 7-year-old child has persistent difficulty initiating conversation, poor eye contact, limited
peer reciprocity, and restricted repetitive interests present since early childhood. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Social anxiety disorder
  B. Selective mutism
  C. Autism spectrum disorder

 D. Reactive attachment disorder
       Answer: C. Autism spectrum disorder
  Rationale: Persistent social communication deficits plus restricted/repetitive behavior
beginning early in development support autism spectrum disorder.

3. Which feature best distinguishes obsession from delusion?
  A. Obsessions are always mood-congruent
  B. Obsessions are experienced as intrusive and unwanted
  C. Delusions always involve hallucinations

 D. Delusions disappear with reassurance
       Answer: B. Obsessions are experienced as intrusive and unwanted
  Rationale: Obsessions are recurrent intrusive thoughts, urges, or images, typically recognized
as unwanted, unlike fixed false beliefs.

4. A patient presents with auditory hallucinations and persecutory delusions for 4 days after
heavy methamphetamine use, with no prior psychotic history. What is the best initial diagnostic
consideration?

  A. Schizophrenia
  B. Delusional disorder
  C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder
  Rationale: The close temporal link between methamphetamine use and psychosis makes
substance-induced psychosis the best initial diagnosis.
5. A clinician suspects that a patient is intentionally feigning symptoms to avoid criminal liability.
Which condition should be ruled out first?

  A. Factitious disorder
  B. Malingering
  C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Malingering
  Rationale: Feigning for an obvious external incentive such as avoiding criminal liability
suggests malingering.

6. A person has recurrent unexpected panic attacks and has become afraid of leaving home
alone because escape may be difficult if symptoms occur. Which diagnosis best fits?

  A. Panic disorder only
  B. Agoraphobia only
  C. Panic disorder with agoraphobic avoidance

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Panic disorder with agoraphobic avoidance
  Rationale: Unexpected panic attacks plus fear and avoidance of places where escape may be
hard fit panic disorder with agoraphobic features.

7. A college student fears embarrassment in recitations and avoids oral reports, but is
comfortable socializing with close friends. Which diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Avoidant personality disorder
  B. Social anxiety disorder
  C. Panic disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Social anxiety disorder
  Rationale: The fear is focused on social scrutiny and embarrassment in performance
situations.

8. Which statement about generalized anxiety disorder is most accurate?
  A. Worry is confined to panic attacks
  B. Anxiety is restricted to traumatic reminders
  C. Excessive worry is difficult to control and spans multiple domains

 D. The person must have compulsions
       Answer: C. Excessive worry is difficult to control and spans multiple domains
  Rationale: GAD involves persistent, difficult-to-control worry across domains like work, health,
and family.

9. A woman repeatedly checks locks for hours because she fears burglars despite knowing the
fear is excessive. The checking is performed to reduce distress. Which diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
  B. Delusional disorder
  C. Paranoid personality disorder
 D. Specific phobia
       Answer: A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
  Rationale: Intrusive fear plus repetitive checking done to reduce distress is classic OCD.

10. A patient persistently believes that her nose is horribly deformed despite minimal observable
defect and repeatedly seeks cosmetic consultation. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Delusional disorder, grandiose type
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Preoccupation with perceived appearance defects plus repetitive behaviors and
cosmetic seeking fits body dysmorphic disorder.

11. Which feature best differentiates hoarding disorder from obsessive-compulsive disorder?
   A. Hoarding always involves contamination fears
   B. Hoarding is never ego-syntonic
   C. Difficulty discarding possessions is the central and persistent problem

 D. OCD never includes saving behaviors
       Answer: C. Difficulty discarding possessions is the central and persistent problem
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder centers on persistent difficulty discarding possessions
regardless of value.

12. A client develops intrusive memories, nightmares, avoidance, hypervigilance, and
exaggerated startle one month after surviving an armed robbery. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Acute stress disorder
   B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   Rationale: Trauma exposure plus intrusion, avoidance, and arousal symptoms persisting
about a month fits PTSD.

13. A person experiences depersonalization episodes but reality testing remains intact. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Psychotic disorder due to another medical condition
   C. Depersonalization/derealization disorder

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: C. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: Depersonalization with intact reality testing supports
depersonalization/derealization disorder.
14. A patient is preoccupied with having a serious disease despite minimal somatic symptoms
and repeated medical reassurance. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Factitious disorder

 D. Conversion disorder
       Answer: A. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Marked disease preoccupation despite minimal somatic symptoms is illness
anxiety disorder.

15. A patient presents with sudden paralysis of the arm after a family conflict. Neurologic
findings are incompatible with recognized neurological disease. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Malingering
       Answer: B. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Neurological symptoms inconsistent with known disease after psychological
conflict suggest conversion disorder.

16. A client falsifies symptoms and tampers with laboratory specimens to assume the sick role,
without obvious external reward. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Malingering
   C. Factitious disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Factitious disorder
   Rationale: Intentional falsification without obvious external reward supports factitious disorder.

17. Which eating disorder is most strongly characterized by low body weight, intense fear of
gaining weight, and disturbance in body image?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Anorexia nervosa

 D. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: C. Anorexia nervosa
   Rationale: Low weight, fear of weight gain, and body image disturbance define anorexia
nervosa.

18. Recurrent binge eating followed by compensatory vomiting at least once a week for 3
months is most consistent with:

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder
 D. Pica
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Recurrent binge eating with compensatory purging at least weekly for 3 months
defines bulimia nervosa.

19. A person has recurrent binge eating with marked distress but no regular compensatory
behavior. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Anorexia nervosa

 D. Rumination disorder
       Answer: B. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge eating with distress but no regular compensatory behavior is binge-eating
disorder.

20. Persistent difficulty falling asleep despite adequate opportunity for sleep, with daytime
impairment, is most consistent with:

   A. Nightmare disorder
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder only
       Answer: B. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Persistent sleep-initiation difficulty despite adequate opportunity with daytime
impairment fits insomnia disorder.

21. Sudden, irresistible sleep attacks with cataplexy are most suggestive of:
   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Nightmare disorder
   C. Narcolepsy

 D. Sleep terror disorder
       Answer: C. Narcolepsy
   Rationale: Sleep attacks and cataplexy strongly indicate narcolepsy.

22. Which disorder involves repeated failure to resist aggressive impulses resulting in serious
assaultive acts or property destruction disproportionate to provocation?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: C. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: Impulsive aggression grossly out of proportion to provocation is characteristic of
intermittent explosive disorder.
23. A 14-year-old repeatedly bullies peers, steals, lies, and has violated major rules for over a
year. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: B. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Bullying, stealing, deceitfulness, and serious rule violations indicate conduct
disorder.

24. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative behavior, and vindictiveness toward
authority figures without serious rights violations is most consistent with:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. Intermittent explosive disorder
       Answer: B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   Rationale: Angry, argumentative, and vindictive behavior without severe rights violations best
fits ODD.

25. Which substance class is a central nervous system depressant?
   A. Cocaine
   B. Alcohol
   C. Amphetamine

 D. LSD
       Answer: B. Alcohol
   Rationale: Alcohol is a depressant affecting the central nervous system.

26. A patient has tolerance, withdrawal, unsuccessful efforts to cut down, and continued heavy
drinking despite marital problems. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Alcohol intoxication
   B. Alcohol use disorder
   C. Alcohol withdrawal only

 D. Sedative use disorder
       Answer: B. Alcohol use disorder
   Rationale: Tolerance, withdrawal, failed control, and continued use despite harm indicate
alcohol use disorder.

27. Recurrent gambling despite major financial, occupational, and family consequences is
classified under:

   A. Impulse-control disorders only
   B. Substance-related disorders
   C. Addictive disorders
   D. Neurocognitive disorders
  Answer: C. Addictive disorders

   Rationale: Gambling disorder is classified with substance-related and addictive disorders.

28. A patient fluctuates in consciousness, is disoriented, and has acute onset visual
hallucinations after surgery. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Major neurocognitive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Acute fluctuating attention disturbance after surgery with hallucinations is classic
delirium.

29. Progressive memory decline plus impairment in daily functioning due to cognitive
deterioration best supports:

   A. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Cognitive decline that interferes with independence in everyday activities indicates
major neurocognitive disorder.

30. Which feature best characterizes paranoid personality disorder?
   A. Grandiosity and need for admiration
   B. Detachment and indifference to praise or criticism
   C. Pervasive distrust and suspiciousness

 D. Instability of identity and relationships
       Answer: C. Pervasive distrust and suspiciousness
   Rationale: Paranoid personality disorder is defined by chronic suspiciousness and mistrust.

31. A client shows frantic efforts to avoid abandonment, unstable relationships, identity
disturbance, impulsivity, and recurrent self-harm. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Abandonment fears, unstable identity, impulsivity, and self-harm are core
borderline features.

32. Which personality disorder is most associated with disregard for and violation of the rights of
others since age 15?

   A. Narcissistic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: C. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: A pervasive disregard for others' rights since adolescence is central to antisocial
personality disorder.

33. A client believes that casual comments by coworkers contain special messages meant only
for him. This is best described as:

   A. Obsession
   B. Thought insertion
   C. Delusion of reference

 D. Flight of ideas
       Answer: C. Delusion of reference
   Rationale: Believing neutral events contain personal messages is a delusion of reference.

34. Which symptom is classified as a negative symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Hallucinations
   B. Delusions
   C. Avolition

 D. Disorganized speech
       Answer: C. Avolition
   Rationale: Avolition is a negative symptom involving reduced motivation.

35. Continuous signs of disturbance for at least 6 months with active-phase psychotic symptoms
for at least 1 month are most consistent with:

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Schizophrenia
   Rationale: Six months of continuous disturbance with active psychotic symptoms supports
schizophrenia.

36. Which diagnosis requires a major mood episode present for the majority of the total duration
of illness, along with psychotic symptoms and at least 2 weeks of delusions or hallucinations
without mood symptoms?

   A. Bipolar I disorder
   B. Schizoaffective disorder
   C. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoaffective disorder
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires mood episodes for most of illness plus at least 2
weeks of psychosis without mood symptoms.
37. Which disorder best explains a fixed false belief of being loved by a famous person, without
prominent hallucinations or marked functional decline outside the delusional impact?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Delusional disorder
   C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: B. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: A circumscribed nonbizarre or bizarre fixed belief with relatively preserved
functioning fits delusional disorder.

38. A child is inattentive in class, forgetful, loses materials, and is easily distracted in multiple
settings. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. ADHD
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. ADHD
   Rationale: Persistent inattention across settings is characteristic of ADHD.

39. A student of average intelligence has persistent difficulty with word reading accuracy and
spelling despite targeted instruction. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. ADHD
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Language disorder
       Answer: C. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Average intelligence with persistent reading/spelling deficits despite instruction
supports specific learning disorder.

40. Which condition is defined by deficits in intellectual functions and adaptive functioning with
onset during the developmental period?

   A. Specific learning disorder
   B. Intellectual disability
   C. ADHD

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Intellectual disability
   Rationale: Deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning beginning in the developmental
period define intellectual disability.

41. Which feature most strongly supports autism spectrum disorder rather than social anxiety
disorder?

   A. Fear of negative evaluation
   B. Onset after a humiliating social event
   C. Restricted repetitive behaviors and persistent social communication deficits

 D. Panic attacks during performance situations
       Answer: C. Restricted repetitive behaviors and persistent social communication deficits
   Rationale: These developmental deficits distinguish autism from social anxiety.

42. Waxy flexibility, stupor, mutism, and posturing are most characteristic of:
   A. Delirium
   B. Catatonia
   C. Dissociative fugue

 D. Conversion disorder
       Answer: B. Catatonia
   Rationale: Stupor, mutism, posturing, and waxy flexibility are classic catatonic signs.

43. Which classic theorist is most associated with psychoanalytic theory?
   A. Aaron Beck
   B. Sigmund Freud
   C. B. F. Skinner

 D. Albert Bandura
       Answer: B. Sigmund Freud
   Rationale: Freud is the major historical figure associated with psychoanalytic theory.

44. Which early medical figure proposed that abnormal behavior could arise from bodily causes
rather than supernatural possession?

   A. Hippocrates
   B. Mesmer
   C. Pinel

 D. Kraepelin
       Answer: A. Hippocrates
   Rationale: Hippocrates advanced naturalistic explanations for abnormal behavior.

45. Which model emphasizes reciprocal influences among biological, psychological, and social
factors?

   A. Supernatural model
   B. Strict biological reductionism
   C. Integrative multidimensional model

 D. Pure behaviorist model
       Answer: C. Integrative multidimensional model
   Rationale: This model emphasizes interacting biological, psychological, and social influences.

46. Which concept refers to environmental influences on gene expression?
   A. Classical conditioning
   B. Epigenetics
   C. Free association
   D. Projective identification
  Answer: B. Epigenetics

   Rationale: Epigenetics concerns environmental effects on gene expression.

47. Learning through association between two stimuli is called:
   A. Operant conditioning
   B. Classical conditioning
   C. Modeling

 D. Extinction burst
       Answer: B. Classical conditioning
   Rationale: Association between two stimuli defines classical conditioning.

48. Learning that behavior is influenced by its consequences is central to:
   A. Operant conditioning
   B. Psychoanalysis
   C. Humanism

 D. Structuralism
       Answer: A. Operant conditioning
   Rationale: Operant conditioning emphasizes reinforcement and punishment.

49. Which psychologist is most associated with cognitive theory of depression involving
negative automatic thoughts?

   A. Ivan Pavlov
   B. Aaron Beck
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. Alfred Adler
       Answer: B. Aaron Beck
   Rationale: Beck developed the cognitive model highlighting negative automatic thoughts and
schemas.

50. A client begins to avoid elevators after experiencing a panic attack inside one. This is best
explained by:

   A. Positive reinforcement
   B. Classical conditioning with avoidance maintenance
   C. Sublimation

 D. Splitting
       Answer: B. Classical conditioning with avoidance maintenance
   Rationale: The panic attack conditions fear to elevators, and avoidance maintains the fear.

51. Which assessment method provides the richest source of detailed symptom history and
mental status information?

   A. EEG
   B. Clinical interview
   C. MRI
   D. Projective drawing alone
  Answer: B. Clinical interview

   Rationale: The clinical interview is central for detailed history, symptom context, and mental
status.

52. Which is the best reason clinicians must rule out substance use before assigning a primary
psychiatric diagnosis?

   A. Substance use never co-occurs with mental disorder
   B. Substance-related causes are a common source of diagnostic error
   C. Primary disorders are always more severe

 D. Substance use invalidates all symptoms permanently
       Answer: B. Substance-related causes are a common source of diagnostic error
   Rationale: Substances can mimic many disorders, so ruling them out prevents a frequent
diagnostic mistake.

53. When a clinician considers whether symptoms are due to a thyroid disorder, seizure
disorder, or other medical illness, the clinician is completing which differential step?

   A. Rule out malingering only
   B. Rule out substance etiology only
   C. Rule out etiological medical condition

 D. Confirm personality disorder
       Answer: C. Rule out etiological medical condition
   Rationale: Considering medical causes is a distinct differential step after feigning and
substances are considered.

54. Which diagnosis is usually considered when emotional or behavioral symptoms occur in
response to an identifiable stressor but do not meet full criteria for another disorder?

   A. Schizoaffective disorder
   B. Adjustment disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: Stress-linked symptoms that do not meet criteria for another disorder are often
diagnosed as adjustment disorder.

55. Which term refers to intentional fabrication of symptoms for clear external incentives?
   A. Dissimulation
   B. Malingering
   C. Conversion

 D. Factitious disorder
       Answer: B. Malingering
   Rationale: Intentional symptom production for external gain defines malingering.

56. A patient has depressed mood but symptoms began shortly after initiating high-dose
corticosteroids. What is the best initial consideration?
   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder only
   C. Substance/medication-induced depressive disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: C. Substance/medication-induced depressive disorder
   Rationale: A close temporal relation between corticosteroid use and depression suggests
medication-induced depression.

57. In DSM-based diagnosis, which term is used when full criteria are not met but the clinician
wishes to communicate the reason?

   A. Provisional only
   B. Other specified
   C. Major

 D. Residual psychosis
       Answer: B. Other specified
   Rationale: "Other specified" is used when criteria are not fully met but the clinician states why.

58. Which condition is most associated with persistent, free-floating worry rather than discrete
surges of terror?

   A. Panic disorder
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Specific phobia

 D. Social anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Free-floating, chronic worry is more characteristic of GAD than panic disorder.

59. An intense fear triggered specifically by dogs, leading to immediate anxiety and avoidance,
is most consistent with:

   A. Agoraphobia
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Specific phobia

 D. Separation anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Specific phobia
   Rationale: An intense, object-specific fear with avoidance supports specific phobia.

60. Which disorder is characterized by persistent fear of separation from attachment figures
beyond developmental expectations?

   A. Selective mutism
   B. Separation anxiety disorder
   C. Reactive attachment disorder

 D. Agoraphobia
       Answer: B. Separation anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Excessive fear regarding separation from attachment figures beyond expected
developmental level defines this disorder.
61. Mutism that occurs only in specific social settings despite normal speech in other settings is
most consistent with:

   A. Autism spectrum disorder
   B. Selective mutism
   C. Social anxiety disorder only

 D. Language disorder
       Answer: B. Selective mutism
   Rationale: Normal speech in some settings but not others, especially social settings, is
selective mutism.

62. Which diagnosis requires evidence of manic episode?
   A. Bipolar II disorder
   B. Cyclothymic disorder
   C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Bipolar I disorder
   Rationale: A full manic episode is the defining feature for Bipolar I disorder.

63. Hypomania differs from mania primarily because hypomania:
   A. includes psychosis by definition
   B. lasts at least 1 day only
   C. does not cause marked impairment or require hospitalization

 D. cannot include decreased need for sleep
       Answer: C. does not cause marked impairment or require hospitalization
   Rationale: Hypomania resembles mania but is not severe enough to cause marked
impairment or hospitalization, and has no psychosis.

64. Chronic depressed mood for at least 2 years with additional depressive symptoms but no
manic episode is most consistent with:

   A. Bipolar II disorder
   B. Persistent depressive disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
   Rationale: Chronic depression for at least 2 years without mania fits persistent depressive
disorder.

65. Severe recurrent temper outbursts with persistently irritable mood in a child are most
consistent with:

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   D. Bipolar I disorder
  Answer: C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

   Rationale: Severe recurrent temper outbursts plus chronic irritability in a child support DMDD.

66. Which statement best distinguishes grief from major depressive disorder?
   A. Grief never involves sadness
   B. Major depressive disorder never follows bereavement
   C. Grief often preserves capacity for positive emotion and is tied to loss-related yearning

 D. Grief always includes psychomotor retardation
       Answer: C. Grief often preserves capacity for positive emotion and is tied to loss-related
yearning
   Rationale: Grief usually revolves around loss and can coexist with preserved self-esteem and
moments of positive feeling.

67. Recurrent unexplained travel away from home with inability to recall one's past is most
suggestive of:

   A. Dissociative amnesia with fugue
   B. Delirium
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Factitious disorder
       Answer: A. Dissociative amnesia with fugue
   Rationale: Purposeful travel away from home plus autobiographical amnesia suggests
dissociative fugue specifier.

68. Which feature most strongly supports dissociative identity disorder?
   A. Stable identity and intact autobiographical continuity
   B. Two or more distinct personality states with discontinuity in sense of self
   C. A fixed persecutory delusion only

 D. Panic attacks triggered by crowds
       Answer: B. Two or more distinct personality states with discontinuity in sense of self
   Rationale: This is the hallmark of dissociative identity disorder.

69. A patient persistently complains of multiple distressing somatic symptoms with
disproportionate thoughts and anxiety about them. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Factitious disorder

 D. Conversion disorder
       Answer: B. Somatic symptom disorder
   Rationale: The key is distressing somatic symptoms plus excessive thoughts, feelings, or
behaviors about them.

70. Which disorder is characterized by preoccupation with perceived defects in appearance,
repetitive checking, and comparison behaviors?

   A. Hoarding disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Narcissistic personality disorder
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Appearance preoccupation and repetitive checking/comparison are core BDD
features.

71. Which paraphilic disorder involves sexual arousal from observing unsuspecting individuals
who are naked, undressing, or engaging in sexual activity?

   A. Fetishistic disorder
   B. Voyeuristic disorder
   C. Frotteuristic disorder

 D. Sexual masochism disorder
       Answer: B. Voyeuristic disorder
   Rationale: Sexual arousal from observing unsuspecting persons in intimate situations defines
voyeuristic disorder.

72. Recurrent intense sexually arousing fantasies involving prepubescent children, acted upon
or causing marked distress, is most consistent with:

   A. Pedophilic disorder
   B. Exhibitionistic disorder
   C. Fetishistic disorder

 D. Voyeuristic disorder
       Answer: A. Pedophilic disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent sexual arousal involving prepubescent children with action or marked
distress supports pedophilic disorder.

73. Which statement about gender dysphoria is most accurate?
   A. It refers simply to any nonconforming gender expression
   B. It requires distress or impairment related to incongruence between experienced gender

and assigned sex
   C. It is classified as a psychotic disorder

 D. It is identical to sexual dysfunction
       Answer: B. It requires distress or impairment related to incongruence between
experienced gender and assigned sex
   Rationale: Gender dysphoria focuses on distress/impairment associated with gender
incongruence.

74. Which defense mechanism involves channeling unacceptable impulses into socially
acceptable activity?

   A. Projection
   B. Sublimation
   C. Denial
   D. Regression
  Answer: B. Sublimation

   Rationale: Sublimation channels unacceptable impulses into acceptable outlets.

75. Which neurotransmitter has been strongly implicated in reward pathways relevant to
substance use disorders?

   A. Acetylcholine
   B. Dopamine
   C. GABA only

 D. Histamine
       Answer: B. Dopamine
   Rationale: Dopamine is central to reward circuitry implicated in addiction.

76. Which statement best reflects contemporary understanding of causation in
psychopathology?

   A. Disorders arise from a single cause in most cases
   B. Biology alone explains most disorders
   C. Multiple interacting vulnerabilities and stressors are typical

 D. Social factors are secondary and usually irrelevant
       Answer: C. Multiple interacting vulnerabilities and stressors are typical
   Rationale: Modern psychopathology emphasizes interacting biological, psychological, and
social factors.

77. Which legal-ethical issue arises when a clinician may need to protect an identifiable person
from a client's serious threat?

   A. Double-blind design
   B. Duty to warn/protect
   C. Test norming

 D. Countertransference
       Answer: B. Duty to warn/protect
   Rationale: Serious threat to an identifiable person may trigger duty to warn or protect.

78. Under the PAP Code, which is most accurate regarding psychometricians?
   A. They may independently conduct psychotherapy
   B. They may practice therapy if confident in their skills
   C. They operate within RA 10029 boundaries and under supervision of a registered

psychologist when applicable

 D. They may release raw test data to teachers freely
       Answer: C. They operate within RA 10029 boundaries and under supervision of a
registered psychologist when applicable
   Rationale: This directly reflects RA 10029-aligned ethical boundaries for psychometricians.

79. Which practice best aligns with ethical test security?
   A. Sharing answer keys with trainees without supervision
   B. Using photocopied secure test materials for convenience
   C. Restricting test materials to qualified and licensed users

 D. Posting raw items online for transparency
       Answer: C. Restricting test materials to qualified and licensed users
   Rationale: Ethical test security requires secure handling by qualified or licensed personnel
only.

80. Which is ethically most appropriate regarding release of raw test data?
   A. Release all raw scores on request of any family member
   B. Release raw data publicly if diagnosis is serious
   C. Do not release raw and scaled scores except as regulated, such as by court order

 D. Always release test booklets to the client
       Answer: C. Do not release raw and scaled scores except as regulated, such as by court
order
   Rationale: The Code restricts release of raw and scaled scores, client responses, and notes
unless regulated by the court.

81. A psychometrician is asked to provide psychotherapy to a distressed client in a
non-emergency setting. The best response is to:

   A. Start therapy immediately
   B. Provide therapy if the client signs consent
   C. Decline and refer within proper professional boundaries

 D. Provide therapy but avoid documentation
       Answer: C. Decline and refer within proper professional boundaries
   Rationale: Psychometricians are prohibited from therapy outside emergency situations and
should refer appropriately.

82. Which is required in informed consent for assessment under the PAP Code?
   A. Concealing limits of confidentiality
   B. Explaining nature of services, risks, and financial arrangements
   C. Guaranteeing favorable results

 D. Omitting discussion with guardians when the client lacks capacity
       Answer: B. Explaining nature of services, risks, and financial arrangements
   Rationale: Informed consent in assessment includes educating clients about services, risks,
limits of confidentiality, and financial arrangements.

83. A clinician wants to post a testimonial from a former vulnerable client praising treatment
outcome. The PAP Code indicates this is:

   A. Encouraged for public education
   B. Allowed if anonymized
   C. Prohibited when it involves vulnerable current or past clients

 D. Required for transparency
       Answer: C. Prohibited when it involves vulnerable current or past clients
   Rationale: The Code prohibits asking for testimonials from vulnerable current or past clients
and similar persons.
84. Which statement best reflects boundaries of competence?
   A. Practice in any area if licensed in psychology
   B. Provide services only within education, training, supervised experience, and competence
   C. Competence is determined solely by years in practice

 D. Referrals are unethical
       Answer: B. Provide services only within education, training, supervised experience, and
competence
   Rationale: Ethical competence is defined by training, education, supervised experience,
consultation, and related preparation.

85. Which symptom pattern is most characteristic of delirium rather than dementia?
   A. Gradual onset and stable course
   B. Acute fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness
   C. Lifelong social deficits

 D. Fixed delusions without cognitive change
       Answer: B. Acute fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness
   Rationale: This feature distinguishes delirium from more gradual, stable neurocognitive
decline.

86. Which disorder is most associated with odd beliefs, eccentric behavior, and social deficits
without frank psychosis?

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Odd beliefs, eccentricity, and interpersonal deficits without sustained frank
psychosis fit schizotypal PD.

87. A client appears detached from social relationships and shows limited emotional expression
but does not particularly desire close relationships. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Avoidant personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Social anxiety disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Social detachment and restricted affect without strong desire for close bonds
suggest schizoid PD.

88. Which personality disorder is marked by excessive emotionality and attention-seeking?
   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Paranoid personality disorder
   C. Dependent personality disorder
 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: A. Histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Excessive emotionality and attention-seeking are core features of histrionic PD.

89. Which personality disorder is most associated with perfectionism, rigidity, and preoccupation
with orderliness at the expense of flexibility?

   A. OCD
   B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   Rationale: Perfectionism, control, rigidity, and orderliness define OCPD.

90. Which is a hallmark of avoidant personality disorder?
   A. Disregard for rules and rights
   B. Social inhibition due to feelings of inadequacy and hypersensitivity to criticism
   C. Detachment without desire for closeness

 D. Grandiose self-importance
       Answer: B. Social inhibition due to feelings of inadequacy and hypersensitivity to criticism
   Rationale: This captures the essence of avoidant personality disorder.

91. In assessment, which is most essential before interpreting test results?
   A. The client must enjoy the test
   B. The tool must be standardized, valid, and appropriate to the client
   C. The test must always be projective

 D. Computer scoring alone is enough
       Answer: B. The tool must be standardized, valid, and appropriate to the client
   Rationale: Proper interpretation depends on psychometrically sound, appropriate assessment
tools.

92. Which statement best describes comorbidity?
   A. A diagnostic error in all cases
   B. The presence of two or more disorders in the same person
   C. A subtype of psychosis

 D. A measure of treatment response
       Answer: B. The presence of two or more disorders in the same person
   Rationale: Comorbidity refers to coexistence of multiple disorders.

93. Which factor most increases suspicion of malingering?
   A. Symptoms causing clear personal distress
   B. Lack of insight
   C. Clear external incentive such as financial compensation or avoiding legal responsibility
   D. Early developmental onset
  Answer: C. Clear external incentive such as financial compensation or avoiding legal

responsibility
   Rationale: Obvious secondary gain heightens suspicion of malingering.

94. Which diagnosis is most appropriate when psychotic symptoms last less than 1 month and
full return to premorbid functioning occurs?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Psychosis under 1 month with return to baseline is brief psychotic disorder.

95. Which diagnosis is most appropriate when schizophrenia-like symptoms last more than 1
month but less than 6 months?

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophreniform disorder
   Rationale: Schizophrenia-like symptoms lasting 1 to under 6 months support
schizophreniform disorder.

96. Which feature best distinguishes delusional disorder from schizophrenia?
   A. Delusions are absent
   B. Hallucinations are always prominent
   C. Functioning is relatively preserved aside from delusional impact

 D. Mood episodes are always present
       Answer: C. Functioning is relatively preserved aside from delusional impact
   Rationale: Delusional disorder usually preserves broader functioning better than
schizophrenia.

97. A patient with severe depression hears voices only during depressive episodes. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Schizoaffective disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   Rationale: When psychosis occurs only during depressive episodes, MDD with psychotic
features is most likely.

98. Which statement about confidentiality is most accurate under the PAP Code?
   A. It never has exceptions
   B. It may be limited by law, imminent danger, or legitimate court request
   C. It applies only to therapy, not assessment

 D. It does not apply to telepsychology
       Answer: B. It may be limited by law, imminent danger, or legitimate court request
   Rationale: The Code recognizes limits to confidentiality in legally mandated situations and
serious danger.

99. A psychologist is asked to explain test findings to parents and teachers. Which is most
appropriate?

   A. Use only technical jargon to preserve authority
   B. Explain results in nontechnical language appropriate to recipients
   C. Release all raw materials instead

 D. Refuse all explanation
       Answer: B. Explain results in nontechnical language appropriate to recipients
   Rationale: Ethical explanation of assessment results to relatives, parents, or teachers should
use nontechnical language.

100. Which action is most ethical when a practitioner becomes aware that a colleague likely
violated the Code and substantial harm may result?

    A. Ignore it to protect collegiality
    B. Post accusations on social media
    C. Take further action and report to appropriate authority if informal resolution is insufficient
and confidentiality is not violated

 D. File a complaint without evidence
        Answer: C. Take further action and report to appropriate authority if informal resolution is
insufficient and confidentiality is not violated
    Rationale: The PAP Code allows informal resolution first, but requires further reporting when
substantial harm is likely and confidentiality is not breached.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 2
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 2

1. A client reports recurrent distress and marked occupational impairment after weeks of
persistent fear, insomnia, and avoidance. Which feature most strongly supports classifying the
presentation as a mental disorder rather than a transient normal reaction?

  A. The symptoms are unusual to the clinician
  B. The presentation causes clinically significant distress or impairment
  C. The client can describe the symptoms clearly

 D. The symptoms began after a stressor
       Answer: B. The presentation causes clinically significant distress or impairment
  Rationale: Clinically significant distress or impairment is a core threshold for diagnosing a
mental disorder; symptoms alone are not sufficient.

2. In comprehensive differential diagnosis, which step should generally be ruled out first
because it can invalidate the accuracy of the entire assessment?

  A. Personality disorder
  B. Malingering or factitious presentation
  C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Neurocognitive disorder
       Answer: B. Malingering or factitious presentation
  Rationale: Feigned or intentionally produced symptoms can undermine diagnostic validity, so
they must be ruled out early.

3. A client has panic-like symptoms after heavy stimulant use and none when abstinent. What is
the most appropriate initial diagnostic inference?

  A. Primary panic disorder
  B. Substance/medication-induced anxiety disorder
  C. Generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Substance/medication-induced anxiety disorder
  Rationale: Symptoms linked to substance use and resolving with abstinence indicate a
substance-induced condition.

4. A 52-year-old with abrupt-onset obsessive symptoms after a neurological illness is being
assessed. Which principle is most important?

  A. Assume a primary obsessive-compulsive disorder because obsessions are present
  B. Consider a disorder due to another medical condition because late or atypical onset
warrants medical evaluation
  C. Diagnose illness anxiety disorder because health issues are involved

 D. Delay diagnosis until symptoms have persisted for one year
       Answer: B. Consider a disorder due to another medical condition because late or atypical
onset warrants medical evaluation
  Rationale: Late or atypical onset suggests possible medical etiology requiring careful rule-out.

5. Which best reflects the integrative approach to psychopathology?
  A. Mental disorders are explained adequately by one dominant cause
  B. Biological factors are primary and psychosocial factors are secondary
  C. Psychological disorders arise from interacting biological, psychological, and social

influences
  D. Only environmental learning histories matter for diagnosis
  Answer: C. Psychological disorders arise from interacting biological, psychological, and

social influences
  Rationale: The integrative model emphasizes interaction of multiple contributing factors.

6. Which research design provides the strongest basis for inferring that a treatment caused
improvement in symptoms?

  A. Cross-sectional survey
  B. Case report
  C. Randomized experiment

 D. Archival chart review
       Answer: C. Randomized experiment
  Rationale: Randomized experiments allow control of variables and strongest causal inference.

7. A psychometrician administers an intelligence test to a child whose native language differs
from the test norms. What is the most defensible interpretation?

  A. The obtained IQ score alone is sufficient for diagnosis
  B. Scores must be interpreted cautiously in light of sociocultural and language factors
  C. Language differences matter only for projective tests

 D. Adaptive functioning is irrelevant once a formal test score is available
       Answer: B. Scores must be interpreted cautiously in light of sociocultural and language
factors
  Rationale: Cultural and linguistic context affects validity of test results.

8. Which statement about abnormal behavior is most accurate from a PRC board perspective?
  A. Behavior that departs from social norms is always pathological
  B. Distress, dysfunction, and cultural context all matter in determining abnormality
  C. Only biological markers define mental disorder

 D. Any severe symptom automatically warrants diagnosis
       Answer: B. Distress, dysfunction, and cultural context all matter in determining abnormality
  Rationale: Modern definitions include distress, dysfunction, and cultural considerations.

9. A clinician is deciding whether a patient's grief-related sadness qualifies as a depressive
disorder. Which principle best applies?

  A. Any sadness after loss should be diagnosed if intense
  B. Clinical judgment must distinguish normal but painful bereavement from a mental disorder
  C. Bereavement never co-occurs with depression

 D. The presence of insomnia alone confirms major depression
       Answer: B. Clinical judgment must distinguish normal but painful bereavement from a
mental disorder
  Rationale: Differential diagnosis requires distinguishing normal grief from pathology.

10. Which pioneer is most strongly associated with psychoanalysis and unconscious conflict?
   A. Ivan Pavlov
   B. Sigmund Freud
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: B. Sigmund Freud
   Rationale: Freud developed psychoanalytic theory emphasizing unconscious processes.

11. A patient has excessive worry occurring more days than not across work, finances, and
family, with muscle tension and sleep disturbance. Which diagnosis is most consistent?
   A. Panic disorder
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Specific phobia

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Persistent, excessive, and uncontrollable worry across multiple domains with
physical symptoms characterizes generalized anxiety disorder.

12. A student experiences sudden surges of intense fear with palpitations and fear of dying,
then begins avoiding malls and buses because escape might be difficult. Which pair best fits?

   A. Generalized anxiety disorder and illness anxiety disorder
   B. Panic disorder and agoraphobia
   C. Specific phobia and acute stress disorder

 D. Social anxiety disorder and OCD
       Answer: B. Panic disorder and agoraphobia
   Rationale: Recurrent panic attacks followed by avoidance of situations where escape is
difficult indicates panic disorder with agoraphobia.

13. A child speaks freely at home but persistently fails to speak at school despite normal
language ability. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Autism spectrum disorder
   B. Selective mutism
   C. Social communication disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Selective mutism
   Rationale: Consistent failure to speak in specific social settings despite ability elsewhere
defines selective mutism.

14. A woman is terrified only of elevators and goes to great lengths to avoid them, while
functioning well otherwise. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Specific phobia
   B. Agoraphobia
   C. Panic disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: A. Specific phobia
   Rationale: Fear limited to a specific object or situation with avoidance is characteristic of
specific phobia.

15. Which learning concept best explains why fear develops rapidly for some stimuli such as
snakes or heights but not for electrical outlets?

   A. Extinction
   B. Prepared learning
   C. Negative reinforcement

 D. Response cost
       Answer: B. Prepared learning
   Rationale: Evolutionarily predisposed fear responses develop more easily for certain stimuli.

16. A man repeatedly washes his hands for hours because of intrusive contamination thoughts
that he recognizes as excessive. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   B. Illness anxiety disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   Rationale: Presence of intrusive obsessions and repetitive compulsions with insight supports
OCD.

17. A client is preoccupied with a slight flaw in appearance and repeatedly checks mirrors,
seeking reassurance and considering unnecessary cosmetic procedures. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Excessive preoccupation with perceived physical defects and repetitive behaviors
defines body dysmorphic disorder.

18. Which feature most strongly differentiates hoarding disorder from ordinary collecting?
   A. Preference for antique items
   B. Difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value, causing clutter and impairment
   C. Strong sentimental attachment to family objects only

 D. Owning many items in a neatly organized storage room
       Answer: B. Difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value, causing clutter
and impairment
   Rationale: Hoarding involves persistent difficulty discarding items leading to functional
impairment.

19. Following a traumatic assault, a client has intrusive memories, avoidance, hypervigilance,
and functional impairment for 10 days. Which diagnosis is most likely if full criteria are met?

   A. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   B. Acute stress disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Acute stress disorder
   Rationale: Symptoms occurring within one month of trauma suggest acute stress disorder.

20. A nurse develops nightmares, intrusive recollections, avoidance, and exaggerated startle
response for 3 months after witnessing a fatal ICU incident. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Acute stress disorder
   B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   C. Generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   Rationale: Trauma-related symptoms persisting beyond one month meet criteria for PTSD.

21. A patient has multiple distressing bodily symptoms, frequent doctor visits, and
disproportionate thoughts about symptom seriousness despite negative workups. Which
diagnosis fits best?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Factitious disorder
   D. Panic disorder
  Answer: B. Somatic symptom disorder

   Rationale: Significant distress about multiple somatic symptoms despite medical reassurance
defines somatic symptom disorder.

22. A woman with minimal physical symptoms is persistently convinced she has a serious
undetected disease and repeatedly seeks reassurance online and from physicians. The best
diagnosis is:

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Illness anxiety disorder
   C. Delusional disorder, somatic type

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Preoccupation with having illness despite minimal symptoms characterizes illness
anxiety disorder.

23. After an argument, a client suddenly develops unilateral arm weakness inconsistent with
neurological examination, with no evidence of malingering. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Conversion disorder
   B. Factitious disorder
   C. Major neurocognitive disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: A. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Neurological symptoms incompatible with medical findings indicate conversion
disorder.

24. A client reports feeling detached from self, as if observing life from outside the body, while
reality testing remains intact. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Psychotic disorder
   B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   C. Dissociative identity disorder

 D. Delirium
       Answer: B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: Persistent feelings of detachment with intact reality testing define this disorder.

25. Which feature most strongly supports dissociative identity disorder over malingering?
   A. Symptoms emerge only during litigation
   B. Stable pattern of identity disruption with recurrent gaps in recall and significant impairment
   C. Client reports many dramatic symptoms matching popular media depictions exactly

 D. Symptoms disappear when collateral information is requested
       Answer: B. Stable pattern of identity disruption with recurrent gaps in recall and significant
impairment
   Rationale: Consistent identity disruption and amnesia support genuine dissociative disorder.

26. A patient has depressed mood, anhedonia, early morning awakening, reduced appetite,
guilt, and poor concentration for 3 weeks. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder
   Rationale: Presence of multiple depressive symptoms for at least two weeks indicates major
depressive disorder.

27. A woman reports depressed mood for years, describing herself as 'never really okay,' with
low energy and hopelessness but no history of mania. Which diagnosis fits best?

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. Persistent depressive disorder
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
   Rationale: Chronic low mood lasting years without mania defines persistent depressive
disorder.

28. Which statement best distinguishes bipolar I disorder from bipolar II disorder?
   A. Bipolar II includes psychosis but bipolar I does not
   B. Bipolar I requires at least one manic episode, whereas bipolar II requires hypomania plus

major depression
   C. Bipolar I is less impairing than bipolar II

 D. Bipolar II can be diagnosed without mood episodes
       Answer: B. Bipolar I requires at least one manic episode, whereas bipolar II requires
hypomania plus major depression
   Rationale: Presence of full manic episode distinguishes bipolar I from bipolar II.

29. A highly energetic entrepreneur sleeps 2 hours nightly for a week, is grandiose, starts
reckless investments, and requires hospitalization. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Substance intoxication
   C. Manic episode consistent with bipolar I disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Manic episode consistent with bipolar I disorder
   Rationale: Severe impairment and hospitalization indicate full manic episode.

30. Which is a well-established major risk factor for suicide completion?
   A. Being physically attractive
   B. Having a detailed plan and access to lethal means
   C. Preferring to be alone occasionally

 D. Having mild exam anxiety
       Answer: B. Having a detailed plan and access to lethal means
   Rationale: Access to means and specific planning significantly increase suicide risk.

31. An underweight adolescent intensely fears gaining weight and persists in restrictive eating
despite medical compromise and body-image disturbance. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   C. Anorexia nervosa

 D. Binge-eating disorder
       Answer: C. Anorexia nervosa
   Rationale: Restriction of intake, fear of weight gain, and body image disturbance define
anorexia nervosa.
32. A normal-weight college student has recurrent binge eating followed by self-induced
vomiting and excessive concern with body shape. Which diagnosis fits best?

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder

 D. Body dysmorphic disorder
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Binge eating with compensatory behaviors such as vomiting characterizes bulimia
nervosa.

33. A patient has recurrent episodes of objectively large food intake with loss of control, marked
distress, and no regular purging. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Binge-eating disorder
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Anorexia nervosa, binge-eating/purging type

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: A. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent binge episodes without compensatory behaviors define binge-eating
disorder.

34. A child avoids many foods because of sensory characteristics and has weight loss but no
fear of fatness. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   C. Obsessive-compulsive disorder

 D. Bulimia nervosa
       Answer: B. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   Rationale: Food restriction without body image disturbance points to ARFID.

35. A client reports dissatisfaction with sleep quantity and quality, difficulty initiating sleep, and
daytime fatigue for months despite adequate opportunity for sleep. Which diagnosis fits best?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Narcolepsy

 D. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder
       Answer: A. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Persistent difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep with impairment defines insomnia
disorder.

36. A patient sleeps long hours, feels unrefreshed, and has excessive daytime sleepiness
without evidence of insufficient sleep. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Sleep terror disorder

 D. Nightmare disorder
       Answer: B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   Rationale: Excessive sleepiness despite adequate sleep duration indicates hypersomnolence
disorder.

37. A man experiences sudden daytime sleep attacks and episodes of loss of muscle tone
triggered by laughter. Which diagnosis is most consistent?
   A. Narcolepsy
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Delirium
       Answer: A. Narcolepsy
   Rationale: Sleep attacks and cataplexy are hallmark features of narcolepsy.

38. A woman has persistent lack of sexual interest causing personal distress, without a better
medical or relational explanation. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Female sexual interest/arousal disorder
   B. Gender dysphoria
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Voyeuristic disorder
       Answer: A. Female sexual interest/arousal disorder
   Rationale: Persistent lack of sexual interest with distress defines this disorder.

39. Which statement best distinguishes a paraphilic interest from a paraphilic disorder?
   A. A paraphilic interest is always criminal
   B. A paraphilic disorder requires distress, impairment, or acted-on behavior involving a

nonconsenting person
   C. A paraphilic interest always involves psychosis

 D. There is no difference between the two
       Answer: B. A paraphilic disorder requires distress, impairment, or acted-on behavior
involving a nonconsenting person
   Rationale: Diagnosis requires harm, impairment, or risk to others.

40. A teenager experiences marked distress because gender identity is incongruent with sex
assigned at birth. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Gender dysphoria
   B. Transvestic disorder
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Gender dysphoria
   Rationale: Distress from gender incongruence defines gender dysphoria.

41. Which diagnosis is most appropriate for a person who continues alcohol use despite
repeated interpersonal, occupational, and health consequences?

   A. Alcohol intoxication only
   B. Alcohol use disorder
   C. Major depressive disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: B. Alcohol use disorder
   Rationale: Continued use despite consequences indicates substance use disorder.

42. A patient becomes tremulous, anxious, diaphoretic, and tachycardic after abruptly stopping
heavy alcohol consumption. Which is the best immediate formulation?

   A. Alcohol withdrawal
   B. Opioid intoxication
   C. Cannabis use disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: A. Alcohol withdrawal
   Rationale: Physiological symptoms after cessation indicate withdrawal.

43. Compared with depressants, stimulants are more likely to produce which acute
presentation?

   A. Psychomotor retardation and slurred speech
   B. Euphoria, decreased need for sleep, and possible paranoia
   C. Profound sedation with pinpoint pupils

 D. Marked amnesia with confabulation
       Answer: B. Euphoria, decreased need for sleep, and possible paranoia
   Rationale: Stimulants increase energy and may cause paranoia.

44. Which principle best explains why substance-induced disorders are often missed in clinical
settings?

   A. Substances rarely affect mental status
   B. Substance use commonly co-occurs with psychiatric symptoms and may mimic many
disorders
   C. Laboratory testing is never useful

 D. Substance-induced syndromes occur only with illegal drugs
       Answer: B. Substance use commonly co-occurs with psychiatric symptoms and may
mimic many disorders
   Rationale: Overlapping symptoms complicate diagnosis.

45. A patient is unable to resist urges to gamble, keeps chasing losses, lies about it, and suffers
serious financial impairment. Which diagnosis fits best?

   A. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   B. Gambling disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Pyromania
       Answer: B. Gambling disorder
   Rationale: Persistent problematic gambling behavior defines gambling disorder.

46. Which diagnosis is characterized by recurrent behavioral outbursts representing failure to
control aggressive impulses that are grossly out of proportion to provocation?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Oppositional defiant disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: Disproportionate aggressive outbursts define this condition.

47. A person repeatedly steals unneeded low-value items and feels tension before the act and
relief afterward. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Kleptomania
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: A. Kleptomania
   Rationale: Impulse-control disorder with tension-relief cycle.

48. Deliberately setting fires on more than one occasion for pleasure, fascination, or relief from
tension is most characteristic of:
   A. Pyromania
   B. Manic episode
   C. Conduct disorder

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: A. Pyromania
   Rationale: Recurrent fire-setting for gratification defines pyromania.

49. Which cognitive factor is commonly implicated in the maintenance of substance-related
disorders?

   A. Realistic appraisal of risk only
   B. Expectation that the substance will reduce distress or enhance functioning
   C. Absence of craving

 D. High tolerance for frustration
       Answer: B. Expectation that the substance will reduce distress or enhance functioning
   Rationale: Expectancies reinforce continued use.

50. A person with stimulant use develops paranoia and auditory hallucinations during heavy
use, which resolve after cessation. Which diagnosis is best supported?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Stimulant-induced psychotic disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: B. Stimulant-induced psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Psychosis linked to substance use supports substance-induced disorder.

51. Which statement best characterizes personality disorders?
   A. They are always episodic and brief
   B. They are enduring patterns of inner experience and behavior that are inflexible and

maladaptive
   C. They occur only during intoxication

 D. They are diagnosed only when psychosis is present
       Answer: B. They are enduring patterns of inner experience and behavior that are inflexible
and maladaptive
   Rationale: Personality disorders are chronic and pervasive.

52. A pervasive pattern of distrust and suspicion such that others' motives are interpreted as
malevolent is most consistent with:

   A. Paranoid personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: A. Paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Core feature is pervasive mistrust.

53. A man shows detachment from social relationships and little desire for close relationships,
appearing emotionally cold. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Paranoid personality disorder

 D. Histrionic personality disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Social detachment and restricted affect define schizoid PD.

54. Eccentric behavior, odd beliefs, and interpersonal deficits with discomfort in close
relationships most strongly suggest:

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Major depressive disorder
       Answer: A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Odd beliefs and social discomfort characterize schizotypal PD.

55. Repeated unlawful behavior, deceitfulness, impulsivity, aggressiveness, and lack of remorse
beginning since adolescence is most consistent with:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Conduct disorder only
       Answer: B. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Persistent violation of others' rights defines antisocial PD.

56. Identity disturbance, frantic efforts to avoid abandonment, recurrent self-harm, and affective
instability are most characteristic of:

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Instability and fear of abandonment are key features.

57. A client is excessively emotional, theatrical, and uncomfortable when not the center of
attention. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Narcissistic personality disorder
   B. Histrionic personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: B. Histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Attention-seeking and emotionality define histrionic PD.

58. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy are hallmark features of:
   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Core traits include grandiosity and lack of empathy.

59. Which personality disorder is most associated with social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy,
and hypersensitivity to negative evaluation?

   A. Avoidant personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder
 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: A. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Social inhibition and fear of rejection define avoidant PD.

60. A person is excessively submissive, has difficulty making everyday decisions without
reassurance, and fears separation because of inability to care for self. Which diagnosis fits
best?

   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Paranoid personality disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: A. Dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Excessive reliance on others and fear of separation characterize dependent PD.

61. Which symptom is classified as a positive symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Avolition
   B. Flat affect
   C. Hallucinations

 D. Alogia
       Answer: C. Hallucinations
   Rationale: Positive symptoms reflect an excess or distortion of normal functions, such as
hallucinations.

62. Avolition and diminished emotional expression in schizophrenia are best described as:
   A. Positive symptoms
   B. Negative symptoms
   C. Catatonic symptoms only

 D. Somatic symptoms
       Answer: B. Negative symptoms
   Rationale: Negative symptoms involve deficits in normal emotional and motivational
functioning.

63. A client has delusions, hallucinations, disorganized speech, and marked functional decline
for 2 months. Which diagnosis is most likely if criteria are otherwise met?

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophreniform disorder
   Rationale: Duration of 1Ł6 months with schizophrenia-like symptoms fits schizophreniform
disorder.

64. A patient has prominent psychotic symptoms for 1 week following a severe stressor and
then returns to premorbid functioning. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Schizoaffective disorder
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: C. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Psychotic symptoms lasting less than 1 month with full recovery define brief
psychotic disorder.

65. Which feature most strongly differentiates schizoaffective disorder from a mood disorder
with psychotic features?

   A. Psychosis occurs only during mood episodes
   B. There is a period of psychosis in the absence of a major mood episode
   C. Negative symptoms are absent

 D. There is no functional impairment
       Answer: B. There is a period of psychosis in the absence of a major mood episode
   Rationale: Independent psychotic episodes distinguish schizoaffective disorder.

66. A patient has one persistent, nonbizarre persecutory delusion for 8 months with otherwise
relatively preserved functioning and no prominent disorganization. Which diagnosis is most
likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: A. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: Presence of a single persistent delusion with minimal impairment defines
delusional disorder.

67. Which historical figure is closely associated with early descriptions of dementia praecox, a
precursor concept to schizophrenia?

   A. Emil Kraepelin
   B. Carl Rogers
   C. Francis Galton

 D. Alfred Adler
       Answer: A. Emil Kraepelin
   Rationale: Kraepelin described dementia praecox as an early concept of schizophrenia.

68. A patient remains mute, immobile, and postured for prolonged periods. Which syndrome
should be strongly considered?

   A. Catatonia
   B. Delirium only
   C. Aphasia

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: A. Catatonia
   Rationale: Motor immobility, mutism, and posturing are classic catatonic features.

69. Why is culture important in the diagnosis of psychotic-like experiences?
   A. Because all unusual beliefs are psychotic in every culture
   B. Because culturally sanctioned beliefs and experiences must be distinguished from

psychopathology
   C. Because culture matters only in children

 D. Because hallucinations cannot occur outside psychosis
       Answer: B. Because culturally sanctioned beliefs and experiences must be distinguished
from psychopathology
   Rationale: Cultural context determines whether experiences are pathological.
70. Which treatment statement is most accurate for schizophrenia?
   A. Medication is never indicated
   B. Antipsychotic medication and psychosocial intervention are often combined
   C. Psychotherapy alone always cures schizophrenia

 D. Hospitalization is required lifelong for all cases
       Answer: B. Antipsychotic medication and psychosocial intervention are often combined
   Rationale: Combined treatment approaches yield best outcomes.

71. A child shows persistent inattention across home and school, frequently loses materials, is
forgetful, and struggles to sustain mental effort. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Specific learning disorder
   B. Attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   C. Generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   Rationale: Pervasive inattention across settings indicates ADHD.

72. Which feature best differentiates ADHD from a primary anxiety disorder in a child with
concentration problems?

   A. ADHD symptoms are usually situational only
   B. ADHD typically begins early and appears across multiple settings, not only during
worry-provoking situations
   C. Anxiety always includes hyperactivity

 D. ADHD can be diagnosed only if intelligence is below average
       Answer: B. ADHD typically begins early and appears across multiple settings, not only
during worry-provoking situations
   Rationale: ADHD is pervasive and early-onset, unlike situational anxiety-related inattention.

73. A bright student has persistent marked difficulty in reading accuracy and spelling despite
adequate education and effort. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. Specific learning disorder
   C. ADHD

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Specific deficits in academic skills despite normal intelligence define SLD.

74. A child has deficits in social reciprocity, limited eye contact, and restricted repetitive
behaviors. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. Selective mutism

 D. Specific learning disorder
       Answer: B. Autism spectrum disorder
   Rationale: Social communication deficits with repetitive behaviors define ASD.

75. Which statement about intellectual disability is most accurate?
   A. IQ score alone is sufficient for diagnosis
   B. Diagnosis requires both deficits in intellectual functions and deficits in adaptive functioning
   C. Adaptive functioning does not matter if test scores are low
   D. The diagnosis can be made only in adulthood
  Answer: B. Diagnosis requires both deficits in intellectual functions and deficits in adaptive

functioning
   Rationale: Both intellectual and adaptive impairments are required.

76. An older hospitalized patient becomes acutely disoriented, has fluctuating attention, and
worsens at night after an infection. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Major neurocognitive disorder
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Acute onset, fluctuating consciousness, and medical cause define delirium.

77. Which feature best differentiates major neurocognitive disorder from delirium?
   A. Major neurocognitive disorder usually has abrupt fluctuation in attention over hours
   B. Delirium always lasts years
   C. Major neurocognitive disorder generally shows a more persistent cognitive decline without

the marked acute fluctuation of delirium

 D. Delirium never has a medical cause
       Answer: C. Major neurocognitive disorder generally shows a more persistent cognitive
decline without the marked acute fluctuation of delirium
   Rationale: Dementia is chronic and progressive, unlike acute fluctuating delirium.

78. A patient with slowly progressive memory decline and impaired daily functioning most likely
has which type of syndrome?

   A. Delirium
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Progressive cognitive decline affecting functioning defines major neurocognitive
disorder.

79. In evaluating suspected intellectual disability, which statement is most defensible?
   A. Group screening tests are always sufficient
   B. Clinical judgment remains essential in interpreting cognitive and adaptive data
   C. Only verbal ability matters

 D. Adaptive behavior should be ignored if the IQ score is below 70
       Answer: B. Clinical judgment remains essential in interpreting cognitive and adaptive data
   Rationale: Diagnosis requires integrated interpretation, not scores alone.

80. Which disorder is most likely to be confused with dementia when acute confusion is
prominent, but differs because attention fluctuates markedly and onset is abrupt?

   A. Generalized anxiety disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Persistent depressive disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Acute onset and fluctuating attention distinguish delirium from dementia.
81. Under Republic Act No. 10029, which activity is explicitly within the authorized functions of a
psychometrician only when conducted under supervision of a licensed psychologist?

   A. Independent psychotherapy
   B. Administering and scoring objective personality tests and preparing a report
   C. Conducting unsupervised projective testing

 D. Issuing final independent clinical diagnoses
       Answer: B. Administering and scoring objective personality tests and preparing a report
   Rationale: Psychometricians may administer and score tests under supervision, not
independently diagnose.

82. Which practice would most clearly violate RA 10029 and PAP ethics?
   A. A licensed psychometrician administering a structured test under supervision
   B. An unlicensed person presenting himself as a psychometrician and offering testing

services
   C. A psychologist supervising test administration

 D. A psychometrician obtaining informed consent before assessment
       Answer: B. An unlicensed person presenting himself as a psychometrician and offering
testing services
   Rationale: Misrepresentation and unlicensed practice violate the law.

83. A psychometrician is asked to administer a projective test independently because the
psychologist is unavailable. What is the most ethical response?

   A. Proceed because all tests are basically similar
   B. Decline and explain that the task exceeds authorized competence and scope
