   C. Administer it but omit interpretation

 D. Let an intern do it instead
       Answer: B. Decline and explain that the task exceeds authorized competence and scope
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires staying within scope and competence.

84. Which is the best application of informed consent in psychological assessment?
   A. Obtain consent only after testing so the client is not influenced
   B. Explain the nature, purpose, probable uses, and limits of confidentiality in understandable

language before assessment
   C. Consent is unnecessary when a fee is paid

 D. Written consent is required only for psychotherapy, never assessment
       Answer: B. Explain the nature, purpose, probable uses, and limits of confidentiality in
understandable language before assessment
   Rationale: Informed consent requires clear explanation prior to assessment.

85. A school asks for an adolescent's test results. The adolescent was evaluated at the parents'
request. Ethically, the assessor should first:

   A. Release the full report immediately because schools are helping institutions
   B. Clarify who the client is, the purpose of disclosure, and the limits of confidentiality
   C. Refuse all communication under any circumstance

 D. Share only the IQ score without explanation
       Answer: B. Clarify who the client is, the purpose of disclosure, and the limits of
confidentiality
   Rationale: Proper handling of confidentiality requires role clarification.

86. A psychometrician begins seeing a close friend as an assessment client because 'it will be
easier.' Which ethical issue is most directly raised?
   A. Prepared learning
   B. Multiple relationship and potential impairment of objectivity
   C. Somatic preoccupation

 D. Projective validity
       Answer: B. Multiple relationship and potential impairment of objectivity
   Rationale: Dual relationships risk bias and ethical violations.

87. A practitioner is asked to provide online assessment using unfamiliar digital procedures.
Which response is most ethical?

   A. Proceed immediately because telepsychology has no special standards
   B. Undertake relevant training, consultation, or study before offering the service beyond
current competence
   C. Offer the service but tell the client accuracy is not guaranteed

 D. Transfer all responsibility to the software provider
       Answer: B. Undertake relevant training, consultation, or study before offering the service
beyond current competence
   Rationale: Competence must be ensured before providing services.

88. When organizational demands conflict with the Code of Ethics, the practitioner should:
   A. Automatically follow the organization
   B. Make the Code known to the organization and attempt to resolve the conflict while

adhering to ethics
   C. Ignore the issue unless a complaint is filed

 D. Resign immediately in every case
       Answer: B. Make the Code known to the organization and attempt to resolve the conflict
while adhering to ethics
   Rationale: Ethical obligations take precedence and require resolution efforts.

89. A psychometrician is experiencing serious personal problems that may impair competent
performance. According to ethics, the best course is to:

   A. Continue working normally to avoid losing income
   B. Take appropriate measures such as consultation and consider limiting, suspending, or
terminating duties if needed
   C. Keep working but avoid documentation

 D. Transfer all cases without informing anyone
       Answer: B. Take appropriate measures such as consultation and consider limiting,
suspending, or terminating duties if needed
   Rationale: Practitioners must ensure competence and protect clients.

90. A client tested positive for severe suicidal intent during assessment. Which ethical principle
takes priority in deciding next steps?

   A. Never break confidentiality under any circumstance
   B. Protect welfare and take reasonable steps to prevent serious harm, consistent with law
and ethical limits
   C. Wait for the next session because rapport is more important

 D. Release all records publicly so others can help
       Answer: B. Protect welfare and take reasonable steps to prevent serious harm, consistent
with law and ethical limits
   Rationale: Duty to protect overrides confidentiality when safety is at risk.

91. Which pair is correctly matched?
   A. Classical conditioning -- B. F. Skinner
   B. Client-centered therapy -- Carl Rogers
   C. Cognitive therapy -- Sigmund Freud

 D. Psychoanalysis -- Ivan Pavlov
       Answer: B. Client-centered therapy -- Carl Rogers
   Rationale: Rogers developed client-centered therapy.

92. A patient with chronic worry avoids uncertainty by constant reassurance seeking, which
temporarily reduces anxiety and thereby strengthens the behavior. This is best explained by:

   A. Positive punishment
   B. Negative reinforcement
   C. Classical extinction

 D. Flooding
       Answer: B. Negative reinforcement
   Rationale: Behavior is maintained because it reduces anxiety.

93. An examinee presents dramatic hallucination claims that change markedly from one
interview to the next and closely resemble popular stereotypes of mental illness, while a legal
incentive is present. What is the best initial formulation?

   A. Schizophrenia is confirmed
   B. Heightened suspicion for malingering
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Normal stress response
       Answer: B. Heightened suspicion for malingering
   Rationale: Inconsistent symptoms with external incentives suggest malingering.

94. Which feature most strongly differentiates factitious disorder from malingering?
   A. Factitious disorder never involves deception
   B. Malingering involves external incentives, whereas factitious disorder lacks obvious external

rewards
   C. Factitious disorder occurs only in hospitals

 D. Malingering requires psychosis
       Answer: B. Malingering involves external incentives, whereas factitious disorder lacks
obvious external rewards
   Rationale: Motivation differs between the two conditions.

95. During assessment, a client's depressive symptoms began before substance use and
persist well beyond withdrawal periods. Which diagnosis is more likely than a
substance-induced depressive disorder?

   A. Primary depressive disorder
   B. Alcohol intoxication
   C. Delirium

 D. Factitious disorder
       Answer: A. Primary depressive disorder
   Rationale: Symptoms independent of substance use indicate primary disorder.

96. A practitioner delegates scoring and report drafting to an assistant with minimal training and
no supervision. Which ethical principle is most directly violated?

   A. Respect for dignity only
   B. Delegation only to persons expected to perform competently with appropriate supervision
   C. Cultural formulation interview
 D. Research replication
       Answer: B. Delegation only to persons expected to perform competently with appropriate
supervision
   Rationale: Delegation requires ensuring competence and supervision.

97. In a forensic referral, the psychologist should clarify expected role, who the client is,
probable uses of information, and limits of confidentiality primarily because:

   A. Forensic work eliminates ethics
   B. Third-party requests require role clarification to avoid confusion and misuse
   C. Doing so guarantees the examinee will be honest

 D. It removes all legal risk
       Answer: B. Third-party requests require role clarification to avoid confusion and misuse
   Rationale: Forensic contexts require clear boundaries and roles.

98. Which statement about psychopathology and culture is most accurate?
   A. Diagnosis should ignore culture to remain objective
   B. Cultural identity, explanatory models, and stressors can shape symptom meaning and

help-seeking
   C. Culture matters only for psychotic disorders

 D. Culture is relevant only when the clinician and client differ ethnically
       Answer: B. Cultural identity, explanatory models, and stressors can shape symptom
meaning and help-seeking
   Rationale: Culture influences symptom expression and interpretation.

99. A psychometrician is renewing practice skills through continuing professional development
because competence must be maintained. Which law is directly referenced by the PAP Code on
this point?

   A. RA 7610
   B. RA 10912
   C. RA 9258

 D. RA 8049
       Answer: B. RA 10912
   Rationale: RA 10912 mandates continuing professional development for licensed
professionals.

100. A review center asks a licensed psychometrician to lend his professional identification card
so the center can advertise psychological services even when he is absent. Under RA 10029,
the best answer is:

    A. Agree if paid fairly
    B. Agree if the center is reputable
    C. Refuse because allowing another person or entity to use one's registration or credentials
for practice is prohibited

 D. Agree only during weekends
        Answer: C. Refuse because allowing another person or entity to use one's registration or
credentials for practice is prohibited
    Rationale: Lending credentials constitutes illegal practice and is prohibited under RA 10029.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 3
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 3

1. A client reports recurrent, intrusive thoughts about contamination and spends hours washing
hands to reduce distress. The thoughts are experienced as unwanted, and the washing is done
to neutralize anxiety. Which diagnosis is most consistent with this presentation?

  A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
  B. Illness anxiety disorder
  C. Generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
  Rationale: The presentation shows obsessions, which are intrusive and unwanted thoughts,
along with compulsions, which are repetitive behaviors performed to reduce distress or
neutralize anxiety, making obsessive-compulsive disorder the best diagnosis.

2. A 7-year-old child has marked deficits in social reciprocity, limited eye contact, restricted
interests, and insistence on sameness beginning early in development. Which diagnosis is most
likely?

  A. Social anxiety disorder
  B. Autism spectrum disorder
  C. Reactive attachment disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Autism spectrum disorder
  Rationale: Autism spectrum disorder is characterized by early-onset deficits in social
communication and interaction together with restricted, repetitive behaviors and insistence on
sameness.

3. Which statement best reflects the integrative approach to psychopathology?
  A. Psychological disorders are caused primarily by intrapsychic conflict
  B. Biological factors outweigh social and psychological influences
  C. Psychological disorders arise from interacting biological, psychological, and social factors

 D. Environmental stress alone is sufficient to explain most disorders
       Answer: C. Psychological disorders arise from interacting biological, psychological, and
social factors
  Rationale: The integrative approach explains psychopathology through the interaction of
biological, psychological, and social influences rather than by a single cause.

4. A patient presents with low mood, anhedonia, insomnia, fatigue, and impaired concentration
for 3 weeks. During evaluation, you learn the symptoms began two days after abrupt heavy
cocaine withdrawal. What is the most appropriate diagnostic priority?

  A. Diagnose major depressive disorder immediately
  B. Rule out a substance-induced condition first
  C. Diagnose persistent depressive disorder

 D. Diagnose adjustment disorder first
       Answer: B. Rule out a substance-induced condition first
  Rationale: Because the depressive symptoms began closely after cocaine withdrawal, the first
diagnostic priority is to determine whether the symptoms are substance-induced before
assigning a primary mood disorder.

5. Which feature most strongly distinguishes panic attack from generalized anxiety?
  A. Fear of negative evaluation
  B. Persistent worry across domains
  C. Abrupt surge of intense fear reaching a peak within minutes

 D. Repetitive compulsive rituals
       Answer: C. Abrupt surge of intense fear reaching a peak within minutes
  Rationale: A panic attack is defined by a sudden surge of intense fear or discomfort that
reaches its peak within minutes, unlike generalized anxiety, which is more chronic and diffuse.

6. A woman has intense fear of public embarrassment and avoids public speaking, eating in
front of others, and initiating conversation with unfamiliar people. She recognizes the fear as
excessive. Which diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Agoraphobia
  B. Social anxiety disorder
  C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Social anxiety disorder
  Rationale: Social anxiety disorder involves marked fear of social or performance situations in
which the person may be scrutinized or embarrassed, leading to avoidance.

7. A patient reports depressed mood for years, with no symptom-free period longer than 2
months, but never met full criteria for a manic episode. Which diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Cyclothymic disorder
  B. Persistent depressive disorder
  C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
  Rationale: Persistent depressive disorder is marked by chronic depressive symptoms lasting
years, with very limited symptom-free periods and without a history of mania.

8. Which finding best differentiates delusion from obsession?
  A. The belief is recurrent
  B. The thought causes distress
  C. The person has some awareness that the thought may be irrational

 D. The belief is fixed and not amenable to contrary evidence
       Answer: D. The belief is fixed and not amenable to contrary evidence
  Rationale: A delusion is a fixed false belief held despite clear contradictory evidence, whereas
an obsession is intrusive and often recognized as unreasonable.
9. A patient presents with hallucinations and disorganized speech for 3 weeks following a
severe psychosocial stressor. Full premorbid functioning returns within a month. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Schizophrenia
  B. Schizophreniform disorder
  C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Brief psychotic disorder
  Rationale: Brief psychotic disorder involves psychotic symptoms lasting more than 1 day but
less than 1 month, followed by full return to premorbid functioning.

10. Which is the clearest example of negative symptom in schizophrenia?
   A. Auditory hallucinations
   B. Delusions of persecution
   C. Flat affect

 D. Loose associations
       Answer: C. Flat affect
   Rationale: Flat affect is a negative symptom because it reflects diminished emotional
expression, unlike hallucinations, delusions, or loose associations, which are positive or
disorganized symptoms.

11. A person has repeated unexpected panic attacks and now avoids malls, buses, and theaters
because escape might be difficult if panic-like symptoms occur. Which diagnosis pair is most
likely?

   A. Panic disorder and agoraphobia
   B. Social anxiety disorder and panic disorder
   C. Specific phobia and generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder and agoraphobia
       Answer: A. Panic disorder and agoraphobia
   Rationale: Recurrent unexpected panic attacks plus avoidance of places where escape may
be difficult is most consistent with panic disorder together with agoraphobia.

12. A client has excessive anxiety and worry occurring more days than not for many months
about finances, family, health, and work, along with restlessness and muscle tension. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Panic disorder
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Generalized anxiety disorder involves excessive, difficult-to-control worry across
multiple life domains accompanied by physical symptoms such as restlessness and muscle
tension.
13. Which disorder is characterized by recurrent binge eating followed by compensatory
behaviors such as self-induced vomiting, with self-evaluation unduly influenced by body shape
and weight?

   A. Binge-eating disorder
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder

 D. Anorexia nervosa
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa is defined by recurrent binge eating episodes followed by
compensatory behaviors and an overvaluation of body shape and weight.

14. A severely underweight adolescent intensely fears gaining weight and persistently perceives
herself as fat despite obvious emaciation. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Body dysmorphic disorder
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Anorexia nervosa

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: C. Anorexia nervosa
   Rationale: Anorexia nervosa is characterized by significantly low body weight, intense fear of
weight gain, and disturbance in the way body weight or shape is experienced.

15. Which sleep-wake disorder is most associated with recurrent irresistible need to sleep,
cataplexy, and sleep-onset REM phenomena?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder
   C. Hypersomnolence disorder

 D. Narcolepsy
       Answer: D. Narcolepsy
   Rationale: Narcolepsy is strongly associated with irresistible sleep attacks, cataplexy, and
REM-related phenomena such as sleep paralysis and hypnagogic experiences.

16. A patient is preoccupied with having a serious disease despite minimal somatic symptoms
and repeated reassurance. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Illness anxiety disorder
   C. Delusional disorder, somatic type

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder involves excessive preoccupation with having or acquiring
a serious illness despite minimal or absent somatic symptoms.

17. Neurological symptoms inconsistent with recognized neurological disease, often associated
with psychological factors, are most consistent with:

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Malingering
       Answer: B. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Conversion disorder involves neurological-type symptoms that are incompatible
with recognized neurological or medical conditions.

18. Which diagnosis involves falsification of symptoms or induction of injury in the absence of
obvious external rewards?

   A. Malingering
   B. Factitious disorder
   C. Conversion disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Factitious disorder
   Rationale: Factitious disorder involves intentional falsification of symptoms or induction of
illness without clear external incentives.

19. A college student reports episodes of depersonalization in which she feels detached from
herself, yet reality testing remains intact. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Psychotic disorder
   B. Dissociative identity disorder
   C. Depersonalization/derealization disorder

 D. Acute stress disorder
       Answer: C. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: This disorder is characterized by persistent or recurrent experiences of
detachment from oneself or one's surroundings while reality testing remains intact.

20. The hallmark feature of dissociative identity disorder is:
   A. Recurrent depersonalization only
   B. Marked memory deficits due to neurocognitive decline
   C. Disruption of identity with distinct personality states and amnesia

 D. Chronic somatic complaints without medical basis
       Answer: C. Disruption of identity with distinct personality states and amnesia
   Rationale: Dissociative identity disorder is marked by identity disruption involving distinct
personality states together with recurrent gaps in memory.

21. Which mood disorder requires at least one lifetime manic episode?
   A. Bipolar II disorder
   B. Cyclothymic disorder
   C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Bipolar I disorder
   Rationale: A manic episode is the defining feature required for the diagnosis of bipolar I
disorder.
22. Which statement correctly distinguishes hypomanic episode from manic episode?
   A. Hypomania must include psychosis
   B. Hypomania causes marked impairment or hospitalization
   C. Hypomania is less severe and not marked by psychosis or severe impairment

 D. Hypomania lasts at least 1 day
       Answer: C. Hypomania is less severe and not marked by psychosis or severe impairment
   Rationale: Hypomania resembles mania but is not severe enough to cause marked
impairment, hospitalization, or psychotic features.

23. A patient has recurrent major depressive episodes and a history of hypomanic, but never
manic, episodes. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Bipolar I disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Major depressive disorder
       Answer: B. Bipolar II disorder
   Rationale: Bipolar II disorder requires at least one major depressive episode and at least one
hypomanic episode, with no history of mania.

24. A child has severe recurrent temper outbursts grossly out of proportion to the situation, with
persistently irritable mood between outbursts for over a year. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. Pediatric bipolar disorder
       Answer: C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   Rationale: DMDD is characterized by chronic irritability and severe recurrent temper outbursts
that are grossly out of proportion to the situation.

25. Which symptom is most characteristic of major depressive episode rather than normal
sadness alone?

   A. Temporary disappointment after setback
   B. Clinically significant impairment with neurovegetative and cognitive symptoms
   C. Brief tearfulness resolving in hours

 D. Mood reactivity in all situations
       Answer: B. Clinically significant impairment with neurovegetative and cognitive symptoms
   Rationale: A major depressive episode involves a clinically significant syndrome that includes
cognitive and vegetative symptoms and causes distress or impairment beyond ordinary
sadness.

26. The disorder most strongly associated with unstable relationships, frantic efforts to avoid
abandonment, identity disturbance, and recurrent self-harm is:

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Borderline personality disorder is marked by instability in relationships, self-image,
and affect, with abandonment fears and recurrent self-harming behavior.

27. Which personality disorder is marked by disregard for and violation of the rights of others
since age 15, with evidence of conduct disorder before age 15?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: C. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Antisocial personality disorder requires a pervasive pattern of violating the rights of
others and evidence of conduct disorder before age 15.

28. A pervasive pattern of social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to
negative evaluation is most consistent with:

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: C. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder is defined by pervasive social inhibition, feelings of
inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to criticism or rejection.

29. A patient persistently suspects others are exploiting or deceiving him, bears grudges, and
interprets benign remarks as threatening. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Paranoid personality disorder
   C. Schizotypal personality disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: B. Paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Paranoid personality disorder involves pervasive distrust and suspiciousness such
that others' motives are interpreted as malevolent.

30. Which diagnosis is characterized by odd beliefs, unusual perceptual experiences, eccentric
behavior, and social deficits, but not persistent frank psychosis?

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Schizotypal personality disorder
   C. Paranoid personality disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizotypal personality disorder includes odd beliefs, unusual perceptual
experiences, eccentricity, and interpersonal deficits without persistent full psychosis.

31. Which diagnosis is most associated with deceitfulness, theft, rule violation, and aggression
toward people or animals in youth?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: B. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Conduct disorder is characterized by repetitive and persistent behavior violating
the rights of others or major age-appropriate social norms.

32. Recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts that are grossly out of proportion and not
premeditated are most consistent with:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: C. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: Intermittent explosive disorder involves impulsive, disproportionate aggressive
outbursts that are not planned or goal-directed.

33. A child shows a persistent pattern of argumentative, defiant, and vindictive behavior toward
authority figures but no serious aggression or major rule violations. Which diagnosis is most
likely?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   Rationale: Oppositional defiant disorder involves a pattern of angry, argumentative, defiant, or
vindictive behavior without the more serious violations seen in conduct disorder.

34. Which disorder is categorized under substance-related and addictive disorders despite not
involving ingestion of a substance?

   A. Pyromania
   B. Kleptomania
   C. Gambling disorder

 D. Conduct disorder
       Answer: C. Gambling disorder
   Rationale: Gambling disorder is classified with addictive disorders because it shares core
features of addiction such as impaired control, craving, and persistence despite harm.
35. Tolerance, withdrawal, craving, and continued use despite harm are core features of:
   A. Substance use disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Substance use disorder
   Rationale: These features are central diagnostic indicators of substance use disorder and
reflect compulsive use despite adverse consequences.

36. Which substance class is most associated with CNS depression, slurred speech, and
potentially dangerous withdrawal syndromes?

   A. Stimulants
   B. Hallucinogens
   C. Depressants

 D. Cannabis
       Answer: C. Depressants
   Rationale: Depressants, such as alcohol and sedative-hypnotics, reduce central nervous
system activity and may produce dangerous withdrawal states.

37. Which disorder is most characterized by inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity that is
developmentally inappropriate and present across settings?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. ADHD

 D. Specific learning disorder
       Answer: C. ADHD
   Rationale: ADHD is defined by persistent inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity that is
developmentally inappropriate and evident in multiple settings.

38. A student of average intelligence has persistent difficulties in word reading accuracy and
spelling despite adequate opportunity to learn. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. ADHD
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: C. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Specific learning disorder involves persistent difficulties in academic skills such as
reading and spelling despite adequate intelligence and opportunity.

39. Which is essential for diagnosis of intellectual disability?
   A. IQ below 100 only
   B. Deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning with onset during developmental period
   C. Severe language impairment only
   D. Academic failure only
  Answer: B. Deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning with onset during

developmental period
   Rationale: Intellectual disability requires impairments in both intellectual functioning and

adaptive functioning, with onset during the developmental period.

40. Which feature best differentiates autism spectrum disorder from social anxiety disorder?
   A. Avoidance of scrutiny
   B. Early-onset deficits in social communication and restricted behaviors
   C. Panic attacks in social settings

 D. Excessive worries about multiple domains
       Answer: B. Early-onset deficits in social communication and restricted behaviors
   Rationale: Autism spectrum disorder is distinguished by developmental social communication
deficits and restricted, repetitive behaviors beginning early in development.

41. A fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness developing over a short period, usually
due to a medical condition or substance, is most consistent with:

   A. Major neurocognitive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Delirium is marked by an acute, fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness
commonly caused by a medical condition or substance.

42. Progressive decline in one or more cognitive domains that interferes with independence is
most consistent with:

   A. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Intellectual disability
       Answer: B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Major neurocognitive disorder involves significant cognitive decline severe enough
to interfere with independent functioning.

43. Which feature most strongly suggests delirium rather than dementia?
   A. Insidious onset
   B. Stable course
   C. Disturbance in attention with acute fluctuating course

 D. Preserved awareness
       Answer: C. Disturbance in attention with acute fluctuating course
   Rationale: The acute onset, fluctuating course, and prominent disturbance in attention
strongly indicate delirium rather than dementia.
44. Hallucinations that occur exclusively during a severe depressive episode are most
consistent with:

   A. Schizoaffective disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   Rationale: When psychotic symptoms occur only during a depressive episode, the diagnosis
is major depressive disorder with psychotic features.

45. Which diagnosis requires a major mood episode concurrent with psychotic symptoms plus at
least 2 weeks of delusions or hallucinations without a major mood episode?

   A. Schizoaffective disorder
   B. Bipolar I disorder
   C. Schizophreniform disorder

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: A. Schizoaffective disorder
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both a major mood episode and a period of
psychosis lasting at least 2 weeks in the absence of mood symptoms.

46. Which psychotic disorder is characterized by one or more delusions for at least 1 month,
with functioning otherwise relatively preserved and no prominent disorganization?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Brief psychotic disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: A. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: Delusional disorder is defined by persistent delusions with relatively preserved
functioning and without the marked disorganization seen in schizophrenia.

47. A patient has prominent persecutory delusions after methamphetamine use, and symptoms
occur during intoxication. The most appropriate diagnosis is:

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder
   Rationale: The close temporal relationship between methamphetamine use and psychotic
symptoms supports a substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder.

48. Which disorder is most associated with trauma exposure followed by intrusion, avoidance,
negative alterations in cognition or mood, and hyperarousal lasting more than one month?

   A. Acute stress disorder
   B. PTSD
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. PTSD
   Rationale: PTSD is characterized by trauma-related intrusion, avoidance, negative mood or
cognitive changes, and increased arousal lasting longer than one month.

49. Which statement best distinguishes acute stress disorder from PTSD?
   A. Acute stress disorder requires psychosis
   B. Acute stress disorder is diagnosed only in children
   C. Acute stress disorder occurs shortly after trauma and has shorter duration

 D. PTSD does not involve avoidance
       Answer: C. Acute stress disorder occurs shortly after trauma and has shorter duration
   Rationale: Acute stress disorder appears in the immediate aftermath of trauma and is
diagnosed over a shorter duration than PTSD.

50. Emotional or behavioral symptoms in response to an identifiable stressor occurring within
months of the stressor, but not meeting criteria for another disorder, are most consistent with:

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. PTSD
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: Adjustment disorder involves maladaptive emotional or behavioral responses to an
identifiable stressor that do not fully meet criteria for another disorder.

51. Which disorder is characterized by recurrent hair pulling resulting in hair loss?
   A. Body dysmorphic disorder
   B. Excoriation disorder
   C. Trichotillomania

 D. OCD
       Answer: C. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Trichotillomania is defined by recurrent hair pulling that leads to noticeable hair
loss.

52. Recurrent skin picking leading to skin lesions is most consistent with:
   A. Body dysmorphic disorder
   B. Excoriation disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Excoriation disorder
   Rationale: Excoriation disorder is characterized by recurrent skin picking that results in skin
lesions.
53. A person cannot discard possessions regardless of actual value, resulting in clutter that
compromises living areas. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. OCD
   B. Hoarding disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. OCPD
       Answer: B. Hoarding disorder
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder involves persistent difficulty discarding possessions, resulting in
clutter that disrupts intended use of living spaces.

54. Which disorder is defined by preoccupation with one or more perceived defects in physical
appearance that are not observable or appear slight to others?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Narcissistic personality disorder
       Answer: C. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Body dysmorphic disorder centers on distressing preoccupation with perceived
defects in appearance that are slight or not observable to others.

55. Which condition is best conceptualized as a cultural and social structural factor that can
influence diagnosis and clinical assessment rather than as a mental disorder itself?

   A. Racism and discrimination
   B. Obsessions
   C. Hallucinations

 D. Catatonia
       Answer: A. Racism and discrimination
   Rationale: Racism and discrimination are contextual social factors that affect mental health,
symptom presentation, and diagnostic interpretation but are not mental disorders themselves.

56. A clinician mistakes culturally normative bereavement expressions for psychosis because of
unfamiliarity with the client's background. What principle was most violated?

   A. Reliability over validity
   B. Cultural formulation in assessment
   C. Projective testing

 D. Symptom count method
       Answer: B. Cultural formulation in assessment
   Rationale: Cultural formulation helps clinicians interpret symptoms within the person's cultural
context and avoid misdiagnosis based on unfamiliar cultural expressions.

57. Which is the best first step in differential diagnosis when symptom exaggeration or
fabrication is suspected?

   A. Rule out malingering and factitious disorder
   B. Diagnose personality disorder
   C. Begin medication immediately

 D. Assume psychosis
       Answer: A. Rule out malingering and factitious disorder
   Rationale: When deception is suspected, the first step is to determine whether the
presentation is due to malingering or factitious disorder before proceeding with other diagnoses.

58. In differential diagnosis, why must substance use always be carefully considered?
   A. It is rare but easy to detect
   B. Substance etiology is one of the most common missed causes of psychiatric symptoms
   C. Substance-related disorders cannot mimic anxiety or mood symptoms

 D. It matters only in forensic settings
       Answer: B. Substance etiology is one of the most common missed causes of psychiatric
symptoms
   Rationale: Substance use can produce a wide range of psychiatric symptoms and is one of
the most commonly overlooked causes in clinical diagnosis.

59. A patient presents with depression, but later records reveal a prior manic episode. The most
likely revised diagnosis is:

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Bipolar I disorder
   C. Major depressive disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Bipolar I disorder
   Rationale: The presence of a prior manic episode automatically supports bipolar I disorder,
even if the current presentation is depressive.

60. Which psychologist is most associated with the hierarchy of needs and humanistic
psychology?

   A. B. F. Skinner
   B. Carl Rogers
   C. Abraham Maslow

 D. Ivan Pavlov
       Answer: C. Abraham Maslow
   Rationale: Abraham Maslow is most associated with humanistic psychology and the hierarchy
of needs.

61. Classical conditioning is most strongly associated with:
   A. Sigmund Freud
   B. Carl Jung
   C. Ivan Pavlov

 D. Albert Bandura
       Answer: C. Ivan Pavlov
   Rationale: Ivan Pavlov is the psychologist most strongly associated with classical
conditioning.
62. Operant conditioning is most strongly associated with:
   A. B. F. Skinner
   B. John Bowlby
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: A. B. F. Skinner
   Rationale: B. F. Skinner is most strongly associated with operant conditioning and
reinforcement principles.

63. The cognitive triad in depression is most associated with:
   A. Aaron Beck
   B. Albert Ellis
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. Erik Erikson
       Answer: A. Aaron Beck
   Rationale: Aaron Beck proposed the cognitive triad of depression involving negative views of
the self, world, and future.

64. Learned helplessness as a model relevant to depression is most associated with:
   A. Martin Seligman
   B. Albert Bandura
   C. Gordon Allport

 D. Raymond Cattell
       Answer: A. Martin Seligman
   Rationale: Martin Seligman developed the learned helplessness model, which became
influential in understanding depression.

65. The term schizophrenia was introduced by:
   A. Emil Kraepelin
   B. Eugen Bleuler
   C. Philippe Pinel

 D. Wilhelm Wundt
       Answer: B. Eugen Bleuler
   Rationale: Eugen Bleuler introduced the term schizophrenia to replace dementia praecox.

66. Kraepelin is historically associated with:
   A. Moral therapy
   B. Dementia praecox classification
   C. Client-centered therapy

 D. Token economy
       Answer: B. Dementia praecox classification
   Rationale: Emil Kraepelin is historically known for classifying dementia praecox, the earlier
concept related to schizophrenia.
67. Psychoanalysis is most closely associated with:
   A. Sigmund Freud
   B. Joseph Wolpe
   C. Albert Ellis

 D. Carl Rogers
       Answer: A. Sigmund Freud
   Rationale: Sigmund Freud founded psychoanalysis and is most closely associated with that
perspective.

68. Exposure with response prevention is a well-established treatment for:
   A. Panic disorder
   B. OCD
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Dissociative identity disorder
       Answer: B. OCD
   Rationale: Exposure with response prevention is a gold-standard behavioral treatment for
obsessive-compulsive disorder.

69. The behavioral concept of modeling is most associated with:
   A. Albert Bandura
   B. Aaron Beck
   C. B. F. Skinner

 D. Carl Rogers
       Answer: A. Albert Bandura
   Rationale: Albert Bandura is most associated with modeling and observational learning in
social learning theory.

70. The principle that psychological treatments should be supported by scientific evidence is
most closely aligned with:

   A. Moral treatment
   B. Evidence-based practice
   C. Eclecticism without evaluation

 D. Intuition-based therapy
       Answer: B. Evidence-based practice
   Rationale: Evidence-based practice requires that treatment approaches be supported by the
best available scientific evidence.

71. In the Philippines, which statement best reflects RA 10029 and the PAP Code regarding
psychometricians?

   A. They may independently provide psychotherapy if supervised informally
   B. They may practice beyond assessment as long as experienced
   C. They operate within legal boundaries and under the supervision of a registered
psychologist when applicable
 D. They may diagnose independently without restriction
       Answer: C. They operate within legal boundaries and under the supervision of a
registered psychologist when applicable
   Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code require psychometricians to work within legally
defined boundaries and under appropriate supervision when their functions require it.

72. Under the PAP Code, psychometricians are prohibited from:
   A. Scoring tests
   B. Conducting therapy except in emergency situations
   C. Preparing test materials

 D. Assisting in assessment
       Answer: B. Conducting therapy except in emergency situations
   Rationale: Under the PAP Code, psychometricians are not allowed to conduct therapy except
in emergency situations.

73. Which ethical principle is most directly involved when a psychologist explains the nature,
risks, benefits, and limits of confidentiality before services begin?

   A. Justice
   B. Informed consent
   C. Fidelity only

 D. Beneficence only
       Answer: B. Informed consent
   Rationale: Informed consent requires that clients be adequately informed about the nature of
services, possible risks and benefits, and the limits of confidentiality before services begin.

74. A client reveals imminent intention to seriously harm another identified person. Which ethical
response is most appropriate?

   A. Maintain secrecy without exception
   B. Release information to appropriate individuals or authorities after careful deliberation
   C. Post about the threat online to warn others

 D. Ignore because confidentiality is absolute
       Answer: B. Release information to appropriate individuals or authorities after careful
deliberation
   Rationale: When there is an imminent threat of serious harm to an identified person,
confidentiality may be limited and protective disclosure to appropriate parties may be ethically
warranted.

75. Which practice most clearly violates ethical standards on public statements?
   A. Stating one's degree and office hours
   B. Describing services factually
   C. Exaggerating success rates and qualifications in advertising

 D. Correcting public misinformation
       Answer: C. Exaggerating success rates and qualifications in advertising
   Rationale: Ethical standards prohibit false, deceptive, or misleading public statements,
including exaggerated claims about qualifications or treatment success.

76. A psychologist is asked to provide services to a friend's spouse while also being involved in
a family business dispute with the same family. The primary ethical concern is:

   A. Test security
   B. Multiple relationships and conflict of interest
   C. Cultural formulation

 D. Differential diagnosis
       Answer: B. Multiple relationships and conflict of interest
   Rationale: Simultaneous personal and professional involvement with the same people can
impair objectivity and create a harmful multiple relationship or conflict of interest.

77. Delegating psychological tasks to an untrained assistant without supervision primarily
violates:

   A. Boundaries of competence
   B. Right to refuse treatment
   C. Free association

 D. Catharsis
       Answer: A. Boundaries of competence
   Rationale: Delegating professional work to an untrained assistant without proper supervision
violates ethical standards requiring competence and appropriate delegation.

78. Which action best protects test security?
   A. Posting protocols online for public education
   B. Allowing unqualified persons to interpret tests
   C. Securing protocols and records from unqualified persons

 D. Giving raw data to anyone who requests it
       Answer: C. Securing protocols and records from unqualified persons
   Rationale: Test security is best protected by restricting access to protocols, materials, and
records so that unqualified individuals cannot misuse them.

79. Which principle is most directly violated when a practitioner continues clinical work despite
severe impairment from personal problems that compromise competence?

   A. Maintaining competence
   B. Cultural humility
   C. Forensic neutrality

 D. Psychodynamic neutrality
       Answer: A. Maintaining competence
   Rationale: Practitioners are ethically required to maintain competence and to limit or suspend
work when personal problems substantially impair professional functioning.

80. A psychometrician begins offering unsupervised psychotherapy sessions online to paying
clients. This is primarily a violation of:
   A. Only confidentiality
   B. RA 10029 scope and ethical boundaries of competence
   C. Only informed consent

 D. Only record keeping rules
       Answer: B. RA 10029 scope and ethical boundaries of competence
   Rationale: Providing unsupervised psychotherapy exceeds the legal scope of psychometric
practice under RA 10029 and violates ethical boundaries of competence.

81. Which of the following best exemplifies malingering?
   A. Fabricating symptoms to assume the sick role without obvious external reward
   B. Producing symptoms to obtain disability benefits
   C. Experiencing conversion symptoms unconsciously

 D. Overvalued health anxiety without deception
       Answer: B. Producing symptoms to obtain disability benefits
   Rationale: Malingering involves intentional symptom fabrication or exaggeration for clear
external gain, such as disability benefits.

82. Which statement best distinguishes somatic symptom disorder from illness anxiety disorder?
   A. Somatic symptom disorder requires no symptoms
   B. Illness anxiety disorder centers on preoccupation with disease despite minimal somatic

symptoms
   C. Illness anxiety disorder always involves delusion

 D. Somatic symptom disorder requires feigning
       Answer: B. Illness anxiety disorder centers on preoccupation with disease despite minimal
somatic symptoms
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder is defined by excessive health-related fear despite minimal
or absent somatic symptoms, unlike somatic symptom disorder, which involves more prominent
bodily complaints.

83. Which diagnosis is most likely when an adolescent restricts food intake because of sensory
aversion and lack of interest in eating, without body image distortion?

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder

 D. Binge-eating disorder
       Answer: C. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   Rationale: ARFID involves restrictive eating due to sensory sensitivity, low interest in food, or
fear of aversive consequences, without weight or shape disturbance.

84. Which disorder is characterized by repeated binge-eating episodes without regular
compensatory behaviors?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Anorexia nervosa
 D. ARFID
       Answer: B. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder is defined by recurrent binge eating episodes that are not
followed by regular compensatory behaviors.

85. A patient with insomnia spends excessive time in bed trying to force sleep, which worsens
arousal and sleep difficulty. Which psychological principle is most relevant?

   A. Stimulus control
   B. Free association
   C. Catatonia

 D. Flooding with response prevention
       Answer: A. Stimulus control
   Rationale: Stimulus control is relevant because it addresses maladaptive associations
between the bed and wakefulness that maintain insomnia.

86. Which disorder is most associated with grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of
empathy?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Narcissistic personality disorder is characterized by grandiosity, a need for
admiration, and lack of empathy.

87. Which personality disorder is most characterized by excessive emotionality and attention
seeking?

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Dependent personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: A. Histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Histrionic personality disorder is marked by pervasive excessive emotionality and
attention-seeking behavior.

88. A patient is preoccupied with orderliness, perfectionism, and control at the expense of
flexibility and efficiency. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. OCD
   B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. Generalized anxiety disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   Rationale: OCPD is characterized by rigid perfectionism, orderliness, and control that
interfere with flexibility and efficiency.
89. Which symptom is more typical of mania than hypomania because of its severity?
   A. Increased activity
   B. Decreased need for sleep
   C. Psychotic features

 D. Elevated mood
       Answer: C. Psychotic features
   Rationale: Psychotic features indicate a level of severity consistent with mania rather than
hypomania.

90. A person has chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive symptoms for years but never
meets full criteria for manic, hypomanic, or major depressive episodes. Which diagnosis is most
likely?

   A. Bipolar I disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Cyclothymic disorder
   Rationale: Cyclothymic disorder involves chronic fluctuations of subthreshold hypomanic and
depressive symptoms that never meet full episode criteria.

91. Which disorder is most associated with recurrent fire setting for pleasure, tension before the
act, and fascination with fire?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Pyromania
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: B. Pyromania
   Rationale: Pyromania involves deliberate fire setting associated with tension or affective
arousal before the act and fascination, interest, or gratification related to fire.

92. Which disorder is characterized by recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal objects not
needed for personal use or monetary value?

   A. Kleptomania
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Conduct disorder

 D. Hoarding disorder
       Answer: A. Kleptomania
   Rationale: Kleptomania is defined by recurrent inability to resist stealing items that are not
needed for personal use or monetary value.

93. A person hears a running commentary voice and shows disorganized behavior, avolition,
and marked social decline for more than 6 months. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophrenia
   Rationale: Schizophrenia is supported by prolonged psychotic symptoms, negative
symptoms, disorganization, and significant functional decline lasting more than 6 months.

94. Which feature most strongly favors schizoaffective disorder over schizophrenia?
   A. Presence of negative symptoms
   B. Mood episodes occur only briefly relative to psychosis
   C. Psychotic symptoms occur exclusively during mood episodes
   D. There is a substantial mood episode and also a period of psychosis without mood

symptoms
       Answer: D. There is a substantial mood episode and also a period of psychosis without
mood symptoms

   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both a major mood episode and a period of
psychosis occurring in the absence of mood symptoms.

95. Which diagnosis should be considered when a client's emotional or behavioral symptoms
are understandable responses to stress but are too mild, brief, or expectable to qualify as a
mental disorder?

   A. Other specified disorder automatically
   B. Adjustment disorder automatically
   C. No mental disorder may be the most appropriate conclusion

 D. Major depressive disorder
       Answer: C. No mental disorder may be the most appropriate conclusion
   Rationale: Not all distress or stress reactions constitute mental disorders; when symptoms
are mild, expectable, or insufficiently impairing, no mental disorder may be the most accurate
conclusion.

96. Which concept refers to the frequency of existing cases of a disorder in a population at a
given time?

   A. Incidence
   B. Prevalence
   C. Prognosis

 D. Etiology
       Answer: B. Prevalence
   Rationale: Prevalence refers to the number or proportion of existing cases of a disorder in a
population at a particular time.

97. Which concept refers to the likely course and outcome of a disorder?
   A. Prognosis
   B. Prevalence
   C. Incidence
 D. Comorbidity
       Answer: A. Prognosis
   Rationale: Prognosis refers to the expected course, development, and likely outcome of a
disorder.

98. A patient's culturally shaped explanation of panic-like symptoms as caused by disturbed
bodily wind is an example of:

   A. Negative symptom
   B. Cultural concept of distress
   C. Factitious presentation

 D. Formal thought disorder
       Answer: B. Cultural concept of distress
   Rationale: A culturally shaped way of understanding and expressing symptoms is an example
of a cultural concept of distress.

99. Which assessment approach is most useful for clarifying symptom onset, course, triggers,
and impairment across disorders?

   A. Clinical interview
   B. Dream analysis alone
   C. Phrenology

 D. Unstructured observation only
       Answer: A. Clinical interview
   Rationale: The clinical interview is the most useful core assessment tool for gathering
detailed information about onset, course, triggers, symptoms, and impairment.

100. Which statement best reflects sound PRC-style diagnostic reasoning in abnormal
psychology?

    A. Diagnose based on the most dramatic symptom alone
    B. Ignore medical and substance causes when symptoms appear psychiatric
    C. Consider differential diagnosis, context, impairment, culture, and rule-outs before final
diagnosis

 D. Favor rare diagnoses because they are more sophisticated
        Answer: C. Consider differential diagnosis, context, impairment, culture, and rule-outs
before final diagnosis
    Rationale: Sound diagnostic reasoning requires careful consideration of differential
diagnoses, contextual and cultural factors, level of impairment, and exclusion of medical or
substance-related causes before arriving at a final diagnosis.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 4
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 4

1. Which statement best reflects the contemporary view of abnormal behavior?
  A. Abnormal behavior is defined solely by biological dysfunction
  B. Abnormal behavior is best understood through interacting biological, psychological, and

social factors
  C. Abnormal behavior is whatever violates social norms, regardless of distress or impairment

 D. Abnormal behavior is any behavior that differs from the statistical average
       Answer: B. Abnormal behavior is best understood through interacting biological,
psychological, and social factors
  Rationale: Contemporary models emphasize a biopsychosocial approach, integrating
biological, psychological, and social influences in understanding psychopathology.

2. A clinician is evaluating a client who appears to exaggerate hallucinations to avoid criminal
responsibility. According to sound differential diagnosis practice, the clinician should first
consider:

  A. Delusional disorder
  B. Factitious disorder
  C. Malingering

 D. Schizophreniform disorder
       Answer: C. Malingering
  Rationale: Malingering involves intentional production or exaggeration of symptoms for
external incentives such as avoiding legal consequences.

3. Which feature most strongly supports a diagnosis of factitious disorder rather than
malingering?

  A. Presence of obvious financial gain
  B. Intentional production of symptoms without clear external reward
  C. Presence of severe distress

 D. Co-occurrence of a medical illness
       Answer: B. Intentional production of symptoms without clear external reward
  Rationale: Factitious disorder involves deliberate symptom production without external
incentives, driven by internal psychological needs.

4. A patient presents with new-onset panic attacks after heavy stimulant use. Before diagnosing
panic disorder, the clinician should first rule out:

  A. Specific phobia
  B. Generalized anxiety disorder
  C. Substance-induced anxiety disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Substance-induced anxiety disorder
  Rationale: Symptoms temporally related to substance use must be evaluated as
substance-induced before diagnosing a primary anxiety disorder.
5. A client reports persistent sadness, fatigue, and anhedonia. Which history finding would most
strongly suggest bipolar disorder rather than major depressive disorder?

  A. Family history of dementia
  B. Past period of decreased need for sleep with increased goal-directed activity
  C. Fear of negative evaluation

 D. Chronic interpersonal mistrust
       Answer: B. Past period of decreased need for sleep with increased goal-directed activity
  Rationale: A history of hypomanic or manic symptoms distinguishes bipolar disorder from
unipolar depression.

6. Which is the best example of a diathesis-stress model?
  A. A disorder caused entirely by trauma
  B. A disorder caused entirely by genetics
  C. A predisposition that manifests when activated by stressors

 D. A disorder maintained only by reinforcement contingencies
       Answer: C. A predisposition that manifests when activated by stressors
  Rationale: The diathesis-stress model posits that disorders emerge when vulnerability
interacts with environmental stress.

7. In psychopathology, prevalence refers to:
  A. Number of new cases over a specific period
  B. Total number of existing cases in a population at a given time
  C. Number of relapses after treatment

 D. Proportion of severe cases needing hospitalization
       Answer: B. Total number of existing cases in a population at a given time
  Rationale: Prevalence measures how widespread a disorder is by counting all existing cases
at a given time.

8. Incidence refers to:
  A. Total current cases
  B. Lifetime risk only
  C. Number of new cases occurring over a period of time

 D. Number of treated cases in a clinic
       Answer: C. Number of new cases occurring over a period of time
  Rationale: Incidence specifically measures new cases developing within a defined time frame.

9. A client's panic attacks occur unexpectedly and are followed by persistent concern about
additional attacks and maladaptive behavior change. The most likely diagnosis is:

  A. Panic disorder
  B. Agoraphobia only
  C. Specific phobia

 D. Acute stress disorder
       Answer: A. Panic disorder
  Rationale: Panic disorder involves recurrent unexpected panic attacks with ongoing concern
and behavioral changes related to the attacks.

10. Fear of public speaking, eating in front of others, and meeting unfamiliar people is most
consistent with:

   A. Agoraphobia
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Separation anxiety disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: B. Social anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Social anxiety disorder is characterized by fear of social situations involving
possible scrutiny or evaluation.

11. A person fears elevators because escape might be difficult if panic-like symptoms occur.
This presentation is most consistent with:

   A. Specific phobia, situational type
   B. Agoraphobia
   C. Social anxiety disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Agoraphobia
   Rationale: Agoraphobia involves fear of situations where escape may be difficult or help
unavailable during panic-like symptoms.

12. Which symptom best distinguishes generalized anxiety disorder from ordinary worry?
   A. Worry limited to one specific object
   B. Worry accompanied by recurrent compulsions
   C. Excessive, difficult-to-control worry across multiple domains

 D. Brief surges of terror lasting minutes only
       Answer: C. Excessive, difficult-to-control worry across multiple domains
   Rationale: GAD involves persistent, excessive, and uncontrollable worry across multiple life
areas.

13. A 9-year-old refuses school because of extreme distress when away from his mother and
recurrent fears that harm will befall her. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Separation anxiety disorder
   C. Selective mutism

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Separation anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Separation anxiety disorder involves excessive fear concerning separation from
attachment figures.

14. A child speaks normally at home but consistently fails to speak in school despite adequate
language ability. The most likely diagnosis is:
   A. Autism spectrum disorder
   B. Selective mutism
   C. Social communication disorder

 D. Specific learning disorder
       Answer: B. Selective mutism
   Rationale: Selective mutism is characterized by failure to speak in specific settings despite
normal speech in others.

15. Persistent intrusive thoughts about contamination accompanied by repetitive washing rituals
best indicate:

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   C. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   Rationale: OCD involves intrusive obsessions and compulsive behaviors aimed at reducing
anxiety.

16. Which feature best differentiates obsessions from psychotic delusions?
   A. Obsessions are always pleasant
   B. Obsessions are experienced as intrusive and unwanted
   C. Obsessions never involve bizarre content

 D. Obsessions are always ego-syntonic
       Answer: B. Obsessions are experienced as intrusive and unwanted
   Rationale: Obsessions are ego-dystonic and recognized as unwanted thoughts, unlike
delusions.

17. A woman is preoccupied with an imagined facial defect and spends hours checking mirrors
and seeking reassurance. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Body dysmorphic disorder involves preoccupation with perceived defects in
appearance and repetitive behaviors.

18. The core feature of hoarding disorder is:
   A. Recurrent stealing due to tension relief
   B. Excessive acquisition and persistent difficulty discarding possessions regardless of value
   C. Repetitive handwashing due to contamination fears

 D. Fear of having a serious disease despite minimal symptoms
       Answer: B. Excessive acquisition and persistent difficulty discarding possessions
regardless of value
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder centers on difficulty discarding possessions, leading to
accumulation and clutter.

19. A person repeatedly pulls out hair, feels mounting tension before doing so, and relief
afterward. The diagnosis is:

   A. Excoriation disorder
   B. Trichotillomania
   C. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder

 D. Body dysmorphic disorder
       Answer: B. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Trichotillomania involves recurrent hair pulling with tension before and relief after
the act.

20. A person repeatedly picks skin causing lesions and unsuccessful efforts to stop. The
diagnosis is:

   A. Excoriation disorder
   B. Factitious disorder
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Excoriation disorder
   Rationale: Excoriation disorder is defined by recurrent skin picking leading to lesions and
failed attempts to stop.

21. Which finding most strongly supports posttraumatic stress disorder rather than acute stress
disorder?

   A. Exposure to a traumatic event
   B. Dissociative symptoms
   C. Duration of symptoms beyond 1 month

 D. Hypervigilance
       Answer: C. Duration of symptoms beyond 1 month
   Rationale: PTSD requires symptoms to persist for more than one month, whereas acute
stress disorder is limited to a shorter duration.

22. A person develops emotional symptoms within 2 months of job loss, but the symptoms do
not meet full criteria for major depressive disorder. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Adjustment disorder
   C. Acute stress disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: Adjustment disorder involves emotional or behavioral symptoms in response to a
stressor that do not meet criteria for another disorder.
23. A client has neurological symptoms incompatible with recognized medical disease and not
intentionally produced. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Malingering
       Answer: B. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Conversion disorder involves neurological symptoms inconsistent with medical
findings and not intentionally produced.

24. Which best characterizes illness anxiety disorder?
   A. Severe somatic symptoms with health-related anxiety
   B. Preoccupation with having or acquiring serious illness with minimal somatic symptoms
   C. Intentional feigning of disease

 D. Delusional belief of body deformity
       Answer: B. Preoccupation with having or acquiring serious illness with minimal somatic
symptoms
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder focuses on excessive concern about having a serious
illness despite minimal symptoms.

25. Somatic symptom disorder is most strongly characterized by:
   A. Absence of any physical symptoms
   B. Intentional fabrication of complaints
   C. Excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors related to somatic symptoms

 D. Exclusive fear of contamination
       Answer: C. Excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors related to somatic symptoms
   Rationale: The disorder emphasizes disproportionate distress and behavioral responses to
somatic symptoms.

26. Dissociative amnesia most often involves inability to recall:
   A. Well-learned academic knowledge
   B. New information after a head injury
   C. Important autobiographical information, usually of a traumatic or stressful nature

 D. Remote semantic memory due to dementia
       Answer: C. Important autobiographical information, usually of a traumatic or stressful
nature
   Rationale: Dissociative amnesia typically affects autobiographical memory related to trauma
or stress.

27. Which statement best distinguishes dissociative identity disorder from schizophrenia?
   A. DID always includes visual hallucinations
   B. Schizophrenia requires memory gaps for daily events
   C. DID centers on identity disruption and discontinuity in sense of self
   D. Schizophrenia is caused by trauma alone
  Answer: C. DID centers on identity disruption and discontinuity in sense of self

   Rationale: DID involves identity fragmentation, unlike schizophrenia which is primarily
psychotic.

28. Recurrent binge eating followed by compensatory vomiting most strongly indicates:
   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder

 D. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa involves binge eating followed by compensatory behaviors such
as vomiting.

29. Significantly low body weight, intense fear of gaining weight, and disturbance in body image
best indicate:

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: A. Anorexia nervosa
   Rationale: Anorexia nervosa is defined by low weight, fear of weight gain, and distorted body
image.

30. Recurrent binge eating without regular compensatory behavior is most consistent with:
   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Pica

 D. Rumination disorder
       Answer: B. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder involves binge episodes without compensatory behaviors.

31. A person has persistent difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep despite adequate opportunity
for sleep and daytime impairment. The diagnosis is:

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder
   C. Hypersomnolence disorder

 D. Nightmare disorder
       Answer: A. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Insomnia disorder involves difficulty sleeping despite opportunity, with daytime
impairment.

32. Excessive sleepiness despite a main sleep period of at least 7 hours, with recurrent sleep
lapses and difficulty being fully awake, is most consistent with:

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Sleep terror disorder

 D. Restless legs syndrome
       Answer: B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   Rationale: Hypersomnolence disorder is characterized by excessive sleepiness despite
adequate sleep.

33. A young adult with cataplexy, sleep paralysis, and irresistible sleep attacks most likely has:
   A. Narcolepsy
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Nightmare disorder
       Answer: A. Narcolepsy
   Rationale: Narcolepsy includes sleep attacks, cataplexy, and sleep paralysis.

34. Which symptom is characteristic of a manic episode?
   A. Mood reactivity to positive events only
   B. At least 1 week of abnormally elevated or irritable mood with increased energy
   C. Chronic low-grade depression for 2 years

 D. Panic attacks triggered by trauma cues
       Answer: B. At least 1 week of abnormally elevated or irritable mood with increased energy
   Rationale: Mania requires sustained elevated or irritable mood with increased energy for at
least one week.

35. Which statement correctly distinguishes hypomania from mania?
   A. Hypomania requires psychotic features
   B. Hypomania lasts at least 2 days
   C. Hypomania is less severe and not severe enough to cause marked impairment or

hospitalization

 D. Hypomania cannot occur in bipolar II disorder
       Answer: C. Hypomania is less severe and not severe enough to cause marked
impairment or hospitalization
   Rationale: Hypomania is a milder form of mania without severe impairment or hospitalization.

36. A patient has recurrent major depressive episodes and at least one hypomanic episode, but
no manic episode. The diagnosis is:

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Bipolar I disorder
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Bipolar II disorder
   Rationale: Bipolar II disorder requires hypomanic and major depressive episodes without full
mania.
37. Chronic depressed mood for at least 2 years with additional depressive symptoms but no
history of mania best fits:

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Persistent depressive disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Brief depressive disorder
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
   Rationale: Persistent depressive disorder involves chronic depression lasting at least two
years.

38. Which cognitive triad is classically associated with depression?
   A. Self, world, and future viewed negatively
   B. Id, ego, and superego conflict
   C. Thought broadcasting, delusions, and passivity

 D. Fear conditioning, avoidance, and extinction
       Answer: A. Self, world, and future viewed negatively
   Rationale: Beck's cognitive triad includes negative views of self, world, and future.

39. A depressed client begins to feel better, becomes more active, and then attempts suicide.
This illustrates:

   A. That suicide risk disappears when energy improves
   B. That suicide risk may increase when psychomotor retardation lifts before hopelessness
resolves
   C. That antidepressants always cause suicidality

 D. That depression with anxious distress cannot involve suicide
       Answer: B. That suicide risk may increase when psychomotor retardation lifts before
hopelessness resolves
   Rationale: Increased energy before mood improves may increase capacity to act on suicidal
thoughts.

40. Which symptom is considered a negative symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Delusion
   B. Hallucination
   C. Avolition

 D. Disorganized speech
       Answer: C. Avolition
   Rationale: Avolition is a negative symptom involving lack of motivation and reduced
goal-directed activity.

41. Thought disorder characterized by loose associations is most closely associated with:
   A. Panic disorder
   B. Schizophrenia spectrum disorders
   C. Dissociative amnesia
   D. Illness anxiety disorder
  Answer: B. Schizophrenia spectrum disorders

   Rationale: Loose associations reflect disorganized thinking, a core feature of schizophrenia
spectrum disorders.

42. A person has prominent delusions for more than 1 month with relatively preserved
functioning and no marked odd behavior. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Delusional disorder
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: B. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: Delusional disorder involves persistent delusions with relatively preserved
functioning and minimal impairment.

43. Which finding most strongly supports schizoaffective disorder?
   A. Psychosis only during substance intoxication
   B. Major mood episode present for the majority of the illness, with at least 2 weeks of

delusions or hallucinations without mood symptoms
   C. Chronic mistrust and suspiciousness

 D. Persistent health anxiety
       Answer: B. Major mood episode present for the majority of the illness, with at least 2
weeks of delusions or hallucinations without mood symptoms
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both mood episodes and periods of psychosis
without mood symptoms.

44. A patient shows sudden onset of psychosis lasting 10 days and then returns fully to
premorbid functioning. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Brief psychotic disorder lasts less than one month with full return to baseline
functioning.

45. Which term refers to a disturbance in consciousness and attention with an acute onset and
fluctuating course?

   A. Dementia
   B. Delirium
   C. Amnestic disorder

 D. Mild intellectual disability
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Delirium involves acute, fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness.
46. Major neurocognitive disorder differs from mild neurocognitive disorder primarily because:
   A. Mild NCD always includes delirium
   B. Major NCD substantially interferes with independence in everyday activities
   C. Mild NCD requires psychosis

 D. Major NCD cannot be due to Alzheimer's disease
       Answer: B. Major NCD substantially interferes with independence in everyday activities
   Rationale: The defining distinction is the level of functional impairment in daily life.

47. Which feature is most typical of Alzheimer's disease?
   A. Abrupt onset with stepwise decline
   B. Early fluctuating consciousness
   C. Insidious onset with gradual progressive decline

 D. Immediate onset after trauma only
       Answer: C. Insidious onset with gradual progressive decline
   Rationale: Alzheimer's disease typically shows gradual onset and continuous cognitive
decline.

48. A vascular pattern of neurocognitive disorder is most suggested by:
   A. Gradual continuous decline with no focal deficits
   B. Stepwise deterioration associated with cerebrovascular disease
   C. Hallucinations only

 D. Exclusive autobiographical amnesia
       Answer: B. Stepwise deterioration associated with cerebrovascular disease
   Rationale: Vascular NCD often presents with stepwise decline linked to vascular events.

49. ADHD is best conceptualized as involving persistent patterns of:
   A. Delusions and hallucinations
   B. Inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity across settings
   C. Repetitive motor stereotypies only

 D. Separation anxiety only
       Answer: B. Inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity across settings
   Rationale: ADHD is defined by persistent inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity in
multiple settings.

50. Which finding best supports autism spectrum disorder rather than social anxiety disorder?
   A. Fear of embarrassment in social situations
   B. Restricted, repetitive patterns of behavior plus deficits in social communication
   C. Panic attacks in crowds

 D. Excessive worry about multiple life areas
       Answer: B. Restricted, repetitive patterns of behavior plus deficits in social communication
   Rationale: Autism spectrum disorder requires both social communication deficits and
restricted/repetitive behaviors.
51. A child has normal intelligence but persistent difficulty in word reading and spelling despite
adequate instruction. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. Specific learning disorder
   C. Communication disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Specific learning disorder involves academic skill deficits despite adequate
instruction and intelligence.

52. Intellectual disability requires deficits in intellectual functions and:
   A. A history of psychosis
   B. Adaptive functioning with onset during developmental period
   C. Mood instability

 D. Obsessions and compulsions
       Answer: B. Adaptive functioning with onset during developmental period
   Rationale: Diagnosis requires deficits in both intellectual and adaptive functioning beginning
in development.

53. Which feature is most central to oppositional defiant disorder?
   A. Serious violation of the rights of others
   B. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, or vindictiveness
   C. Repetitive fire-setting for pleasure

 D. Impulsive stealing of unneeded objects
       Answer: B. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, or
vindictiveness
