   Rationale: ODD is defined by persistent patterns of defiance, irritability, and hostility.

54. Which behavior most strongly suggests conduct disorder rather than oppositional defiant
disorder?

   A. Frequent arguments with adults
   B. Deliberate cruelty to animals
   C. Temper tantrums

 D. Easily annoyed mood
       Answer: B. Deliberate cruelty to animals
   Rationale: Conduct disorder involves serious violations of rights, including cruelty to animals.

55. Recurrent behavioral outbursts representing failure to control aggressive impulses that are
grossly out of proportion best describe:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: IED involves impulsive aggressive outbursts disproportionate to provocation.

56. Which feature is required for antisocial personality disorder?
   A. Age less than 15 years
   B. Evidence of conduct disorder before age 15
   C. Presence of panic attacks

 D. Social inhibition due to feelings of inadequacy
       Answer: B. Evidence of conduct disorder before age 15
   Rationale: ASPD requires prior conduct disorder symptoms before age 15.

57. A client frantically avoids abandonment, has unstable relationships, recurrent self-harm, and
affective instability. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: These features are core characteristics of borderline personality disorder.

58. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy are most characteristic of:
   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Narcissistic personality disorder includes grandiosity and lack of empathy.

59. Social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to criticism are most
characteristic of:

   A. Avoidant personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Paranoid personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: A. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder is marked by social inhibition and sensitivity to
rejection.

60. A pervasive need to be taken care of leading to submissive and clinging behavior is most
characteristic of:

   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. Schizotypal personality disorder

 D. Narcissistic personality disorder
       Answer: A. Dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Dependent personality disorder involves excessive reliance on others.

61. Preoccupation with orderliness, perfectionism, and control at the expense of flexibility best
describes:

   A. OCD
   B. OCPD
   C. Hoarding disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. OCPD
   Rationale: Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder involves a pervasive pattern of
perfectionism, rigidity, and control that is ego-syntonic.

62. Repeated use of a substance despite impairment, craving, and unsuccessful efforts to cut
down best indicates:

   A. Substance use disorder
   B. Substance intoxication only
   C. Substance withdrawal only

 D. Factitious disorder
       Answer: A. Substance use disorder
   Rationale: Substance use disorder is characterized by impaired control, craving, and
continued use despite negative consequences.

63. Which finding most strongly supports substance withdrawal rather than intoxication?
   A. Recent ingestion producing maladaptive behavioral changes
   B. Syndrome following reduction or cessation after prolonged heavy use
   C. Delusions lasting years with no substance history

 D. Fear of illness despite reassurance
       Answer: B. Syndrome following reduction or cessation after prolonged heavy use
   Rationale: Withdrawal occurs after reduction or cessation of prolonged substance use.

64. Gambling disorder is classified with substance-related and addictive disorders primarily
because it:

   A. Always involves intoxication
   B. Shares core features of impaired control, craving-like urges, and continued behavior
despite harm
   C. Is always illegal

 D. Requires psychotic symptoms
       Answer: B. Shares core features of impaired control, craving-like urges, and continued
behavior despite harm
   Rationale: Gambling disorder shares behavioral and neurobiological similarities with
substance addictions.

65. Recurrent stealing of objects not needed for personal use or monetary value is:
   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Kleptomania
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Hoarding disorder
       Answer: B. Kleptomania
   Rationale: Kleptomania involves recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal items of little
value.

66. Deliberate and purposeful fire-setting on more than one occasion with fascination for fire
suggests:

   A. Intermittent explosive disorder
   B. Pyromania
   C. Conduct disorder only

 D. Mania
       Answer: B. Pyromania
   Rationale: Pyromania involves repeated fire-setting with fascination and tension/arousal
before the act.

67. Which is the strongest indicator of malingering in a forensic setting?
   A. Distress about symptoms
   B. Clear external incentive for appearing mentally ill
   C. Family history of schizophrenia

 D. Onset in adolescence
       Answer: B. Clear external incentive for appearing mentally ill
   Rationale: Malingering is strongly suggested by the presence of external incentives such as
legal avoidance.

68. Which psychologist is most strongly associated with classical psychoanalysis?
   A. Aaron Beck
   B. B. F. Skinner
   C. Sigmund Freud

 D. Albert Bandura
       Answer: C. Sigmund Freud
   Rationale: Freud is the founder of psychoanalysis and emphasized unconscious processes
and conflict.

69. The behavioral perspective is most strongly associated with:
   A. Observable behavior and learning principles
   B. Archetypes and collective unconscious
   C. Free association

 D. Moral therapy alone
       Answer: A. Observable behavior and learning principles
   Rationale: Behaviorism focuses on observable behavior and learning mechanisms such as
conditioning.
70. Which theorist is most associated with client-centered or person-centered therapy?
   A. Carl Rogers
   B. Ivan Pavlov
   C. Emil Kraepelin

 D. Albert Ellis
       Answer: A. Carl Rogers
   Rationale: Rogers developed person-centered therapy emphasizing empathy and
unconditional positive regard.

71. The concept of systematic desensitization is most associated with:
   A. Carl Jung
   B. Joseph Wolpe
   C. Alfred Adler

 D. Fritz Perls
       Answer: B. Joseph Wolpe
   Rationale: Wolpe introduced systematic desensitization as a behavioral treatment for anxiety.

72. Aaron Beck is best known for:
   A. Classical conditioning of phobic responses
   B. Cognitive therapy emphasizing maladaptive automatic thoughts
   C. Psychosexual stages

 D. Modeling and observational learning
       Answer: B. Cognitive therapy emphasizing maladaptive automatic thoughts
   Rationale: Beck developed cognitive therapy focusing on automatic thoughts and cognitive
distortions.

73. Albert Bandura's work is most closely linked to:
   A. Learned helplessness
   B. Social learning and modeling
   C. Moral treatment

 D. Deinstitutionalization
       Answer: B. Social learning and modeling
   Rationale: Bandura emphasized observational learning and modeling in behavior.

74. Martin Seligman is strongly associated with the concept of:
   A. Learned helplessness
   B. Reciprocal inhibition
   C. Free association

 D. Token economy
       Answer: A. Learned helplessness
   Rationale: Seligman developed the concept of learned helplessness in relation to depression.

75. Emil Kraepelin is important in abnormal psychology because he:
   A. Developed person-centered therapy
   B. Helped classify mental disorders based on symptom patterns and course
   C. Founded behavior therapy

 D. Proposed the hierarchy of needs
       Answer: B. Helped classify mental disorders based on symptom patterns and course
   Rationale: Kraepelin contributed to modern psychiatric classification systems.

76. Philippe Pinel is historically associated with:
   A. Trephination
   B. Moral treatment and more humane care of the mentally ill
   C. Aversion therapy

 D. Psychopharmacology
       Answer: B. Moral treatment and more humane care of the mentally ill
   Rationale: Pinel advocated humane treatment of individuals with mental illness.

77. Which statement about defense mechanisms is most accurate in psychodynamic theory?
   A. They are deliberate, conscious lies
   B. They are unconscious processes used to manage internal conflict and anxiety
   C. They occur only in psychotic disorders

 D. They are identical to compulsions
       Answer: B. They are unconscious processes used to manage internal conflict and anxiety
   Rationale: Defense mechanisms operate unconsciously to reduce anxiety and conflict.

78. A client attributes his own hostile impulses to others and insists everyone else is angry with
him. This defense mechanism is:

   A. Sublimation
   B. Projection
   C. Displacement

 D. Regression
       Answer: B. Projection
   Rationale: Projection involves attributing one's own unacceptable feelings to others.

79. Which statement best reflects the integrative approach to treatment?
   A. One treatment model works equally well for all disorders and all clients
   B. Effective treatment often requires combining biological, psychological, and social

considerations
   C. Medications always outperform psychotherapy

 D. Ethical issues are secondary to symptom reduction
       Answer: B. Effective treatment often requires combining biological, psychological, and
social considerations
   Rationale: Integrative approaches combine multiple perspectives for comprehensive care.

80. In research, a variable manipulated by the investigator is the:
   A. Dependent variable
   B. Confounding variable
   C. Independent variable

 D. Criterion variable
       Answer: C. Independent variable
   Rationale: The independent variable is manipulated to observe its effect on outcomes.

81. The major advantage of a randomized controlled trial is that it:
   A. Eliminates all attrition
   B. Allows stronger causal inference
   C. Guarantees ecological validity

 D. Replaces need for clinical judgment
       Answer: B. Allows stronger causal inference
   Rationale: Randomization reduces bias and strengthens causal conclusions.

82. A statistically significant result means:
   A. The treatment effect is always large and clinically meaningful
   B. The result is unlikely due to chance alone, given the statistical assumptions
   C. The null hypothesis is proven false in all populations

 D. Every patient improved substantially
       Answer: B. The result is unlikely due to chance alone, given the statistical assumptions
   Rationale: Statistical significance indicates low probability of results occurring by chance.

83. Which method is best for examining whether two variables are related without manipulating
them?

   A. Experimental design
   B. Correlational design
   C. Case formulation only

 D. Multiple-baseline intervention
       Answer: B. Correlational design
   Rationale: Correlational designs assess relationships without manipulation.

84. Which diagnosis should be considered when depressive symptoms are better explained by
a medical condition such as hypothyroidism?

   A. Major depressive disorder only
   B. Depressive disorder due to another medical condition
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Depressive disorder due to another medical condition
   Rationale: Symptoms caused by medical conditions are classified separately from primary
mood disorders.

85. A person has panic attacks only during episodes of cocaine intoxication. The most
appropriate diagnosis is:

   A. Panic disorder
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Substance-induced anxiety disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Substance-induced anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Symptoms occurring exclusively during substance use are classified as
substance-induced.

86. Which disorder involves a pattern of detachment from social relationships and restricted
range of emotional expression?

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Schizotypal personality disorder

 D. Social anxiety disorder
       Answer: A. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizoid personality disorder involves detachment and limited emotional
expression.

87. Odd beliefs, unusual perceptual experiences, and social deficits are most characteristic of:
   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizotypal personality disorder includes eccentric behavior and
cognitive-perceptual distortions.

88. Which finding best distinguishes obsessive-compulsive personality disorder from
obsessive-compulsive disorder?

   A. OCPD includes perfectionism that is often ego-syntonic
   B. OCPD always includes intrusive obsessions
   C. OCD is always ego-syntonic

 D. OCD never includes repetitive behavior
       Answer: A. OCPD includes perfectionism that is often ego-syntonic
   Rationale: OCPD traits are typically ego-syntonic, unlike OCD symptoms.

89. Under RA 10029 and the PAP Code, which statement is most accurate?
   A. Any psychology graduate may independently practice psychometrics if supervised

informally
   B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians are legally allowed to

practice their profession within legal boundaries
   C. Test interpretation may be delegated to any office staff member

 D. Licensure is optional in telepsychology
       Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians are legally
allowed to practice their profession within legal boundaries
   Rationale: RA 10029 restricts professional practice to licensed individuals within defined
scopes.

90. A psychometrician is asked to administer a test for a referral question outside the intended
purpose of the instrument and for a population without relevant norms. The most ethical
response is to:

   A. Proceed because any standardized test is acceptable
   B. Use the test but omit the limitations in the report
   C. Decline or recommend a more appropriate assessment method or referral

 D. Alter the scoring to fit the client's background
       Answer: C. Decline or recommend a more appropriate assessment method or referral
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires appropriate test use and recognition of limitations.

91. Which is most consistent with ethical handling of test data?
   A. Releasing raw scores to any requesting teacher by phone
   B. Posting protocols in a shared office drive for convenience
   C. Restricting release of test data and interpretations to authorized parties, subject to proper

consent and legal limits

 D. Sending all materials to family members without explanation
       Answer: C. Restricting release of test data and interpretations to authorized parties,
subject to proper consent and legal limits
   Rationale: Confidentiality and proper authorization govern release of assessment data.

92. In third-party requested assessment, the psychologist or psychometrician should clarify at
the outset:

   A. That confidentiality is unlimited
   B. Role expectations, who the client is, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
   C. That the referral source automatically owns all test data

 D. That informed consent is unnecessary
       Answer: B. Role expectations, who the client is, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
   Rationale: Clarifying roles and limits of confidentiality is essential in third-party contexts.

93. Which practice best reflects ethical informed consent in assessment?
   A. Obtaining consent only after testing is complete
   B. Using highly technical language so the client recognizes expertise
   C. Explaining the nature and purpose of services, risks, financial arrangements, and limits of

confidentiality in understandable language

 D. Avoiding discussion of limits of confidentiality to reduce anxiety
       Answer: C. Explaining the nature and purpose of services, risks, financial arrangements,
and limits of confidentiality in understandable language
   Rationale: Informed consent requires clear, understandable disclosure of relevant
information.
94. A practitioner experiences personal problems that may impair professional functioning.
Ethically, the best course is to:

   A. Continue working unchanged because self-disclosure is unprofessional
   B. Ignore the issue unless a complaint is filed
   C. Seek consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or terminate
duties

 D. Transfer all responsibility to trainees immediately
       Answer: C. Seek consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or
terminate duties
   Rationale: Professionals must address impairment to prevent harm and maintain
competence.

95. A psychometrician is asked to independently interpret complex neuropsychological findings
beyond training and competence. The best ethical action is to:

   A. Provide the interpretation to appear helpful
   B. Interpret only the sections that seem familiar and guess the rest
   C. Work within competence and refer to a qualified professional as needed

 D. Ask the client to decide the meaning of the results
       Answer: C. Work within competence and refer to a qualified professional as needed
   Rationale: Ethical standards require practice within one's competence and appropriate
referral.

96. Which action is most ethical when another practitioner's conduct may be causing substantial
harm?

   A. Ignore it to preserve collegiality
   B. Publicly shame the practitioner online
   C. Take appropriate action, which may include reporting to proper authorities if informal
resolution is insufficient and confidentiality rights are respected

 D. File a complaint without evidence
       Answer: C. Take appropriate action, which may include reporting to proper authorities if
informal resolution is insufficient and confidentiality rights are respected
   Rationale: Ethical responsibility includes preventing harm through appropriate reporting and
action.

97. In telepsychology, the PAP Code indicates that:
   A. Ethics for face-to-face work do not apply online
   B. Online services are exempt from confidentiality standards
   C. The same ethical principles governing face-to-face services apply to services conducted

virtually

 D. Test security is irrelevant if the client agrees
       Answer: C. The same ethical principles governing face-to-face services apply to services
conducted virtually
   Rationale: Ethical principles remain applicable regardless of service modality.
98. When explaining test results to clients or authorized recipients, the most ethical approach is
to:

   A. Use only technical jargon to preserve precision
   B. Explain findings clearly, including limitations, in language appropriate to the recipient
   C. Share all raw items to prove transparency

 D. Withhold all findings to avoid emotional reactions
       Answer: B. Explain findings clearly, including limitations, in language appropriate to the
recipient
   Rationale: Ethical feedback requires clarity, appropriateness, and inclusion of limitations.

99. A board exam candidate is asked which situation most clearly violates competence
boundaries. Which is the best answer?

   A. Referring a case to a more qualified specialist
   B. Studying a new method before using it under proper supervision
   C. Accepting a forensic evaluation without adequate training in relevant legal and
administrative rules

 D. Seeking consultation for a complex case
       Answer: C. Accepting a forensic evaluation without adequate training in relevant legal and
administrative rules
   Rationale: Practicing beyond competence, especially in specialized areas like forensic work,
violates ethical standards.

100. Which statement best captures ethical and professional responsibility in abnormal
psychology practice in the Philippines?

    A. Legal compliance alone is sufficient even if clients are harmed
    B. Ethical practice requires competence, respect for dignity, confidentiality, integrity, and
adherence to applicable law such as RA 10029
    C. Ethics apply only to psychotherapy, not assessment

 D. A good outcome justifies questionable methods
        Answer: B. Ethical practice requires competence, respect for dignity, confidentiality,
integrity, and adherence to applicable law such as RA 10029
    Rationale: Ethical and legal practice requires adherence to professional standards, client
welfare, and governing laws.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 5
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 5

1. A clinician evaluating a patient with newly reported hallucinations should first consider which
broad diagnostic principle before concluding that a primary psychotic disorder is present?

  A. Whether the hallucinations are culturally sanctioned
  B. Whether malingering, substance effects, or a medical condition may account for the
symptoms
  C. Whether the patient has a family history of schizophrenia

 D. Whether the patient meets criteria for a personality disorder
       Answer: B. Whether malingering, substance effects, or a medical condition may account
for the symptoms
  Rationale: Differential diagnosis begins by ruling out feigning, substance-induced causes, and
medical etiologies before concluding that a primary psychiatric disorder is present.

2. A patient intentionally fabricates psychiatric symptoms to avoid criminal prosecution. The
most appropriate classification is:

  A. Factitious disorder
  B. Somatic symptom disorder
  C. Malingering

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Malingering
  Rationale: Malingering involves intentional production or exaggeration of symptoms for clear
external incentives, such as avoiding prosecution.

3. Which feature most strongly suggests factitious disorder rather than malingering?
  A. The presence of obvious financial gain
  B. The absence of clear external rewards despite deliberate symptom falsification
  C. The presence of severe distress about health

 D. The existence of a co-occurring medical illness
       Answer: B. The absence of clear external rewards despite deliberate symptom falsification
  Rationale: Factitious disorder is distinguished by intentional falsification of symptoms without
obvious external incentives.

4. A 19-year-old college student develops paranoid ideation and auditory hallucinations after
several days of stimulant binge use. The most appropriate initial diagnostic consideration is:

  A. Delusional disorder
  B. Schizophreniform disorder
  C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder
  Rationale: When psychotic symptoms occur in close temporal relationship to stimulant
intoxication or withdrawal, a substance-induced psychotic disorder must be considered before a
primary psychotic disorder.
5. Which of the following best illustrates the need to rule out an etiological medical condition in
abnormal psychology?

  A. A patient with panic attacks triggered by public speaking
  B. A patient with abrupt personality change following head trauma
  C. A patient with chronic perfectionism and rigidity

 D. A patient with long-standing fear of contamination
       Answer: B. A patient with abrupt personality change following head trauma
  Rationale: A sudden personality change after head trauma raises concern for a neurological
or medical cause that must be ruled out before assigning a primary mental disorder diagnosis.

6. A person presents with depressed mood after job loss but does not meet full criteria for major
depressive disorder. Symptoms began within three months of the stressor and cause marked
distress. The best diagnosis is:

  A. Persistent depressive disorder
  B. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood
  C. Unspecified depressive disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood
  Rationale: Adjustment disorder is appropriate when symptoms arise in response to an
identifiable stressor, cause distress or impairment, and do not meet criteria for another full
disorder.

7. Which statement best reflects the multidimensional model of psychopathology?
  A. Most mental disorders are caused by a single dominant factor
  B. Biological factors are more important than psychosocial influences
  C. Psychopathology results from interacting biological, psychological, and social factors

 D. Social factors explain most disorders better than neuroscience
       Answer: C. Psychopathology results from interacting biological, psychological, and social
factors
  Rationale: The multidimensional model holds that mental disorders emerge from the
interaction of biological, psychological, and social influences.

8. Which psychologist is most strongly associated with classical psychoanalysis and the role of
unconscious conflict?

  A. Ivan Pavlov
  B. Sigmund Freud
  C. Carl Rogers

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: B. Sigmund Freud
  Rationale: Freud is the central figure in psychoanalysis and emphasized unconscious conflict,
early experience, and intrapsychic processes.

9. The principle of moral therapy emphasized:
  A. Restraint and institutional isolation
  B. Humane treatment, structured routines, and respectful care
  C. Punishment of deviant behavior

 D. Exclusive reliance on somatic treatments
       Answer: B. Humane treatment, structured routines, and respectful care
  Rationale: Moral therapy emphasized humane, compassionate, orderly, and respectful
treatment of individuals with mental disorders.

10. Hippocrates is historically important in abnormal psychology because he:
   A. Proposed demonological explanations of mental disorder
   B. Argued that mental disorders had natural rather than supernatural causes
   C. Developed psychoanalytic theory

 D. Introduced behavioral therapy
       Answer: B. Argued that mental disorders had natural rather than supernatural causes
   Rationale: Hippocrates helped shift thinking away from supernatural explanations by
proposing natural bodily causes for mental disturbances.

11. A child begins to fear dogs after being bitten. Later, the child avoids parks, sidewalks, and
even pictures of dogs. This pattern is best explained initially by:

   A. Classical conditioning
   B. Projective identification
   C. Free association

 D. Response cost
       Answer: A. Classical conditioning
   Rationale: The fear response became associated with dogs after the bite, illustrating
acquisition of phobic fear through classical conditioning.

12. Which concept is most closely associated with Seligman's reformulation of depression?
   A. Systematic desensitization
   B. Learned helplessness
   C. Reciprocal inhibition

 D. Token economy
       Answer: B. Learned helplessness
   Rationale: Seligman's model proposes that exposure to uncontrollable stressors can foster
passivity, hopelessness, and depressive symptoms.

13. A clinician using the scientist-practitioner model would most likely:
   A. Avoid research because it interferes with therapy
   B. Base decisions on intuition alone
   C. Integrate clinical observation, evidence, and outcome monitoring

 D. Focus only on randomized trials and never on case material
       Answer: C. Integrate clinical observation, evidence, and outcome monitoring
   Rationale: The scientist-practitioner model combines empirical evidence, systematic clinical
observation, and ongoing evaluation of outcomes.
14. Which assessment method is generally most useful for obtaining a broad history, current
symptoms, and contextual information?

   A. Neuroimaging
   B. Clinical interview
   C. Projective drawing task

 D. Polygraph testing
       Answer: B. Clinical interview
   Rationale: The clinical interview is the primary broad assessment tool for obtaining presenting
concerns, history, symptom course, and psychosocial context.

15. A psychometrician in the Philippines is asked to administer a projective test independently in
a private clinic. Under RA 10029, the most appropriate response is:

   A. Proceed independently if previously exposed to the test in school
   B. Proceed if the client signs informed consent
   C. Decline or refer because this exceeds the authorized scope of psychometric practice

 D. Proceed if raw scores are reviewed later by a psychologist
       Answer: C. Decline or refer because this exceeds the authorized scope of psychometric
practice
   Rationale: Projective and other higher-level psychological tests exceed the authorized
independent scope of psychometric practice under RA 10029.

16. Under RA 10029, which activity is within the authorized functions of a psychometrician when
properly supervised?

   A. Independent psychotherapy
   B. Administration and scoring of objective personality tests
   C. Independent interpretation of projective tests for court use

 D. Independent diagnosis of schizophrenia
       Answer: B. Administration and scoring of objective personality tests
   Rationale: Psychometricians may administer and score objective and structured personality
tests when properly supervised.

17. A psychometrician is asked to conduct intake interviewing before psychological intervention
sessions. Under RA 10029, this is:

   A. Prohibited in all settings
   B. Allowed only for psychiatrists
   C. Allowed under supervision of a licensed psychologist

 D. Allowed only without documentation
       Answer: C. Allowed under supervision of a licensed psychologist
   Rationale: Preparatory intake interviewing may be performed by a psychometrician when
done under the supervision of a licensed psychologist.

18. Which is the best example of a conflict of interest in psychological practice?
   A. Referring a client for laboratory work
   B. Providing services in one's area of competence
   C. Taking on a case in which personal financial interests may impair objectivity

 D. Explaining confidentiality at intake
       Answer: C. Taking on a case in which personal financial interests may impair objectivity
   Rationale: A conflict of interest exists when personal or financial interests may impair
professional objectivity or expose the client to harm or exploitation.

19. A psychologist agrees to evaluate an employee at the request of the employer. Ethically, the
psychologist should first clarify:

   A. Only the employee's diagnosis
   B. The nature of the relationship, who the client is, and limits of confidentiality
   C. Whether the employee likes testing

 D. Whether treatment will be free
       Answer: B. The nature of the relationship, who the client is, and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: In third-party referral situations, the psychologist must clarify roles, identify who the
client is, and explain the limits of confidentiality.

20. Which ethical principle is most directly violated when a practitioner discloses identifiable test
findings to a client's coworkers without authorization?

   A. Beneficence
   B. Fidelity
   C. Confidentiality

 D. Competence
       Answer: C. Confidentiality
   Rationale: Unauthorized disclosure of identifiable assessment information violates
confidentiality and privacy protections.

21. Which statement about informed consent is most accurate?
   A. It is unnecessary when assessment is brief
   B. It requires reasonably understandable language and discussion of relevant limits
   C. It applies only to psychotherapy, not assessment

 D. It can be replaced by implied compliance in all situations
       Answer: B. It requires reasonably understandable language and discussion of relevant
limits
   Rationale: Valid informed consent requires understandable explanation of the service,
procedures, and relevant limits such as confidentiality.

22. A practitioner uses a test with no appropriate normative data for the client's population and
then makes strong conclusions. This primarily violates ethical standards on:

   A. Barter
   B. Test selection and interpretation
   C. Advertising

 D. Record retention
       Answer: B. Test selection and interpretation
   Rationale: Using instruments without appropriate norms and then making strong conclusions
violates standards requiring valid and appropriate test selection and interpretation.

23. Which of the following should generally not be released as part of ordinary test disclosure?
   A. A feedback summary in understandable language
   B. The referral question
   C. Raw and scaled scores to unauthorized persons

 D. General recommendations
       Answer: C. Raw and scaled scores to unauthorized persons
   Rationale: Raw and scaled scores and other test data should not be released to unauthorized
individuals because of test security and risk of misuse.

24. A 7-year-old child shows persistent inattention across home and school, often loses
materials, is forgetful in daily activities, and interrupts others. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Autism spectrum disorder
   B. Attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   C. Oppositional defiant disorder

 D. Separation anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   Rationale: Persistent inattention, forgetfulness, losing materials, and interrupting across
settings strongly fit ADHD.

25. Which finding best distinguishes autism spectrum disorder from social anxiety disorder?
   A. Social discomfort in performance situations
   B. Persistent deficits in social communication plus restricted, repetitive patterns of behavior
   C. Fear of embarrassment

 D. Panic attacks during peer interaction
       Answer: B. Persistent deficits in social communication plus restricted, repetitive patterns
of behavior
   Rationale: Autism spectrum disorder requires both social communication deficits and
restricted, repetitive behaviors, which distinguish it from social anxiety disorder.

26. A student of average intelligence has marked difficulty in reading accuracy and spelling
despite adequate instruction. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. Specific learning disorder
   C. Communication disorder due to autism

 D. Developmental coordination disorder
       Answer: B. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Circumscribed academic difficulty in reading and spelling despite adequate
instruction and average intelligence is characteristic of specific learning disorder.

27. Which feature is required for intellectual disability?
   A. Psychosis before age 18
   B. Deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning with onset during the developmental period
   C. Severe motor abnormalities only

 D. A history of institutionalization
       Answer: B. Deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning with onset during the
developmental period
   Rationale: Intellectual disability requires deficits in both intellectual and adaptive functioning
beginning during the developmental period.

28. Tourette's disorder requires:
   A. One motor tic only
   B. One vocal tic only
   C. Multiple motor tics and at least one vocal tic at some time during the illness

 D. Tics caused by substance use
       Answer: C. Multiple motor tics and at least one vocal tic at some time during the illness
   Rationale: Tourette's disorder requires both multiple motor tics and at least one vocal tic,
though they need not occur simultaneously.

29. Which symptom is a positive symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Avolition
   B. Flat affect
   C. Delusions

 D. Alogia
       Answer: C. Delusions
   Rationale: Positive symptoms are additions to normal experience, and delusions are a classic
positive symptom of schizophrenia.

30. Which symptom is a negative symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Hallucinations
   B. Disorganized speech
   C. Diminished emotional expression

 D. Catatonic excitement
       Answer: C. Diminished emotional expression
   Rationale: Negative symptoms involve reduction or loss of normal functioning, including
diminished emotional expression.

31. A person has delusions for more than one month, with relatively preserved functioning and
no prominent hallucinations or marked disorganization. The diagnosis most consistent with this
presentation is:

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Schizoaffective disorder
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: A. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: Persistent delusions with relatively preserved functioning and without broad
psychotic deterioration are most consistent with delusional disorder.

32. Schizoaffective disorder is differentiated from schizophrenia primarily by the presence of:
   A. Any depressive symptom
   B. A major mood episode concurrent with psychotic symptoms, with psychosis also occurring

for at least a period without mood symptoms
   C. Panic attacks

 D. Substance use
       Answer: B. A major mood episode concurrent with psychotic symptoms, with psychosis
also occurring for at least a period without mood symptoms
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both a major mood episode and a period of
psychosis occurring without mood symptoms.

33. A patient has psychotic symptoms lasting less than one month, followed by full return to
premorbid functioning. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Brief psychotic disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: B. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Brief psychotic disorder involves psychosis lasting more than one day but less
than one month, followed by full return to premorbid functioning.

34. Which statement best distinguishes bipolar I disorder from bipolar II disorder?
   A. Bipolar I requires psychosis; bipolar II does not
   B. Bipolar II is more severe than bipolar I
   C. Bipolar I requires at least one manic episode; bipolar II requires hypomanic and major

depressive episodes without mania

 D. Bipolar I includes anxiety; bipolar II does not
       Answer: C. Bipolar I requires at least one manic episode; bipolar II requires hypomanic
and major depressive episodes without mania
   Rationale: A manic episode defines bipolar I disorder, whereas bipolar II disorder requires
hypomania plus major depressive episodes and no history of mania.

35. Cyclothymic disorder is characterized by:
   A. Alternating psychosis and depression
   B. Chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive symptoms that do not meet full episode

criteria
   C. A single manic episode

 D. Only seasonal depression
       Answer: B. Chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive symptoms that do not meet full
episode criteria
   Rationale: Cyclothymic disorder involves chronic mood fluctuation with subthreshold
hypomanic and depressive symptoms over time.

36. Which symptom is most characteristic of mania rather than hypomania?
   A. Mild increased productivity only
   B. Elevated mood with no impairment
   C. Marked impairment, possible hospitalization, or psychotic features

 D. Sleepiness and social withdrawal
       Answer: C. Marked impairment, possible hospitalization, or psychotic features
   Rationale: Mania is distinguished from hypomania by marked impairment, need for
hospitalization, or possible psychotic features.

37. Persistent depressive disorder is best described as:
   A. Acute severe depression with psychotic features
   B. Chronic depressed mood lasting at least two years in adults
   C. Mood reactivity with hypersomnia only

 D. Depression occurring only after bereavement
       Answer: B. Chronic depressed mood lasting at least two years in adults
   Rationale: Persistent depressive disorder involves long-term depressed mood for most of the
day, more days than not, for at least two years in adults.

38. A child with recurrent severe temper outbursts and persistently irritable mood between
outbursts is most consistent with:

   A. Pediatric bipolar I disorder
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder only
       Answer: C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   Rationale: DMDD is defined by severe recurrent temper outbursts and persistent irritability in
children.

39. Which cognitive pattern is commonly associated with depression?
   A. Grandiosity and pressured speech
   B. Overestimation of control and optimism
   C. Negative automatic thoughts about self, world, and future

 D. Obsessions about contamination only
       Answer: C. Negative automatic thoughts about self, world, and future
   Rationale: Beck's cognitive triad describes depressive thinking as negative views of the self,
the world, and the future.

40. A patient reports recurrent unexpected panic attacks and persistent concern about having
more attacks. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Generalized anxiety disorder
   B. Panic disorder
   C. Specific phobia

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Panic disorder
   Rationale: Panic disorder involves recurrent unexpected panic attacks followed by persistent
concern or behavioral change related to future attacks.

41. Agoraphobia involves marked fear or anxiety about:
   A. Social judgment only
   B. Separation from attachment figures only
   C. Situations where escape may be difficult or help unavailable if panic-like symptoms occur

 D. Contamination from public objects only
       Answer: C. Situations where escape may be difficult or help unavailable if panic-like
symptoms occur
   Rationale: Agoraphobia involves fear of situations where escape may be difficult or help may
be unavailable if panic-like or incapacitating symptoms occur.

42. Which feature best distinguishes generalized anxiety disorder from panic disorder?
   A. Worry in GAD is excessive, persistent, and broad across domains
   B. Panic disorder always includes depression
   C. GAD requires compulsions

 D. Panic disorder has no physical symptoms
       Answer: A. Worry in GAD is excessive, persistent, and broad across domains
   Rationale: Generalized anxiety disorder is defined by chronic, excessive, and
difficult-to-control worry across multiple life domains.

43. A client is intensely afraid of being negatively evaluated in conversations, meetings, and
performances. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Panic disorder
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Social anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Social anxiety disorder centers on fear of negative evaluation in social or
performance situations.

44. Which treatment has the strongest evidence base for many anxiety disorders and phobias?
   A. Insight-oriented dream analysis alone
   B. Exposure-based cognitive behavioral therapy
   C. Long-term hospitalization

 D. Electroconvulsive therapy
       Answer: B. Exposure-based cognitive behavioral therapy
   Rationale: Exposure-based CBT is among the most strongly supported treatments for many
anxiety disorders and phobias.
45. Posttraumatic stress disorder requires exposure to trauma plus symptoms from which
clusters?

   A. Only sadness and insomnia
   B. Intrusion, avoidance, negative alterations in cognition/mood, and arousal/reactivity
   C. Delusions and disorganized speech

 D. Hyperactivity and impulsivity
       Answer: B. Intrusion, avoidance, negative alterations in cognition/mood, and
arousal/reactivity
   Rationale: PTSD requires trauma exposure plus symptoms from the core clusters of intrusion,
avoidance, negative changes in cognition or mood, and arousal/reactivity.

46. Which diagnosis is most appropriate when symptoms develop soon after a trauma but do
not persist beyond one month?

   A. PTSD
   B. Acute stress disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Acute stress disorder
   Rationale: Acute stress disorder occurs soon after trauma and is limited to the first month
following the event.

47. Obsessions are best defined as:
   A. Repetitive behaviors performed to reduce anxiety
   B. Fixed false beliefs not amenable to evidence
   C. Intrusive, unwanted thoughts, urges, or images that cause distress

 D. Recurrent mood swings
       Answer: C. Intrusive, unwanted thoughts, urges, or images that cause distress
   Rationale: Obsessions are intrusive, unwanted mental events that cause distress and are
usually resisted or neutralized.

48. Compulsions are:
   A. Hallucinations triggered by stress
   B. Repetitive behaviors or mental acts performed in response to obsessions or rigid rules
   C. Mood-congruent delusions

 D. Sudden aggressive impulses only
       Answer: B. Repetitive behaviors or mental acts performed in response to obsessions or
rigid rules
   Rationale: Compulsions are repetitive behaviors or mental acts performed to reduce anxiety
or prevent a feared outcome.

49. A person persistently misperceives slight facial irregularities as hideous defects and
engages in repetitive mirror checking. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Narcissistic personality disorder
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Body dysmorphic disorder involves preoccupation with perceived appearance
defects and repetitive behaviors such as mirror checking.

50. Which feature best characterizes hoarding disorder?
   A. Fear of fatness and food restriction
   B. Persistent difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value
   C. Intrusive sexual thoughts alone

 D. Impulsive fire-setting
       Answer: B. Persistent difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder is defined by persistent difficulty discarding possessions,
leading to clutter and impairment.

51. Recurrent hair pulling resulting in noticeable hair loss is most consistent with:
   A. Excoriation disorder
   B. Trichotillomania
   C. OCD with poor insight

 D. Body dysmorphic disorder
       Answer: B. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Trichotillomania involves recurrent hair pulling that causes hair loss and repeated
attempts to stop.

52. Somatic symptom disorder emphasizes:
   A. Complete absence of somatic complaints
   B. Excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors related to distressing somatic symptoms
   C. Deliberate production of illness

 D. Fear of one disease without any bodily symptoms whatsoever
       Answer: B. Excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors related to distressing somatic
symptoms
   Rationale: Somatic symptom disorder emphasizes an excessive psychological response to
distressing somatic symptoms rather than whether symptoms are medically explained.

53. Illness anxiety disorder is most likely when a person:
   A. Has multiple neurological conversion symptoms
   B. Is preoccupied with having or acquiring serious illness despite minimal or absent somatic

symptoms
   C. Fabricates illness for external gain

 D. Has chronic psychotic symptoms about infection
       Answer: B. Is preoccupied with having or acquiring serious illness despite minimal or
absent somatic symptoms
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder centers on persistent preoccupation with serious illness
despite minimal or absent physical symptoms.
54. Conversion disorder involves:
   A. Intentional feigning of neurological symptoms
   B. Neurological-like symptoms incompatible with recognized medical conditions
   C. Fear of having illness with no symptoms

 D. Obsessive concern about appearance
       Answer: B. Neurological-like symptoms incompatible with recognized medical conditions
   Rationale: Conversion disorder involves motor or sensory symptoms suggesting neurological
illness that are incompatible with recognized neurological disease.

55. Which diagnosis involves falsification of symptoms or induction of illness without obvious
external rewards?

   A. Malingering
   B. Factitious disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Factitious disorder
   Rationale: Factitious disorder involves deliberate falsification or induction of symptoms
without clear external incentives.

56. Depersonalization refers to:
   A. Loss of autobiographical memory after trauma
   B. A sense of unreality or detachment from one's self
   C. A belief that others control one's thoughts

 D. Confabulation due to brain injury
       Answer: B. A sense of unreality or detachment from one's self
   Rationale: Depersonalization is the experience of feeling detached from one's own thoughts,
body, or self.

57. Dissociative amnesia is characterized primarily by:
   A. Inability to learn new material because of dementia
   B. Inability to recall important autobiographical information, usually of a traumatic or stressful

nature
   C. Hallucinations after substance use

 D. Chronic depersonalization only
       Answer: B. Inability to recall important autobiographical information, usually of a traumatic
or stressful nature
   Rationale: Dissociative amnesia involves inability to recall important personal information,
often related to trauma or stress, beyond ordinary forgetting.

58. Which statement about dissociative identity disorder is most accurate?
   A. It is defined by ordinary forgetfulness only
   B. It involves disruption of identity with discontinuity in sense of self and recurrent amnesia
   C. It is synonymous with schizophrenia
 D. It always indicates malingering
       Answer: B. It involves disruption of identity with discontinuity in sense of self and recurrent
amnesia
   Rationale: Dissociative identity disorder involves identity disruption together with recurrent
gaps in memory for everyday events or traumatic experiences.

59. Anorexia nervosa is most clearly associated with:
   A. Recurrent binge eating without compensatory behavior only
   B. Restriction of energy intake leading to significantly low body weight and intense fear of

gaining weight
   C. Night eating only

 D. Normal weight with panic attacks
       Answer: B. Restriction of energy intake leading to significantly low body weight and
intense fear of gaining weight
   Rationale: Anorexia nervosa is defined by restriction of intake leading to significantly low body
weight and intense fear of weight gain.

60. Bulimia nervosa includes:
   A. Starvation without body image disturbance
   B. Recurrent binge eating with inappropriate compensatory behaviors and overvaluation of

shape/weight
   C. Food restriction due to sensory aversion only

 D. Pica in adolescence
       Answer: B. Recurrent binge eating with inappropriate compensatory behaviors and
overvaluation of shape/weight
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa involves binge eating together with compensatory behaviors and
excessive concern with body shape or weight.

61. Binge-eating disorder differs from bulimia nervosa because binge-eating disorder:
   A. Includes no distress
   B. Lacks recurrent inappropriate compensatory behaviors
   C. Occurs only in underweight individuals

 D. Always includes purging
       Answer: B. Lacks recurrent inappropriate compensatory behaviors
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder involves binge episodes with distress but without the
recurrent compensatory behaviors seen in bulimia nervosa.

62. Which sleep-wake disorder is characterized by dissatisfaction with sleep quantity or quality
and associated daytime impairment despite adequate opportunity for sleep?

   A. Narcolepsy
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder

 D. Nightmare disorder
       Answer: B. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Insomnia disorder involves dissatisfaction with sleep quantity or quality and
resulting daytime impairment despite adequate opportunity for sleep.

63. Narcolepsy is commonly associated with:
   A. Sleep paralysis and cataplexy
   B. Grandiose delusions
   C. Severe food restriction

 D. Compulsive rituals
       Answer: A. Sleep paralysis and cataplexy
   Rationale: Narcolepsy commonly features excessive daytime sleepiness and may include
cataplexy and sleep paralysis.

64. Alcohol is classified as a:
   A. Hallucinogen
   B. Depressant
   C. Stimulant

 D. Dissociative anesthetic only
       Answer: B. Depressant
   Rationale: Alcohol is a central nervous system depressant.

65. Which neurotransmitter system is strongly implicated in the reward pathway of substance
use disorders?

   A. Dopamine
   B. Acetylcholine only
   C. Glycine only

 D. Oxytocin only
       Answer: A. Dopamine
   Rationale: Dopamine is strongly involved in reward circuitry and reinforcement processes in
substance use disorders.

66. Tolerance refers to:
   A. Withdrawal symptoms after stopping use
   B. Reduced effect of a substance at the same dose or need for increased amounts to achieve

the desired effect
   C. Legal immunity for drug use

 D. Complete loss of craving
       Answer: B. Reduced effect of a substance at the same dose or need for increased
amounts to achieve the desired effect
   Rationale: Tolerance reflects adaptation to repeated substance use, requiring more of the
substance or producing less effect at the same dose.

67. Withdrawal is best defined as:
   A. Refusal to discuss substance use
   B. A syndrome occurring when heavy and prolonged substance use is reduced or stopped
   C. Sudden psychodynamic insight

 D. Any intoxication effect
       Answer: B. A syndrome occurring when heavy and prolonged substance use is reduced or
stopped
   Rationale: Withdrawal is the physiological and psychological syndrome that emerges when
prolonged heavy substance use is reduced or stopped.

68. Gambling disorder is classified with substance-related and addictive disorders primarily
because of:

   A. Similar reward-related mechanisms and clinical features of addiction
   B. Presence of hallucinations during betting
   C. Mandatory withdrawal seizures

 D. It always occurs with alcohol dependence
       Answer: A. Similar reward-related mechanisms and clinical features of addiction
   Rationale: Gambling disorder shares impaired control, persistence despite harm, and
reward-related mechanisms similar to addictive disorders.

69. Intermittent explosive disorder is characterized by:
   A. Premeditated aggression for gain
   B. Recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts grossly out of proportion to provocation
   C. Persistent deceitfulness and theft as a lifestyle

 D. Fire-setting for pleasure only
       Answer: B. Recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts grossly out of proportion to
provocation
   Rationale: Intermittent explosive disorder involves impulsive aggressive outbursts that are
disproportionate to the provocation.

70. Kleptomania involves:
   A. Theft motivated by monetary need or revenge
   B. Recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal unneeded objects
   C. Destruction of property through anger

 D. Sexual arousal from stealing
       Answer: B. Recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal unneeded objects
   Rationale: Kleptomania is defined by recurrent impulse-driven theft of objects not needed for
personal use or monetary value.

71. Pyromania is best described as:
   A. Fire-setting for insurance fraud
   B. Deliberate fire-setting on more than one occasion associated with tension before the act

and fascination with fire
   C. Arson due to conduct disorder only

 D. Fire-setting exclusively during psychosis
       Answer: B. Deliberate fire-setting on more than one occasion associated with tension
before the act and fascination with fire
   Rationale: Pyromania involves repeated deliberate fire-setting accompanied by tension
before the act and fascination or relief related to fire.

72. Which personality disorder cluster is characterized as odd or eccentric?
   A. Cluster A
   B. Cluster B
   C. Cluster C

 D. Mixed cluster only
       Answer: A. Cluster A
   Rationale: Cluster A personality disorders are classified as odd or eccentric and include
paranoid, schizoid, and schizotypal personality disorders.

73. A pervasive distrust and suspicion that others are exploiting or deceiving the person is most
characteristic of:

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Paranoid personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Paranoid personality disorder is defined by pervasive distrust and suspiciousness
toward others.

74. A person who shows detachment from social relationships and restricted emotional
expression most likely has:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizoid personality disorder involves social detachment and restricted emotional
expression.

75. Which feature is most characteristic of antisocial personality disorder?
   A. Fear of criticism
   B. Instability in relationships plus frantic efforts to avoid abandonment
   C. Disregard for and violation of the rights of others since age 15, with evidence of conduct

problems

 D. Perfectionism and orderliness
       Answer: C. Disregard for and violation of the rights of others since age 15, with evidence
of conduct problems
   Rationale: Antisocial personality disorder requires a longstanding pattern of violating others'
rights beginning with conduct-related problems.

76. Borderline personality disorder is strongly associated with:
   A. Grandiose self-importance only
   B. Instability in affect, identity, and relationships, with impulsivity
   C. Social detachment and indifference

 D. Compulsive stealing
       Answer: B. Instability in affect, identity, and relationships, with impulsivity
   Rationale: Borderline personality disorder is marked by instability in mood, self-image,
relationships, and impulsive behavior.

77. Excessive emotionality and attention seeking best describe:
   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Schizotypal personality disorder
   C. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: A. Histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Histrionic personality disorder is characterized by excessive emotionality and a
strong need for attention.

78. A pervasive pattern of grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy is most
consistent with:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Narcissistic personality disorder centers on grandiosity, admiration seeking,
entitlement, and lack of empathy.

79. Avoidant personality disorder is distinguished by:
   A. Disregard for rules and others
   B. Social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to negative evaluation
   C. Need to be the center of attention

 D. Detachment without desire for relationships
       Answer: B. Social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to negative
evaluation
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder involves social inhibition and intense sensitivity to
criticism due to feelings of inadequacy.

80. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder is most associated with:
   A. Intrusive obsessions and compulsions
   B. Perfectionism, rigidity, and control at the expense of flexibility
   C. Dramatic emotionality

 D. Chronic impulsive aggression
       Answer: B. Perfectionism, rigidity, and control at the expense of flexibility
   Rationale: Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder is characterized by maladaptive
perfectionism, rigidity, and overcontrol.

81. Schizotypal personality disorder includes:
   A. Recurrent violation of others' rights
   B. Acute manic episodes
   C. Social deficits with cognitive or perceptual distortions and eccentric behavior

 D. Complete emotional indifference only
       Answer: C. Social deficits with cognitive or perceptual distortions and eccentric behavior
   Rationale: Schizotypal personality disorder involves interpersonal deficits together with
cognitive or perceptual distortions and eccentric behavior.

82. A child repeatedly violates rules, lies, steals, and shows aggression toward peers and
animals. The diagnosis most consistent is:

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Social anxiety disorder

 D. DMDD
       Answer: B. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Conduct disorder involves repeated serious violations of rules and the rights of
others, including aggression, deceitfulness, and theft.

83. Oppositional defiant disorder is best characterized by:
   A. Severe violations of others' rights
   B. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, or vindictiveness
   C. Psychotic symptoms with irritability

 D. Panic and avoidance
       Answer: B. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, or
vindictiveness
   Rationale: Oppositional defiant disorder centers on irritable mood, defiance, and
vindictiveness rather than serious rights violations.

84. Which feature most helps distinguish delirium from major neurocognitive disorder?
   A. Delirium always includes memory loss only
   B. Delirium has an acute onset and fluctuating course with disturbances in attention and

awareness
   C. Delirium begins gradually over years

 D. Delirium requires a prior psychiatric history
       Answer: B. Delirium has an acute onset and fluctuating course with disturbances in
attention and awareness
   Rationale: Delirium is marked by an acute and fluctuating disturbance in attention and
awareness.

85. Major neurocognitive disorder due to Alzheimer's disease typically shows:
   A. Abrupt stepwise decline after strokes
   B. Progressive decline with prominent memory impairment
   C. Early onset psychopathy only

 D. Substance intoxication only
       Answer: B. Progressive decline with prominent memory impairment
   Rationale: Alzheimer's disease typically presents with gradual progressive decline, especially
in memory early in the course.

86. Vascular neurocognitive disorder is most associated with:
   A. Only auditory hallucinations
   B. Stepwise decline linked to cerebrovascular disease
   C. Pure amnesia after trauma

 D. Cataplexy
       Answer: B. Stepwise decline linked to cerebrovascular disease
   Rationale: Vascular neurocognitive disorder commonly follows cerebrovascular disease and
may show a stepwise decline.

87. Which condition is best described as confusion, impaired attention, and fluctuating
consciousness due to a medical or substance-related cause?

   A. Delirium
   B. Dissociative amnesia
   C. Schizoaffective disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: A. Delirium
   Rationale: Delirium is defined by confusion, impaired attention, and fluctuating awareness
due to a medical condition or substance-related cause.

88. Which pioneer is most closely associated with client-centered therapy?
   A. Carl Rogers
   B. B. F. Skinner
   C. Emil Kraepelin

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: A. Carl Rogers
   Rationale: Carl Rogers developed client-centered therapy, emphasizing empathy,
genuineness, and unconditional positive regard.

89. Aaron Beck is most closely associated with:
   A. Classical conditioning
   B. Cognitive therapy emphasizing maladaptive thinking patterns
   C. Humanistic nondirectiveness

 D. Psychosexual stages
       Answer: B. Cognitive therapy emphasizing maladaptive thinking patterns
   Rationale: Aaron Beck is associated with cognitive therapy and the role of maladaptive
thoughts in emotional disorders.
90. B. F. Skinner is most closely associated with:
   A. Operant conditioning
   B. Cognitive distortions
   C. Dream analysis

 D. Attachment theory
       Answer: A. Operant conditioning
   Rationale: B. F. Skinner is known for operant conditioning and the role of reinforcement in
shaping behavior.

91. Emil Kraepelin is historically important because he:
   A. Developed person-centered therapy
   B. Advanced descriptive classification of severe mental disorders
   C. Originated exposure therapy

 D. Created the MMPI
       Answer: B. Advanced descriptive classification of severe mental disorders
   Rationale: Kraepelin made major contributions to psychiatric classification by distinguishing
severe mental disorders based on symptoms and course.

92. A practitioner's personal distress is beginning to impair professional judgment and
performance. The most ethical course is to:

   A. Continue working and conceal the difficulty
   B. Seek consultation or assistance and determine whether duties should be limited,
suspended, or terminated
   C. Transfer all confidential files to friends

 D. Diagnose oneself and continue practicing unchanged
       Answer: B. Seek consultation or assistance and determine whether duties should be
limited, suspended, or terminated
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires addressing personal problems that impair competence by
seeking help and adjusting duties as needed to protect clients.

93. Which action best reflects ethical delegation of work?
   A. Assigning complex assessment tasks to untrained staff without oversight
   B. Delegating only tasks a person can perform competently with appropriate supervision
   C. Allowing family members to administer tests informally

 D. Permitting a supervisee to exceed legal limits if the client consents
       Answer: B. Delegating only tasks a person can perform competently with appropriate
supervision
   Rationale: Ethical delegation requires assigning only tasks that the person can perform
competently, either independently or with proper supervision.

94. Which is the best response when an ethics code conflicts with governing law and the conflict
cannot be resolved?

   A. Ignore both and follow personal values
   B. Follow the law while first attempting to resolve the conflict in a manner consistent with
ethics

   C. Publicly disclose all case records

 D. Resign immediately in every case
       Answer: B. Follow the law while first attempting to resolve the conflict in a manner
consistent with ethics
   Rationale: When ethical conflict with law cannot be resolved, the practitioner should first
attempt resolution and then adhere to governing law.

95. A psychometrician is asked by a school to email raw test protocols directly to classroom
teachers. The best response is:

   A. Send immediately because teachers are stakeholders
   B. Refuse because raw test data should not be released to unauthorized persons
   C. Send only if the teachers promise confidentiality

 D. Upload publicly for transparency
       Answer: B. Refuse because raw test data should not be released to unauthorized persons
   Rationale: Raw test data and protocols should not be released to unauthorized persons
because of confidentiality and test security concerns.

96. During teleassessment, which issue should be discussed with the client beforehand?
   A. Only the practitioner's preferred internet provider
   B. The implications of poor internet connectivity on test performance, especially for timed

tests
   C. That scores are always interchangeable with in-person testing

 D. That confidentiality no longer applies online
       Answer: B. The implications of poor internet connectivity on test performance, especially
for timed tests
   Rationale: Teleassessment requires discussion of technological limitations, including how
unstable connectivity may affect performance validity, especially on timed tests.

97. A clinician is considering a diagnosis in a culturally diverse client. Which practice is most
appropriate?

   A. Assume all unusual beliefs are delusions
   B. Ignore cultural background to reduce bias
   C. Evaluate symptoms within the client's cultural context and sources of distress

 D. Diagnose only by checklist regardless of context
       Answer: C. Evaluate symptoms within the client's cultural context and sources of distress
   Rationale: Culturally informed assessment helps distinguish psychopathology from culturally
normative experience and improves diagnostic accuracy.

98. A patient expresses suicidal ideation with intent and access to means. The best immediate
clinical priority is:

   A. Explore childhood dreams
   B. Delay action until formal testing is complete
   C. Conduct urgent safety assessment and intervention

 D. Focus first on personality diagnosis
       Answer: C. Conduct urgent safety assessment and intervention
   Rationale: Imminent suicide risk requires immediate safety-focused assessment and
intervention to protect the patient.

99. Which statement best reflects authentic board-style differential diagnosis reasoning?
   A. The first apparent diagnosis is usually sufficient
   B. Symptoms should be interpreted without considering medical or substance causes
   C. Similar symptoms can arise from multiple disorders, so rule-outs and context matter

 D. Diagnosis is based primarily on one symptom
       Answer: C. Similar symptoms can arise from multiple disorders, so rule-outs and context
matter
   Rationale: Differential diagnosis requires recognizing that similar symptoms may arise from
different disorders, substances, medical conditions, or contextual factors.

100. In Philippine professional practice, which statement is most accurate?
    A. Any psychology graduate may independently practice psychometrics
    B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally practice

within the boundaries prescribed by law
    C. Supervision is optional when experience is high

 D. Confidentiality may be waived for convenience
        Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally
practice within the boundaries prescribed by law
    Rationale: Philippine law requires that only licensed and registered psychologists and
psychometricians practice, and only within the legal scope of their profession.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 6
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 6

1. Which statement best captures the contemporary understanding of abnormal behavior?
  A. Abnormal behavior is any behavior that violates social norms
  B. Abnormal behavior is defined exclusively by biological pathology
  C. Abnormal behavior is best understood through interacting biological, psychological, and

social factors

 D. Abnormal behavior is any unusual behavior regardless of distress or impairment
       Answer: C. Abnormal behavior is best understood through interacting biological,
psychological, and social factors
  Rationale: Contemporary abnormal psychology uses an integrative model that explains
abnormal behavior through the interaction of biological, psychological, and social influences
rather than a single-cause explanation.

2. A clinician avoids making an immediate diagnosis after a single interview because symptoms
may change as more history becomes available. This most directly reflects the principle that:

  A. diagnosis should always be delayed for several months
  B. clinical judgment and differential diagnosis are iterative processes
  C. only laboratory tests can establish a valid diagnosis

 D. patients are unreliable historians in most cases
       Answer: B. clinical judgment and differential diagnosis are iterative processes
  Rationale: Diagnostic formulation often develops over time as additional interview data,
collateral information, history, and follow-up observations clarify the case.

3. A client presents with psychotic symptoms. Before concluding a primary psychotic disorder,
the most appropriate first diagnostic consideration is:

  A. personality disorder
  B. malingering or factitious presentation, substance effects, and medical causes
  C. specific learning disorder

 D. adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. malingering or factitious presentation, substance effects, and medical causes
  Rationale: A sound differential diagnosis first rules out feigned symptoms, substance-induced
causes, and medical etiologies before assigning a primary psychotic disorder.

4. A person feigns hallucinations to avoid criminal liability. The most accurate classification is:
  A. factitious disorder
  B. illness anxiety disorder
  C. malingering

 D. somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: C. malingering
  Rationale: Malingering involves the intentional production or exaggeration of symptoms for a
clear external gain, such as avoiding legal consequences.
5. A patient intentionally produces symptoms to assume the sick role despite no obvious
external reward. This presentation is most consistent with:

  A. factitious disorder
  B. conversion disorder
  C. malingering

 D. panic disorder
       Answer: A. factitious disorder
  Rationale: Factitious disorder involves intentional falsification or production of symptoms
without obvious external incentives, often to assume the role of a patient.

6. In differential diagnosis, which is the strongest reason substance-induced conditions must be
ruled out early?

  A. They are rare but dangerous
  B. They commonly mimic many psychiatric presentations
  C. They are easy to treat with psychotherapy alone

 D. They only occur in adolescents
       Answer: B. They commonly mimic many psychiatric presentations
  Rationale: Substance use and withdrawal can produce symptoms resembling depression,
anxiety, psychosis, sleep disturbance, and cognitive problems, making them frequent sources of
diagnostic error.

7. Which feature most strongly suggests delirium rather than major neurocognitive disorder?
  A. gradual progression
  B. stable level of consciousness
  C. fluctuating attention and awareness

 D. lifelong cognitive limitations
       Answer: C. fluctuating attention and awareness
  Rationale: Delirium is defined by an acute and fluctuating disturbance in attention and
awareness, which distinguishes it from the more stable and progressive pattern seen in major
neurocognitive disorder.

8. A child with persistent deficits in social communication and restricted, repetitive behavior
patterns is most likely to meet criteria for:

  A. social anxiety disorder
  B. autism spectrum disorder
  C. selective mutism

 D. reactive attachment disorder
       Answer: B. autism spectrum disorder
  Rationale: Autism spectrum disorder is characterized by persistent deficits in social
communication together with restricted, repetitive patterns of behavior or interests.

9. Which feature best distinguishes intellectual disability from specific learning disorder?
  A. presence of academic weakness
  B. deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning
  C. onset before adulthood

 D. poor school performance
       Answer: B. deficits in intellectual and adaptive functioning
  Rationale: Intellectual disability requires deficits in both intellectual functioning and adaptive
functioning, whereas specific learning disorder involves more circumscribed academic skill
deficits.

10. A child is often distracted, interrupts others, and cannot remain seated across home and
school settings for several months. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. oppositional defiant disorder
   B. conduct disorder
   C. attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder

 D. disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: C. attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   Rationale: ADHD is marked by persistent inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity occurring
across multiple settings and causing functional impairment.

11. Which finding most strongly supports specific learning disorder rather than intellectual
disability?

   A. broad impairment across reasoning, self-care, and communication
   B. isolated persistent difficulty in reading despite adequate opportunity to learn
   C. global developmental delay since infancy

 D. severe deficits in adaptive functioning across settings
       Answer: B. isolated persistent difficulty in reading despite adequate opportunity to learn
   Rationale: Specific learning disorder involves persistent difficulty in a particular academic
area despite adequate instruction and opportunity, without the global deficits seen in intellectual
disability.

12. A 7-year-old speaks normally at home but consistently fails to speak in school despite
understanding language and wanting to interact. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. autism spectrum disorder
   B. selective mutism
   C. communication disorder due to intellectual disability

 D. social pragmatic communication disorder
       Answer: B. selective mutism
   Rationale: Selective mutism is characterized by consistent failure to speak in specific social
settings despite normal speech in other settings.

13. Which symptom is classified as a positive symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. flat affect
   B. avolition
   C. delusions

 D. alogia
       Answer: C. delusions
   Rationale: Positive symptoms are excesses or distortions of normal functioning, and
delusions are a classic example of this category.

14. A client has delusions, hallucinations, disorganized speech, and marked impairment lasting
3 months. The duration most strongly suggests:

   A. brief psychotic disorder
   B. schizophreniform disorder
   C. schizophrenia

 D. delusional disorder
       Answer: B. schizophreniform disorder
   Rationale: Schizophreniform disorder includes schizophrenia-like symptoms lasting more than
1 month but less than 6 months.

15. A person has a fixed false belief of being poisoned, with otherwise relatively preserved
functioning and no prominent hallucinations. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. schizophrenia
   B. schizoaffective disorder
   C. delusional disorder

 D. obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: C. delusional disorder
   Rationale: Delusional disorder involves one or more persistent delusions with relatively
preserved functioning and without the full symptom picture of schizophrenia.

16. Which condition requires a major mood episode to be present for the majority of the illness,
together with psychotic symptoms and at least some period of psychosis without mood
symptoms?

   A. bipolar II disorder
   B. schizoaffective disorder
   C. delusional disorder

 D. cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. schizoaffective disorder
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both a major mood episode for most of the illness
and at least a period of psychosis occurring independently of mood symptoms.

17. A manic episode is best characterized by:
   A. elevated mood for at least 2 days without impairment
   B. persistent low mood with occasional irritability
   C. abnormally elevated, expansive, or irritable mood with increased activity or energy and

marked impairment

 D. psychosis occurring only during intoxication
       Answer: C. abnormally elevated, expansive, or irritable mood with increased activity or
energy and marked impairment
   Rationale: A manic episode involves abnormally elevated, expansive, or irritable mood with
increased energy or activity and significant impairment, hospitalization, or psychotic features.
18. Which diagnosis requires at least one lifetime manic episode?
   A. bipolar I disorder
   B. bipolar II disorder
   C. cyclothymic disorder

 D. persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: A. bipolar I disorder
