   Rationale: The defining diagnostic requirement for bipolar I disorder is the occurrence of at
least one manic episode.

19. A client reports repeated depressive episodes and at least one hypomanic episode, but no
history of mania. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. bipolar I disorder
   B. bipolar II disorder
   C. cyclothymic disorder

 D. disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: B. bipolar II disorder
   Rationale: Bipolar II disorder requires at least one hypomanic episode and at least one major
depressive episode, with no full manic episode.

20. A 10-year-old has severe recurrent temper outbursts and persistently irritable mood
between outbursts for more than a year. The diagnosis most consistent with this is:

   A. oppositional defiant disorder
   B. disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   C. intermittent explosive disorder

 D. bipolar I disorder
       Answer: B. disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   Rationale: DMDD is characterized by severe recurrent temper outbursts with persistent
irritability between episodes in children.

21. Which symptom is more characteristic of major depressive disorder than normal grief alone?
   A. sadness after loss
   B. yearning for the deceased
   C. pervasive worthlessness and suicidal ideation unrelated to reunion fantasies

 D. transient waves of emotion triggered by reminders
       Answer: C. pervasive worthlessness and suicidal ideation unrelated to reunion fantasies
   Rationale: Severe worthlessness and suicidal thinking grounded in self-devaluation are more
indicative of major depressive disorder than normal grief.

22. Persistent depressive disorder is best described as:
   A. mild sadness after stress that resolves within 2 weeks
   B. chronic depressed mood lasting at least 2 years in adults
   C. alternating mania and depression for at least 1 year
   D. depression caused solely by bereavement
  Answer: B. chronic depressed mood lasting at least 2 years in adults

   Rationale: Persistent depressive disorder is a chronic depressive condition defined by
depressed mood for most of the day, more days than not, for at least 2 years in adults.

23. Which anxiety disorder is defined by excessive anxiety and worry occurring more days than
not about multiple events or activities?

   A. panic disorder
   B. generalized anxiety disorder
   C. specific phobia

 D. separation anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. generalized anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Generalized anxiety disorder is defined by excessive and difficult-to-control worry
about multiple areas of life occurring more days than not.

24. The defining feature of panic disorder is:
   A. constant worry about health
   B. recurrent unexpected panic attacks with persistent concern or maladaptive behavioral

change
   C. fear limited to social situations

 D. trauma exposure with flashbacks
       Answer: B. recurrent unexpected panic attacks with persistent concern or maladaptive
behavioral change
   Rationale: Panic disorder involves recurrent unexpected panic attacks followed by ongoing
concern or behavioral change related to the attacks.

25. A college student has intense fear only when speaking in front of groups because of
possible embarrassment and negative evaluation. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. agoraphobia
   B. social anxiety disorder
   C. generalized anxiety disorder

 D. panic disorder
       Answer: B. social anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Social anxiety disorder is characterized by marked fear of situations involving
possible scrutiny or negative evaluation by others.

26. A person avoids bridges, buses, and crowded malls because escape might be difficult if
panic-like symptoms occur. This pattern is most consistent with:

   A. agoraphobia
   B. specific phobia
   C. separation anxiety disorder

 D. body dysmorphic disorder
       Answer: A. agoraphobia
   Rationale: Agoraphobia involves fear and avoidance of situations where escape may be
difficult or help may not be available if panic-like symptoms develop.
27. The most distinguishing feature of obsessive-compulsive disorder is:
   A. intrusive obsessions and/or compulsions aimed at reducing distress
   B. pervasive fear of being judged in public
   C. fixed somatic delusions

 D. fluctuating disorientation
       Answer: A. intrusive obsessions and/or compulsions aimed at reducing distress
   Rationale: OCD is defined by intrusive obsessions and/or compulsive acts performed to
reduce distress or prevent feared outcomes.

28. A client is preoccupied with a slight facial flaw and repeatedly checks mirrors for hours daily.
The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. narcissistic personality disorder
   B. body dysmorphic disorder
   C. illness anxiety disorder

 D. delusional disorder, grandiose type
       Answer: B. body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Body dysmorphic disorder involves preoccupation with perceived defects in
appearance along with repetitive behaviors such as mirror checking.

29. Difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value, leading to clutter and
impairment, is most characteristic of:

   A. obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   B. hoarding disorder
   C. generalized anxiety disorder

 D. schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. hoarding disorder
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder is defined by persistent difficulty discarding possessions
regardless of value, resulting in clutter and significant impairment.

30. Hair pulling resulting in noticeable hair loss with repeated attempts to stop is most consistent
with:

   A. excoriation disorder
   B. trichotillomania
   C. stereotypic movement disorder

 D. body dysmorphic disorder
       Answer: B. trichotillomania
   Rationale: Trichotillomania is characterized by recurrent hair pulling resulting in hair loss and
repeated unsuccessful attempts to stop.

31. Which diagnosis requires exposure to a traumatic event followed by intrusion, avoidance,
negative mood/cognitions, and arousal symptoms lasting more than 1 month?

   A. adjustment disorder
   B. panic disorder
   C. posttraumatic stress disorder

 D. acute stress disorder
       Answer: C. posttraumatic stress disorder
   Rationale: PTSD requires exposure to trauma and the presence of intrusion, avoidance,
negative alterations in cognition or mood, and arousal symptoms lasting longer than 1 month.

32. Symptoms following trauma that meet full posttraumatic stress criteria but last only 10 days
are most consistent with:

   A. acute stress disorder
   B. posttraumatic stress disorder
   C. generalized anxiety disorder

 D. dissociative amnesia
       Answer: A. acute stress disorder
   Rationale: Acute stress disorder involves trauma-related symptoms similar to PTSD but with a
shorter duration of 3 days to 1 month.

33. Emotional or behavioral symptoms in response to an identifiable stressor, out of proportion
to its severity but not meeting criteria for another disorder, most strongly suggest:

   A. major depressive disorder
   B. adjustment disorder
   C. persistent depressive disorder

 D. acute stress disorder
       Answer: B. adjustment disorder
   Rationale: Adjustment disorder is diagnosed when maladaptive emotional or behavioral
symptoms arise in response to a stressor but do not meet criteria for a more specific disorder.

34. A patient has multiple distressing physical symptoms plus excessive thoughts, feelings, or
behaviors related to these symptoms. The diagnosis most consistent with this is:

   A. illness anxiety disorder
   B. somatic symptom disorder
   C. factitious disorder

 D. conversion disorder
       Answer: B. somatic symptom disorder
   Rationale: Somatic symptom disorder involves one or more distressing somatic symptoms
together with disproportionate concern, anxiety, or maladaptive behaviors related to them.

35. Preoccupation with having a serious illness despite minimal or no somatic symptoms is most
characteristic of:

   A. illness anxiety disorder
   B. panic disorder
   C. somatic symptom disorder

 D. delusional disorder
       Answer: A. illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder centers on excessive fear of having or acquiring a serious
illness despite minimal or absent somatic symptoms.

36. Sudden paralysis after conflict, inconsistent with neurological disease and not intentionally
produced, most strongly suggests:

   A. factitious disorder
   B. malingering
   C. conversion disorder

 D. major neurocognitive disorder
       Answer: C. conversion disorder
   Rationale: Conversion disorder involves neurological-type symptoms incompatible with
recognized medical conditions and not intentionally produced.

37. Which condition involves falsification of illness or injury in self or another in the absence of
obvious external incentives?

   A. illness anxiety disorder
   B. factitious disorder
   C. panic disorder

 D. somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. factitious disorder
   Rationale: Factitious disorder involves deliberate falsification or induction of illness without
clear external rewards.

38. In depersonalization/derealization disorder, reality testing is typically:
   A. grossly impaired
   B. absent during episodes
   C. generally intact

 D. replaced by delusional beliefs
       Answer: C. generally intact
   Rationale: Individuals with depersonalization/derealization disorder usually recognize that
their altered experiences are subjective, so reality testing remains intact.

39. In dissociative amnesia, the memory disturbance most often involves:
   A. inability to form new memories due to dementia
   B. forgetting only trivial daily events
   C. inability to recall important autobiographical information, often traumatic or stressful

 D. progressive memory loss from neurodegeneration
       Answer: C. inability to recall important autobiographical information, often traumatic or
stressful
   Rationale: Dissociative amnesia typically involves inability to remember important
autobiographical material, especially related to trauma or severe stress.

40. Which feature best differentiates dissociative identity disorder from psychotic disorders?
   A. presence of trauma history
   B. disruption of identity with distinct personality states and amnestic gaps
   C. social withdrawal

 D. unusual perceptual experiences only
       Answer: B. disruption of identity with distinct personality states and amnestic gaps
   Rationale: Dissociative identity disorder is defined by identity disruption involving distinct
personality states together with recurrent memory gaps.

41. Which pattern best fits anorexia nervosa?
   A. recurrent binges followed by laxative misuse at normal weight
   B. significantly low body weight with intense fear of gaining weight and body image

disturbance
   C. obesity with loss of control eating

 D. food restriction due solely to poverty
       Answer: B. significantly low body weight with intense fear of gaining weight and body
image disturbance
   Rationale: Anorexia nervosa is characterized by significantly low body weight, intense fear of
weight gain, and disturbance in body image or self-evaluation.

42. Recurrent binge eating followed by compensatory behaviors such as vomiting most strongly
indicates:

   A. anorexia nervosa
   B. bulimia nervosa
   C. binge-eating disorder

 D. avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: B. bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa involves recurrent binge eating episodes followed by
compensatory behaviors such as vomiting, laxative misuse, fasting, or excessive exercise.

43. Recurrent binge eating without regular inappropriate compensatory behaviors is most
consistent with:

   A. bulimia nervosa
   B. binge-eating disorder
   C. anorexia nervosa

 D. pica
       Answer: B. binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder is defined by recurrent binge eating episodes without the
regular compensatory behaviors seen in bulimia nervosa.

44. Which sleep-wake disorder is characterized by dissatisfaction with sleep quantity or quality
associated with difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep?

   A. hypersomnolence disorder
   B. insomnia disorder
   C. narcolepsy
   D. nightmare disorder
  Answer: B. insomnia disorder

   Rationale: Insomnia disorder involves persistent dissatisfaction with sleep quantity or quality
due to difficulty falling asleep, staying asleep, or waking too early.

45. Excessive sleepiness despite a main sleep period lasting at least 7 hours is most
characteristic of:

   A. insomnia disorder
   B. hypersomnolence disorder
   C. obstructive sleep apnea only

 D. circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder only
       Answer: B. hypersomnolence disorder
   Rationale: Hypersomnolence disorder is marked by excessive sleepiness despite apparently
adequate main sleep duration.

46. Erectile disorder is categorized under:
   A. paraphilic disorders
   B. sexual dysfunctions
   C. gender dysphoria

 D. impulse-control disorders
       Answer: B. sexual dysfunctions
   Rationale: Erectile disorder is classified among sexual dysfunctions because it involves
impaired sexual response rather than atypical sexual preference or gender incongruence.

47. Which statement best reflects the concept of gender dysphoria?
   A. It is identical to sexual dysfunction
   B. It refers to distress associated with incongruence between experienced gender and

assigned sex
   C. It is classified as a paraphilic disorder

 D. It always requires surgical treatment
       Answer: B. It refers to distress associated with incongruence between experienced gender
and assigned sex
   Rationale: Gender dysphoria refers to clinically significant distress associated with
incongruence between experienced gender and assigned sex.

48. Recurrent behavioral outbursts representing failure to control aggressive impulses that are
grossly out of proportion to provocation is most characteristic of:

   A. conduct disorder
   B. oppositional defiant disorder
   C. intermittent explosive disorder

 D. antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: C. intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: Intermittent explosive disorder involves recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts
that are disproportionate to the provocation.
49. Which feature most strongly distinguishes conduct disorder from oppositional defiant
disorder?

   A. irritability
   B. argumentativeness
   C. violation of major rights of others or age-appropriate societal norms

 D. temper outbursts only
       Answer: C. violation of major rights of others or age-appropriate societal norms
   Rationale: Conduct disorder is distinguished by more severe behaviors involving aggression,
deceit, destruction, theft, or serious rule violations.

50. Repeated unlawful behavior since age 15, deceitfulness, impulsivity, aggression, and lack of
remorse in an adult most strongly suggest:

   A. narcissistic personality disorder
   B. antisocial personality disorder
   C. borderline personality disorder

 D. conduct disorder
       Answer: B. antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Antisocial personality disorder requires a pervasive pattern of disregard for and
violation of the rights of others since age 15, including deceitfulness, impulsivity, aggression,
and lack of remorse.

51. Instability in relationships, self-image, and affect, with marked impulsivity and recurrent
self-harm, most strongly indicates:

   A. histrionic personality disorder
   B. borderline personality disorder
   C. dependent personality disorder

 D. cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Borderline personality disorder is characterized by instability in relationships,
self-image, and affect, along with impulsivity and recurrent self-harming behavior.

52. Excessive emotionality and attention-seeking behavior is most characteristic of:
   A. schizotypal personality disorder
   B. obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. histrionic personality disorder

 D. paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: C. histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Histrionic personality disorder is defined by pervasive excessive emotionality and
attention-seeking behavior.

53. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy are core features of:
   A. narcissistic personality disorder
   B. avoidant personality disorder
   C. schizoid personality disorder
 D. dependent personality disorder
       Answer: A. narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Narcissistic personality disorder is marked by grandiosity, a strong need for
admiration, and limited empathy for others.

54. Social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to criticism are most
characteristic of:

   A. schizoid personality disorder
   B. avoidant personality disorder
   C. dependent personality disorder

 D. social anxiety disorder only
       Answer: B. avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder is characterized by social inhibition, feelings of
inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to negative evaluation.

55. Which feature best characterizes obsessive-compulsive personality disorder?
   A. intrusive obsessions with ritual neutralization
   B. perfectionism and rigid control at the expense of flexibility and efficiency
   C. dramatic emotional displays and seductiveness

 D. identity disturbance and self-harm
       Answer: B. perfectionism and rigid control at the expense of flexibility and efficiency
   Rationale: Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder involves rigid perfectionism,
orderliness, and control that interfere with flexibility and task completion.

56. Persistent suspiciousness and tendency to interpret others' motives as malevolent is most
typical of:

   A. paranoid personality disorder
   B. schizoid personality disorder
   C. avoidant personality disorder

 D. dependent personality disorder
       Answer: A. paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Paranoid personality disorder is defined by pervasive distrust and suspiciousness
such that others' motives are interpreted as malevolent.

57. Which substance category is most associated with intoxication marked by disinhibition,
slurred speech, and impaired coordination?

   A. hallucinogens
   B. depressants
   C. stimulants

 D. cannabis only
       Answer: B. depressants
   Rationale: Depressant intoxication, especially with alcohol or sedative-hypnotics, commonly
produces disinhibition, slurred speech, and impaired coordination.
58. Tolerance, withdrawal, craving, and continued use despite harm are central indicators of:
   A. substance use disorder
   B. substance intoxication only
   C. malingering

 D. factitious disorder
       Answer: A. substance use disorder
   Rationale: These are core features of substance use disorder because they reflect impaired
control, physiological adaptation, and persistence despite negative consequences.

59. Which is a behavioral addiction recognized in DSM classification?
   A. compulsive buying disorder
   B. internet use disorder
   C. gambling disorder

 D. workaholism disorder
       Answer: C. gambling disorder
   Rationale: Gambling disorder is the recognized behavioral addiction formally included in DSM
classification.

60. Which statement about comorbidity is most accurate?
   A. It means symptoms are fabricated
   B. It refers to the co-occurrence of two or more disorders in the same individual
   C. It only occurs in personality disorders

 D. It invalidates all diagnoses made
       Answer: B. It refers to the co-occurrence of two or more disorders in the same individual
   Rationale: Comorbidity refers to the presence of multiple disorders in the same person at the
same time or across the same period.

61. A client develops depressed mood after heavy stimulant withdrawal. The best immediate
diagnostic consideration is:

   A. persistent depressive disorder
   B. substance/medication-induced depressive disorder
   C. cyclothymic disorder

 D. adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. substance/medication-induced depressive disorder
   Rationale: When depressive symptoms develop in close temporal relation to stimulant
withdrawal, a substance-induced depressive disorder must be considered first.

62. Which symptom is especially associated with opioid withdrawal?
   A. pinpoint pupils and sedation
   B. elevated mood and grandiosity
   C. lacrimation, rhinorrhea, aches, and craving

 D. vivid visual hallucinations only
       Answer: C. lacrimation, rhinorrhea, aches, and craving
   Rationale: Opioid withdrawal commonly produces tearing, runny nose, muscle aches, and
intense craving.

63. Which of the following is a key principle in assessment?
   A. administer every available test
   B. rely on a single method for efficiency
   C. integrate interview, observation, history, and when indicated, testing

 D. avoid collateral information to protect rapport
       Answer: C. integrate interview, observation, history, and when indicated, testing
   Rationale: Good assessment is multimethod and integrates clinical interview, observation,
background history, and appropriate testing to improve accuracy.

64. The primary purpose of differential diagnosis is to:
   A. assign the rarest disorder possible
   B. distinguish among disorders with overlapping features
   C. avoid using DSM terminology

 D. replace clinical judgment with algorithms
       Answer: B. distinguish among disorders with overlapping features
   Rationale: Differential diagnosis helps identify which disorder best accounts for the symptoms
when several possible conditions share similar features.

65. Which condition most commonly involves a chronic psychotic process with functional decline
and negative symptoms?

   A. delusional disorder
   B. schizophrenia
   C. obsessive-compulsive disorder

 D. illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. schizophrenia
   Rationale: Schizophrenia commonly includes chronic psychosis, functional deterioration, and
negative symptoms such as flat affect and avolition.

66. A person hears voices only during severe depressive episodes and has no psychosis
outside mood episodes. The diagnosis is most likely:

   A. schizoaffective disorder
   B. major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   C. schizophrenia

 D. delusional disorder
       Answer: B. major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   Rationale: When psychotic symptoms occur exclusively during depressive episodes, the
correct diagnosis is major depressive disorder with psychotic features.

67. Which statement about suicide risk is most accurate?
   A. Asking about suicide increases suicidal behavior
   B. Previous attempts are among the strongest predictors of future attempts
   C. Suicide risk is unrelated to mood disorders

 D. Only psychotic patients die by suicide
       Answer: B. Previous attempts are among the strongest predictors of future attempts
   Rationale: A history of prior suicide attempts is one of the strongest known predictors of later
suicidal behavior.

68. A client reports fear of heart attack during abrupt surges of intense terror, palpitations,
shortness of breath, and dizziness peaking within minutes. This episode is best described as:

   A. obsession
   B. panic attack
   C. dissociative fugue

 D. flashback
       Answer: B. panic attack
   Rationale: A panic attack is an abrupt surge of intense fear or discomfort accompanied by
physical symptoms that peak within minutes.

69. Which is most consistent with agoraphobia rather than social anxiety disorder?
   A. fear of negative evaluation during conversations
   B. fear of embarrassment in eating publicly
   C. fear of being unable to escape or get help in certain places

 D. fear limited to being criticized by authority figures
       Answer: C. fear of being unable to escape or get help in certain places
   Rationale: Agoraphobia is specifically centered on situations where escape may be difficult or
help unavailable if panic-like symptoms occur.

70. A client with schizophrenia shows diminished emotional expression and poverty of speech.
These are:

   A. catatonic symptoms
   B. positive symptoms
   C. negative symptoms

 D. manic symptoms
       Answer: C. negative symptoms
   Rationale: Diminished emotional expression and poverty of speech are negative symptoms
because they reflect reductions in normal emotional and verbal functioning.

71. Which characteristic most strongly supports delusional disorder over schizophrenia?
   A. bizarre delusions with marked disorganization
   B. prominent negative symptoms
   C. relatively preserved functioning apart from the delusional belief

 D. hallucinations occurring across many sensory modalities
       Answer: C. relatively preserved functioning apart from the delusional belief
   Rationale: Delusional disorder typically involves less global impairment, with functioning often
relatively preserved except in areas directly affected by the delusion.
72. Which statement best distinguishes obsession from delusion?
   A. Obsessions are always pleasurable thoughts
   B. Obsessions are experienced as intrusive and usually recognized as products of one's own

mind
   C. Delusions are repetitive behaviors

 D. Delusions occur only in OCD
       Answer: B. Obsessions are experienced as intrusive and usually recognized as products
of one's own mind
   Rationale: Obsessions are intrusive, unwanted thoughts or impulses that are usually
recognized as originating from one's own mind, unlike delusions, which are fixed false beliefs.

73. Which finding best supports illness anxiety disorder rather than somatic symptom disorder?
   A. numerous distressing physical symptoms
   B. excessive health anxiety despite minimal somatic symptoms
   C. neurological deficits after conflict

 D. deliberate falsification of illness
       Answer: B. excessive health anxiety despite minimal somatic symptoms
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder is marked by intense fear of serious illness despite having
few or no significant physical symptoms.

74. A client reports recurrent episodes of binge eating, intense shame, and self-induced
vomiting, but body weight remains within normal range. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. anorexia nervosa
   B. bulimia nervosa
   C. binge-eating disorder

 D. avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: B. bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa commonly presents with binge eating and compensatory vomiting
while body weight often remains in the normal range.

75. Which condition most commonly presents with unstable identity, frantic efforts to avoid
abandonment, and chronic feelings of emptiness?

   A. avoidant personality disorder
   B. narcissistic personality disorder
   C. borderline personality disorder

 D. dependent personality disorder
       Answer: C. borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Borderline personality disorder is strongly associated with identity instability,
intense fear of abandonment, and chronic emptiness.

76. In clinical research, which design allows stronger causal inference than correlational
studies?

   A. case study
   B. naturalistic observation
   C. experiment with manipulation and control

 D. archival review alone
       Answer: C. experiment with manipulation and control
   Rationale: Experimental designs permit stronger causal conclusions because variables are
manipulated under controlled conditions.

77. Which statement best reflects the scientist-practitioner model?
   A. Science and practice are separate roles
   B. Clinicians should rely only on intuition
   C. Clinical work should be informed by evidence, and practice can also inform science

 D. Research is unnecessary in abnormal psychology
       Answer: C. Clinical work should be informed by evidence, and practice can also inform
science
   Rationale: The scientist-practitioner model emphasizes that clinical practice should be guided
by research evidence and that systematic clinical work can also contribute to scientific
knowledge.

78. A practitioner interprets a client's symptoms solely as the result of one neurotransmitter
imbalance and ignores trauma history, culture, and cognition. This error reflects:

   A. multidimensional integration
   B. one-dimensional reductionism
   C. evidence-based practice

 D. differential diagnosis
       Answer: B. one-dimensional reductionism
   Rationale: One-dimensional reductionism occurs when complex psychopathology is
explained by a single factor while ignoring other relevant biological, psychological, and social
influences.

79. Which defense-related or unconscious-process idea from psychodynamic traditions
contributed historically to abnormal psychology?

   A. all symptoms are learned by operant conditioning only
   B. internal conflicts can influence behavior outside awareness
   C. all disorders are caused by neurotransmitter depletion

 D. personality is irrelevant to psychopathology
       Answer: B. internal conflicts can influence behavior outside awareness
   Rationale: A major historical contribution of psychodynamic thought is the idea that
unconscious internal conflicts can influence thoughts, feelings, and behavior.

80. Which statement is most consistent with behavioral theories?
   A. maladaptive behavior may be acquired and maintained through learning
   B. all mental disorders are inherited in a Mendelian pattern
   C. symptoms have no environmental determinants

 D. unconscious conflict is the sole cause of phobia
       Answer: A. maladaptive behavior may be acquired and maintained through learning
   Rationale: Behavioral theories explain abnormal behavior as something learned and
maintained through conditioning, reinforcement, and environmental contingencies.

81. Which condition is characterized by excessive dependence and submissive behavior
leading to difficulty making everyday decisions without reassurance?

   A. dependent personality disorder
   B. avoidant personality disorder
   C. borderline personality disorder

 D. schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: A. dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Dependent personality disorder is marked by excessive need to be taken care of,
submissive behavior, and difficulty making everyday decisions without reassurance.

82. A client persistently prefers solitary activities, shows emotional coldness, and neither desires
nor enjoys close relationships. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. avoidant personality disorder
   B. schizoid personality disorder
   C. social anxiety disorder

 D. dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizoid personality disorder involves detachment from social relationships and
restricted emotional expression.

83. Odd beliefs, perceptual distortions, and acute discomfort in close relationships are most
characteristic of:

   A. paranoid personality disorder
   B. schizotypal personality disorder
   C. schizoid personality disorder

 D. obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: B. schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizotypal personality disorder is defined by eccentric behavior, odd beliefs or
perceptual experiences, and marked interpersonal discomfort.

84. Under Republic Act No. 10029, which statement is most accurate?
   A. Any guidance worker may independently practice psychology without licensure
   B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally practice

within the bounds of the law
   C. Psychometricians may independently perform all interventions reserved for psychologists

 D. Students may represent themselves as licensed practitioners during internship
       Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally
practice within the bounds of the law
   Rationale: RA 10029 legally regulates the practice of psychology in the Philippines and
requires proper licensure and registration within the limits set by law.
85. A psychometrician is asked to provide a complex psychotherapy service independently
despite lacking training for such intervention. The most ethical response is to:

   A. accept because any mental health service is within psychometric practice
   B. proceed if the client insists
   C. decline or refer and practice only within competence and legal scope

 D. provide the service secretly to gain experience
       Answer: C. decline or refer and practice only within competence and legal scope
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires professionals to work only within their lawful scope and
demonstrated competence, making referral or decline the proper response.

86. A practitioner uses a new assessment technology unfamiliar to them. According to ethical
standards on competence, the best course is to:

   A. use it immediately if it seems efficient
   B. undergo relevant education, training, supervision, consultation, or study first
   C. rely on intuition rather than manuals

 D. delegate interpretation to the client
       Answer: B. undergo relevant education, training, supervision, consultation, or study first
   Rationale: Ethical standards require practitioners to gain appropriate competence before
using unfamiliar tools, techniques, or technologies.

87. A licensed professional receives a third-party request for assessment. The most appropriate
initial step is to:

   A. withhold all information from everyone
   B. clarify the nature of the professional relationship, the client, probable uses of information,
and limits of confidentiality
   C. refuse all third-party requests

 D. disclose the full report to all interested parties without consent
       Answer: B. clarify the nature of the professional relationship, the client, probable uses of
information, and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires role clarification at the outset when third parties request
services, including who the client is and how information will be used.

88. Which action best reflects informed consent in psychological services?
   A. obtaining agreement using language reasonably understandable to the client
   B. securing consent only when billing is discussed
   C. avoiding discussion of risks to prevent anxiety

 D. limiting information so the client will comply
       Answer: A. obtaining agreement using language reasonably understandable to the client
   Rationale: Informed consent requires that clients receive understandable information
sufficient for a voluntary and informed decision.

89. A clinician discusses an identifiable client case in a public elevator. This most clearly
violates:

   A. beneficence
   B. confidentiality
   C. informed consent

 D. competence
       Answer: B. confidentiality
   Rationale: Discussing identifiable client information in a public place breaches the obligation
to protect private and confidential information.

90. A supervisor assigns a complex psychological interpretation task to an untrained assistant
without supervision. This primarily violates ethical standards on:

   A. delegation of work and competence
   B. record keeping only
   C. fee collection

 D. test norms only
       Answer: A. delegation of work and competence
   Rationale: Ethical standards require that delegated work match the assistant's training and
that proper supervision be provided.

91. A practitioner enters a business partnership with a current therapy client, creating risk of
exploitation and impaired objectivity. This is best described as:

   A. acceptable networking
   B. multiple relationship with ethical risk
   C. standard referral practice

 D. emergency intervention
       Answer: B. multiple relationship with ethical risk
   Rationale: A business relationship with a current client creates a multiple relationship that
may impair objectivity and increase the risk of exploitation.

92. A psychologist learns that another practitioner's conduct poses substantial harm to a person
or organization. The ethics code indicates the psychologist should:

   A. always ignore it to preserve collegiality
   B. take further appropriate action, including reporting to proper authorities when warranted
   C. post the allegation publicly online

 D. disclose confidential client material to unrelated parties
       Answer: B. take further appropriate action, including reporting to proper authorities when
warranted
   Rationale: When likely substantial harm is involved, ethical standards support taking
appropriate further action, including formal reporting when necessary.

93. Which statement about telepsychology is most consistent with the ethical code?
   A. Online services are exempt from ordinary ethical principles
   B. Virtual services are covered by the same ethical principles governing face-to-face services
   C. Confidentiality does not apply online
   D. Informed consent is unnecessary online
  Answer: B. Virtual services are covered by the same ethical principles governing

face-to-face services
   Rationale: Ethical standards explicitly apply to services delivered through telepsychology and

other online formats in the same way they apply to in-person practice.

94. A practitioner experiencing severe personal distress that impairs competence should:
   A. continue all duties unchanged
   B. conceal the problem from everyone
   C. obtain consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or terminate

duties

 D. transfer all files to friends informally
       Answer: C. obtain consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or
terminate duties
   Rationale: Ethical responsibility requires practitioners to address personal problems that
impair competence and to take protective steps regarding professional duties.

95. Which action best reflects evidence-based practice?
   A. choosing the treatment with the strongest research support while considering clinical

expertise and client factors
   B. selecting interventions solely because they are popular online
   C. ignoring diagnosis and assessment findings

 D. avoiding outcome monitoring
       Answer: A. choosing the treatment with the strongest research support while considering
clinical expertise and client factors
   Rationale: Evidence-based practice integrates the best available research evidence with
clinical expertise and the client's characteristics, context, and preferences.

96. Which of the following is the clearest example of avoidance behavior maintaining anxiety?
   A. repeated exposure to the feared object until distress declines
   B. escaping feared situations, which temporarily reduces distress and reinforces avoidance
   C. expressing anger openly

 D. sleeping longer during weekends
       Answer: B. escaping feared situations, which temporarily reduces distress and reinforces
avoidance
   Rationale: Avoidance is maintained because escaping feared situations reduces anxiety in
the short term, reinforcing the behavior.

97. In risk assessment, the presence of which factor most strongly elevates concern for
imminent self-harm?

   A. good social support
   B. no psychiatric history
   C. suicidal ideation with plan, intent, and access to means

 D. future-oriented goals only
       Answer: C. suicidal ideation with plan, intent, and access to means
   Rationale: The combination of suicidal ideation, a specific plan, intent, and access to means
indicates significantly increased immediate risk.

98. A clinician suspects a patient's depressive symptoms may be due to hypothyroidism. The
next best step is to:

   A. diagnose major depressive disorder immediately
   B. ignore medical possibilities because mood symptoms are psychological
   C. evaluate for an etiological medical condition before finalizing a primary psychiatric
diagnosis

 D. diagnose malingering
       Answer: C. evaluate for an etiological medical condition before finalizing a primary
psychiatric diagnosis
   Rationale: When a medical condition such as hypothyroidism may explain depressive
symptoms, medical etiology must be evaluated before assigning a primary psychiatric diagnosis.

99. Which statement about diagnosis is most defensible?
   A. Diagnosis is useless if disorders overlap
   B. Diagnosis helps organize information, guide treatment, and communicate clinically, but

must be used with judgment
   C. Diagnosis should replace individualized assessment

 D. Diagnosis is determined only by checklist scoring
       Answer: B. Diagnosis helps organize information, guide treatment, and communicate
clinically, but must be used with judgment
   Rationale: Diagnosis is valuable for communication and treatment planning, but it must be
applied with clinical judgment and individualized assessment.

100. Which of the following best reflects a high-quality board-style approach to
psychopathology?

    A. relying on memorization alone
    B. integrating diagnostic criteria, differential diagnosis, etiology, functional impairment, and
ethical/legal context
    C. avoiding situational questions

 D. focusing only on rare disorders
        Answer: B. integrating diagnostic criteria, differential diagnosis, etiology, functional
impairment, and ethical/legal context
    Rationale: A strong board-style approach requires integrating classification, clinical
reasoning, causal understanding, impairment, and professional ethical-legal considerations.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 7
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 7

1. Which statement best reflects the contemporary understanding of abnormal behavior?
  A. Psychological disorders are caused by either biology or environment, but not both.
  B. Abnormal behavior is best understood through an interaction of biological, psychological,

and social factors.
  C. Abnormal behavior is primarily a result of unconscious conflict.

 D. Mental disorders are only valid if a biological lesion is identified.
       Answer: B. Abnormal behavior is best understood through an interaction of biological,
psychological, and social factors.
  Rationale: This reflects the integrative model of psychopathology, which explains abnormal
behavior through the interaction of biological, psychological, and social influences rather than
any single cause.

2. A psychometrician evaluates a client who reports severe sadness, insomnia, fatigue, and
hopelessness. Before concluding that the client has major depressive disorder, the most
appropriate differential diagnostic step is to:

  A. Rule out malingering, substance effects, and medical causes
  B. Begin psychotherapy and observe the response
  C. Ask only about family history of depression

 D. Assume depression because the symptoms are classic
       Answer: A. Rule out malingering, substance effects, and medical causes
  Rationale: Differential diagnosis requires first excluding feigning, substance-induced
symptoms, and medical conditions because these may account for depressive presentations
without indicating a primary mood disorder.

3. In the DSM differential diagnostic process, malingering is most strongly suspected when:
  A. Symptoms occur without apparent gain
  B. Symptoms are accompanied by guilt and shame
  C. Symptoms are intentionally produced for a clear external incentive

 D. Symptoms fluctuate over time
       Answer: C. Symptoms are intentionally produced for a clear external incentive
  Rationale: Malingering is defined by the intentional production or exaggeration of symptoms
for a recognizable external benefit such as money, avoiding responsibility, or obtaining drugs.

4. A patient presents with new-onset visual hallucinations after abruptly stopping heavy alcohol
use. The most appropriate initial diagnosis to consider is:

  A. Schizophrenia
  B. Alcohol withdrawal-related condition
  C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Alcohol withdrawal-related condition
  Rationale: Hallucinations occurring after abrupt cessation of heavy alcohol use strongly
suggest a withdrawal-related condition and should be considered before diagnosing a primary
psychotic disorder.

5. Which feature most strongly suggests a mental disorder due to another medical condition
rather than a primary psychiatric disorder?

  A. Long-standing personality pattern since adolescence
  B. Symptoms temporally linked to a documented neurological or endocrine condition
  C. Presence of family history of mental illness

 D. Symptoms that improve with insight-oriented therapy
       Answer: B. Symptoms temporally linked to a documented neurological or endocrine
condition
  Rationale: A clear temporal relationship between psychiatric symptoms and a documented
medical illness supports the conclusion that the mental disturbance is secondary to the medical
condition.

6. A person develops sadness and anxiety after losing a job, but the symptoms do not meet full
criteria for a depressive or anxiety disorder. The most appropriate diagnosis is:

  A. Bipolar II disorder
  B. Adjustment disorder
  C. Persistent depressive disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder
  Rationale: Adjustment disorder is diagnosed when emotional or behavioral symptoms arise in
response to an identifiable stressor but do not meet full criteria for another mental disorder.

7. Which of the following best distinguishes a mental disorder from culturally sanctioned
behavior?

  A. It is unusual to the clinician
  B. It involves any form of distress
  C. It reflects dysfunction with clinically significant distress or impairment not better explained
by cultural context

 D. It is rare in the general population
       Answer: C. It reflects dysfunction with clinically significant distress or impairment not better
explained by cultural context
  Rationale: A mental disorder requires dysfunction plus significant distress or impairment, and
the behavior must not be better understood as a culturally accepted response or practice.

8. The historical supernatural model of abnormal behavior commonly explained mental
disturbance as:

  A. Neurotransmitter imbalance
  B. Reinforcement history
  C. Demonic possession or spirit influence
  D. Cognitive distortion
  Answer: C. Demonic possession or spirit influence

  Rationale: The supernatural model attributed abnormal behavior to possession, curses, or
spiritual forces rather than natural or psychological causes.

9. Hippocrates' contribution to understanding abnormal behavior is most associated with:
  A. Exorcism
  B. Humoral imbalance
  C. Operant conditioning

 D. Dream interpretation
       Answer: B. Humoral imbalance
  Rationale: Hippocrates proposed that abnormal behavior resulted from imbalances in bodily
humors, marking an early biological explanation of mental disturbance.

10. Moral therapy is best described as:
   A. Punishing deviant behavior to promote discipline
   B. Treating patients with kindness, structured routine, and humane care
   C. Using medication as the first-line treatment

 D. Interpreting unconscious sexual conflicts
       Answer: B. Treating patients with kindness, structured routine, and humane care
   Rationale: Moral therapy emphasized dignity, compassion, structure, and humane treatment
as beneficial for individuals with mental illness.

11. Which statement best reflects the scientist-practitioner model in abnormal psychology?
   A. Clinical practice should be based only on personal experience
   B. Research is useful only in laboratory settings
   C. Clinical decisions should be informed by evidence, assessment, and systematic

observation

 D. Practice and research are separate roles that should not overlap
       Answer: C. Clinical decisions should be informed by evidence, assessment, and
systematic observation
   Rationale: The scientist-practitioner model integrates empirical research, clinical expertise,
and careful assessment to guide psychological practice.

12. Which concept best captures the tendency for multiple causal influences to contribute to one
disorder?

   A. Equifinality
   B. Dichotomy
   C. Reductionism

 D. Parsimony
       Answer: A. Equifinality
   Rationale: Equifinality refers to the idea that different causal pathways can lead to the same
disorder, highlighting the complexity of psychopathology.

13. The term "equifinality" means that:
   A. One cause always leads to one disorder
   B. Many different pathways can lead to the same disorder
   C. One disorder can never have more than one cause

 D. Biological causes are more important than psychosocial causes
       Answer: B. Many different pathways can lead to the same disorder
   Rationale: Equifinality means that a single outcome, such as a disorder, may result from
multiple distinct developmental or causal routes.

14. A child inherits a vulnerability for anxiety, but whether the disorder develops depends heavily
on parenting style and stress exposure. This best illustrates:

   A. Mass hysteria
   B. Gene-environment interaction
   C. Classical conditioning alone

 D. Projective identification
       Answer: B. Gene-environment interaction
   Rationale: Gene-environment interaction explains how inherited vulnerability may or may not
result in disorder depending on environmental experiences and stressors.

15. Epigenetics is most concerned with:
   A. The permanent elimination of all genetic risk
   B. How the environment can influence gene expression
   C. Replacing diagnosis with temperament categories

 D. The idea that behavior is unrelated to biology
       Answer: B. How the environment can influence gene expression
   Rationale: Epigenetics studies how environmental factors affect the activation or suppression
of genes without altering the DNA sequence itself.

16. Which brain structure is most directly involved in fear responding and threat detection?
   A. Cerebellum
   B. Amygdala
   C. Medulla

 D. Parietal lobe
       Answer: B. Amygdala
   Rationale: The amygdala plays a central role in processing fear, detecting threats, and
generating emotional responses to danger.

17. Neurotransmitters are best described as:
   A. Endocrine glands in the brain
   B. Electrical impulses moving through bone
   C. Chemical messengers that transmit signals across synapses

 D. Fixed personality traits
       Answer: C. Chemical messengers that transmit signals across synapses
   Rationale: Neurotransmitters are chemicals released by neurons to communicate signals
across synaptic gaps to other neurons.
18. Learned helplessness is most closely associated with:
   A. Elevated mood after reinforcement
   B. A perception that one has no control over aversive events
   C. Increased sensory acuity

 D. Improvement in problem solving under stress
       Answer: B. A perception that one has no control over aversive events
   Rationale: Learned helplessness develops when repeated exposure to uncontrollable
negative events leads a person to believe that efforts to change outcomes are futile.

19. In classical conditioning, a neutral stimulus begins to elicit fear after being paired with an
aversive event. This process is called:

   A. Modeling
   B. Generalization
   C. Conditioning

 D. Extinction burst
       Answer: C. Conditioning
   Rationale: Classical conditioning occurs when a previously neutral stimulus acquires the
ability to evoke fear after repeated pairing with an aversive stimulus.

20. A person develops fear of dogs after being bitten once, then begins fearing all furry animals.
The spread of fear to similar stimuli is:

   A. Habituation
   B. Generalization
   C. Flooding

 D. Counterconditioning
       Answer: B. Generalization
   Rationale: Generalization occurs when a conditioned fear response extends from the original
feared stimulus to other similar stimuli.

21. Prepared learning helps explain why:
   A. All fears are equally easy to acquire
   B. Humans are biologically more ready to fear some stimuli than others
   C. Conditioning never occurs without awareness

 D. Phobias are always consciously chosen
       Answer: B. Humans are biologically more ready to fear some stimuli than others
   Rationale: Prepared learning proposes that humans are evolutionarily predisposed to acquire
certain fears, such as fear of snakes or heights, more readily than others.

22. Which assessment method is most useful for obtaining a broad picture of current symptoms,
history, and functional impairment?

   A. Clinical interview
   B. EEG
   C. Projective drawing alone
 D. Single subtest of an IQ measure
       Answer: A. Clinical interview
   Rationale: The clinical interview provides comprehensive information about symptoms,
history, context, and impairment, making it the foundation of psychological assessment.

23. Behavioral assessment is especially useful when the clinician wants to:
   A. Identify unconscious symbolism only
   B. Observe antecedents and consequences of specific behavior
   C. Diagnose neurological disease without referral

 D. Replace all interviews
       Answer: B. Observe antecedents and consequences of specific behavior
   Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and the environmental
events that precede and follow it, helping identify patterns that maintain the behavior.

24. Which is the best example of a reliability issue in diagnosis?
   A. Whether a diagnosis predicts treatment outcome
   B. Whether two clinicians agree on the same diagnosis
   C. Whether the disorder is stigmatizing

 D. Whether a diagnosis is covered by insurance
       Answer: B. Whether two clinicians agree on the same diagnosis
   Rationale: Reliability refers to consistency, and diagnostic reliability is demonstrated when
different clinicians independently arrive at the same diagnosis.

25. Validity in diagnosis refers primarily to:
   A. Whether a diagnosis is easy to remember
   B. Whether a diagnosis measures or captures what it claims to represent
   C. Whether the manual is popular

 D. Whether the client likes the diagnosis
       Answer: B. Whether a diagnosis measures or captures what it claims to represent
   Rationale: Validity concerns whether a diagnostic category accurately represents the disorder
or construct it is intended to identify.

26. A clinician uses multiple methods such as interview, self-report, behavioral observation, and
collateral information. This approach best reflects:

   A. Assessment triangulation
   B. Narrowband testing
   C. Diagnostic minimalism

 D. The placebo effect
       Answer: A. Assessment triangulation
   Rationale: Assessment triangulation strengthens diagnostic accuracy by combining multiple
data sources and methods rather than relying on a single measure.

27. Which research method is best for determining cause-and-effect relationships?
   A. Case study
   B. Correlational study
   C. Experimental design

 D. Archival summary
       Answer: C. Experimental design
   Rationale: Experimental design allows researchers to manipulate variables and control
conditions, making causal conclusions possible.

28. A correlation between two variables means that:
   A. One variable definitely causes the other
   B. They are associated, but causation cannot be concluded
   C. They are identical constructs

 D. Experimental control has been established
       Answer: B. They are associated, but causation cannot be concluded
   Rationale: Correlation shows that variables are related, but it does not establish that one
causes the other.

29. Which statement about case studies is most accurate?
   A. They are useless in clinical science
   B. They can provide rich detail but have limited generalizability
   C. They always establish causal laws

 D. They replace controlled research
       Answer: B. They can provide rich detail but have limited generalizability
   Rationale: Case studies offer detailed clinical information and can generate hypotheses, but
findings from one case may not apply broadly to others.

30. Ethical research with human participants requires:
   A. Deception whenever possible
   B. Elimination of informed consent
   C. Protection from unnecessary harm and respect for autonomy

 D. Publication before review
       Answer: C. Protection from unnecessary harm and respect for autonomy
   Rationale: Ethical research requires minimizing harm, obtaining informed consent, and
respecting the rights and dignity of participants.

31. Which presentation is most characteristic of generalized anxiety disorder?
   A. Recurrent unexpected panic attacks only
   B. Excessive and difficult-to-control worry across multiple domains
   C. Fear limited to one specific object

 D. Intrusive obsessions with rituals
       Answer: B. Excessive and difficult-to-control worry across multiple domains
   Rationale: Generalized anxiety disorder is marked by chronic, excessive worry about various
aspects of life that is difficult to control.

32. Panic disorder is most strongly associated with:
   A. Persistent delusions of persecution
   B. Recurrent unexpected panic attacks and concern about additional attacks
   C. Exclusive fear of public scrutiny

 D. Chronic sadness with hypersomnia
       Answer: B. Recurrent unexpected panic attacks and concern about additional attacks
   Rationale: Panic disorder involves repeated unexpected panic attacks followed by persistent
worry about future attacks or their consequences.

33. Agoraphobia is best defined as:
   A. Fear of social criticism
   B. Fear of contamination
   C. Anxiety about situations where escape may be difficult or help unavailable

 D. Fear of all outdoor settings because of trauma
       Answer: C. Anxiety about situations where escape may be difficult or help unavailable
   Rationale: Agoraphobia centers on fear of situations in which escape might be hard or
assistance unavailable if panic-like symptoms occur.

34. A student can speak normally at home but consistently fails to speak at school despite
understanding language and wanting to respond. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Selective mutism
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. Conversion disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: A. Selective mutism
   Rationale: Selective mutism involves consistent failure to speak in specific social settings
despite the ability to speak in other settings.

35. Social anxiety disorder is characterized primarily by:
   A. Fear of having a heart attack
   B. Fear of negative evaluation in social or performance situations
   C. Fear of sleep-related paralysis

 D. Fear of being away from home only
       Answer: B. Fear of negative evaluation in social or performance situations
   Rationale: Social anxiety disorder is defined by marked fear of embarrassment, criticism, or
negative judgment in social or performance settings.

36. A child refuses school because of intense distress when separated from parents and fears
that harm will befall them. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Separation anxiety disorder
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Disinhibited social engagement disorder
       Answer: B. Separation anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Separation anxiety disorder involves excessive distress about separation from
attachment figures and fears that harm may come to them.

37. Which feature best distinguishes obsessive-compulsive disorder from generalized anxiety
disorder?

   A. Worry about real-life events only
   B. Presence of obsessions and/or compulsions aimed at reducing distress
   C. Absence of anxiety

 D. Presence of low self-esteem only
       Answer: B. Presence of obsessions and/or compulsions aimed at reducing distress
   Rationale: OCD is distinguished by intrusive obsessions and repetitive compulsions
performed to reduce anxiety or prevent feared outcomes.

38. A patient spends hours checking mirrors and seeking reassurance that a minor skin blemish
is not grotesque. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Delusional disorder, grandiose type

 D. Bulimia nervosa
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Body dysmorphic disorder involves preoccupation with perceived flaws in
appearance and repetitive behaviors such as mirror checking and reassurance seeking.

39. Hoarding disorder is characterized by:
   A. Pleasure in stealing useless objects
   B. Persistent difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value
   C. Obsessions limited to contamination fears

 D. Intentional property destruction
       Answer: B. Persistent difficulty discarding possessions regardless of actual value
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder involves ongoing difficulty discarding possessions, leading to
clutter and impairment, regardless of the items' actual worth.

40. Recurrent hair pulling resulting in hair loss is most consistent with:
   A. Excoriation disorder
   B. Trichotillomania
   C. Stereotypic movement disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Trichotillomania is defined by recurrent hair pulling that causes noticeable hair loss
and repeated attempts to stop.

41. PTSD requires exposure to:
   A. Any common life stressor
   B. Actual or threatened death, serious injury, or sexual violence
   C. Only combat trauma

 D. Any event remembered as embarrassing
       Answer: B. Actual or threatened death, serious injury, or sexual violence
   Rationale: PTSD requires exposure to a qualifying traumatic event involving threat to life,
serious injury, or sexual violence.

42. Which presentation best fits acute stress disorder rather than PTSD?
   A. Symptoms persist for more than 1 year
   B. Symptoms occur immediately after trauma and last less than 1 month
   C. Symptoms begin after a divorce and do not include intrusion

 D. Symptoms are due to a substance
       Answer: B. Symptoms occur immediately after trauma and last less than 1 month
   Rationale: Acute stress disorder develops soon after trauma and lasts from a few days up to
less than one month.

43. A client develops distress, insomnia, and poor concentration after a breakup, but does not
show trauma-specific intrusion and avoidance patterns. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. PTSD
   B. Acute stress disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: C. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: The symptoms follow an identifiable stressor but do not meet trauma-related
diagnostic requirements, making adjustment disorder the best fit.

44. Somatic symptom disorder is best characterized by:
   A. Intentionally feigned symptoms
   B. Distressing somatic symptoms plus excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors related to

them
   C. No physical symptoms but intense fear of illness only

 D. Neurological symptoms incompatible with medical disease only
       Answer: B. Distressing somatic symptoms plus excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors
related to them
   Rationale: Somatic symptom disorder involves real or perceived somatic symptoms
accompanied by disproportionate concern, anxiety, or behavioral response.

45. Illness anxiety disorder is most likely when a person:
   A. Has multiple severe somatic symptoms and no health concerns
   B. Has minimal somatic symptoms but persistent fear of having a serious illness
   C. Fakes symptoms for compensation

 D. Has psychotic delusions about parasites
       Answer: B. Has minimal somatic symptoms but persistent fear of having a serious illness
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder is characterized by high health anxiety despite absent or
only mild somatic symptoms.
46. Conversion disorder is most likely when:
   A. Symptoms are consciously produced for gain
   B. Neurological-type symptoms are incompatible with recognized neurological mechanisms

and are not intentionally feigned
   C. The patient has no distress

 D. Symptoms occur only during intoxication
       Answer: B. Neurological-type symptoms are incompatible with recognized neurological
mechanisms and are not intentionally feigned
   Rationale: Conversion disorder involves functional neurological symptoms that cannot be fully
explained by known medical disease and are not intentionally produced.

47. Factitious disorder differs from malingering in that factitious disorder involves:
   A. Clear external incentives such as money or avoiding charges
   B. Intentional symptom production without obvious external rewards
   C. Unconscious symptom formation only

 D. Genuine neurological disease
       Answer: B. Intentional symptom production without obvious external rewards
   Rationale: Factitious disorder involves deliberate falsification or induction of symptoms
without a clear external incentive, unlike malingering.

48. Dissociative amnesia involves:
   A. Progressive loss of language due to dementia
   B. Inability to recall important autobiographical information, usually of a traumatic or stressful

nature
   C. Hallucinations during intoxication

 D. Fear of social embarrassment
       Answer: B. Inability to recall important autobiographical information, usually of a traumatic
or stressful nature
   Rationale: Dissociative amnesia is defined by memory loss for important personal
information, often related to trauma or severe stress, beyond normal forgetting.

49. Dissociative identity disorder is most associated with:
   A. Two or more distinct personality states and discontinuity in sense of self
   B. Persistent fear of contamination
   C. Manic grandiosity

 D. Global cognitive decline
       Answer: A. Two or more distinct personality states and discontinuity in sense of self
   Rationale: Dissociative identity disorder involves disruption of identity with distinct personality
states and marked discontinuity in self-experience and memory.

50. Depersonalization/derealization disorder is characterized by:
   A. Persistent delusions that the body is dead
   B. Experiences of unreality or detachment from self or surroundings with reality testing intact
   C. Loss of motor function after head injury

 D. Intentional avoidance of mirrors
       Answer: B. Experiences of unreality or detachment from self or surroundings with reality
testing intact
   Rationale: Depersonalization/derealization disorder features detachment from oneself or the
environment while the person still recognizes that these experiences are not objectively real.

51. Which feature most strongly distinguishes anorexia nervosa from avoidant/restrictive food
intake disorder?

   A. Weight loss
   B. Nutritional deficiency
   C. Disturbance in body image and fear of gaining weight

 D. Selective eating
       Answer: C. Disturbance in body image and fear of gaining weight
   Rationale: Anorexia nervosa involves intense fear of weight gain and distorted body image,
which are not required in avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder.

52. Bulimia nervosa is characterized by:
   A. Binge eating with no compensatory behavior
   B. Recurrent binge eating followed by inappropriate compensatory behaviors
   C. Restriction without shape concerns

 D. Psychotic refusal to eat
       Answer: B. Recurrent binge eating followed by inappropriate compensatory behaviors
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa requires repeated binge episodes accompanied by compensatory
behaviors such as vomiting, fasting, or excessive exercise.

53. Binge-eating disorder differs from bulimia nervosa because binge-eating disorder:
   A. Includes regular purging
   B. Requires psychosis
   C. Does not involve recurrent compensatory behavior

 D. Occurs only in males
       Answer: C. Does not involve recurrent compensatory behavior
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder includes recurrent binge episodes but lacks the regular
compensatory behaviors that define bulimia nervosa.

54. Which sleep-wake disorder is characterized by repeated dissatisfaction with sleep quantity
or quality, with difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep?

   A. Narcolepsy
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Circadian misperception syndrome
       Answer: B. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Insomnia disorder is defined by persistent difficulty initiating sleep, maintaining
sleep, or waking too early, along with dissatisfaction about sleep quality or quantity.
55. Narcolepsy is most strongly associated with:
   A. Persistent insomnia due to worry
   B. Sudden sleep attacks and, in some cases, cataplexy
   C. Fear of sleeping in public

 D. Nightmares only
       Answer: B. Sudden sleep attacks and, in some cases, cataplexy
   Rationale: Narcolepsy is characterized by irresistible sleep episodes and may include
cataplexy, a sudden loss of muscle tone.

56. Major depressive disorder requires:
   A. At least 1 day of euphoric mood
   B. A distinct period of depressed mood or loss of interest plus associated symptoms causing

distress or impairment
   C. Lifelong shyness

 D. Mood change due only to bereavement in all cases
       Answer: B. A distinct period of depressed mood or loss of interest plus associated
symptoms causing distress or impairment
   Rationale: Major depressive disorder requires a depressive syndrome centered on depressed
mood and/or loss of interest, along with associated symptoms and clinically significant
impairment.

57. Persistent depressive disorder is best described as:
   A. Chronic depressive symptoms lasting at least 2 years in adults
   B. Brief episodes of sadness after stress
   C. Alternating mania and depression every week

 D. Depression caused by substance intoxication only
       Answer: A. Chronic depressive symptoms lasting at least 2 years in adults
   Rationale: Persistent depressive disorder involves long-standing depressive symptoms that
persist for at least two years in adults.

58. Bipolar I disorder requires:
   A. At least one manic episode
   B. At least one hypomanic episode only
   C. Chronic low-grade depression only

 D. Panic attacks with grandiosity
       Answer: A. At least one manic episode
   Rationale: A diagnosis of Bipolar I disorder requires the occurrence of at least one manic
episode, regardless of whether depressive episodes also occur.

59. Bipolar II disorder is diagnosed when there is:
   A. A full manic episode without depression
   B. Hypomanic episode plus major depressive episode, with no history of mania
   C. Mood swings within a single day only
 D. Cyclothymic temperament without impairment
       Answer: B. Hypomanic episode plus major depressive episode, with no history of mania
   Rationale: Bipolar II disorder requires at least one hypomanic episode and at least one major
depressive episode, without any past manic episode.

60. Cyclothymic disorder involves:
   A. Rapidly changing psychotic symptoms
   B. Chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive symptoms that do not meet full episode

criteria
   C. One severe manic episode

 D. Depression secondary to thyroid disease
       Answer: B. Chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive symptoms that do not meet full
episode criteria
   Rationale: Cyclothymic disorder is a chronic mood disturbance involving recurring
subthreshold hypomanic and depressive symptoms over time.

61. Which symptom is considered a negative symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Hallucinations
   B. Delusions
   C. Avolition

 D. Flight of ideas
       Answer: C. Avolition
   Rationale: Avolition, or diminished motivation and goal-directed behavior, is a classic negative
symptom of schizophrenia.

62. Which of the following best describes delusion?
   A. A false sensory perception
   B. A fixed false belief not ordinarily accepted by one's culture
   C. A severe memory gap

 D. An intrusive obsession recognized as irrational
       Answer: B. A fixed false belief not ordinarily accepted by one's culture
   Rationale: A delusion is a firmly held false belief that is not consistent with cultural norms and
is maintained despite contrary evidence.

63. A patient has at least 1 month of psychotic symptoms but the disturbance has lasted less
than 6 months overall. The diagnosis most consistent with this is:

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophreniform disorder
   Rationale: Schizophreniform disorder involves schizophrenia-like symptoms lasting more than
one month but less than six months.
64. Delusional disorder differs from schizophrenia in that delusional disorder:
   A. Never involves false beliefs
   B. Usually lacks the broad functional deterioration and prominent bizarre psychotic symptoms

typical of schizophrenia
   C. Is always caused by substances

 D. Requires depressed mood
       Answer: B. Usually lacks the broad functional deterioration and prominent bizarre
psychotic symptoms typical of schizophrenia
   Rationale: Delusional disorder is generally more circumscribed, with relatively preserved
functioning outside the delusional belief system.

65. Schizoaffective disorder requires:
   A. Only psychotic symptoms
   B. A major mood episode concurrent with psychotic symptoms, plus a period of psychosis

without mood symptoms
   C. Lifelong odd beliefs only

 D. Panic attacks with derealization
       Answer: B. A major mood episode concurrent with psychotic symptoms, plus a period of
psychosis without mood symptoms
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both a major mood episode and psychotic
symptoms, with psychosis also occurring for a period independent of mood symptoms.

66. Catatonia may include:
   A. Compulsions and obsessions only
   B. Stupor, mutism, posturing, and echolalia
   C. Euphoria and distractibility only

 D. Rumination and binge eating
       Answer: B. Stupor, mutism, posturing, and echolalia
   Rationale: Catatonia is characterized by marked psychomotor disturbance such as immobility,
mutism, posturing, and echo phenomena.

67. Which disorder is most strongly associated with persistent disregard for and violation of the
rights of others since age 15, with evidence of conduct disorder before age 15?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Antisocial personality disorder requires a pattern of violating the rights of others
since age 15 and evidence of conduct disorder before age 15.

68. A pervasive pattern of instability in relationships, self-image, affect, and impulsivity is most
consistent with:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Borderline personality disorder is defined by instability in emotions, identity,
relationships, and impulsive behavior.

69. A person who is detached from social relationships and shows restricted emotional
expression most likely has:

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Dependent personality disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizoid personality disorder is marked by social detachment and limited
emotional expression in interpersonal contexts.

70. A pervasive pattern of social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to
negative evaluation is most consistent with:

   A. Avoidant personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: A. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder features chronic social inhibition and feelings of
inadequacy driven by fear of rejection or criticism.

71. Which feature best distinguishes obsessive-compulsive personality disorder from
obsessive-compulsive disorder?

   A. OCPD involves perfectionism and control as personality traits rather than true obsessions
and compulsions

   B. OCPD includes hallucinations
   C. OCD never includes distress

 D. OCPD requires panic attacks
       Answer: A. OCPD involves perfectionism and control as personality traits rather than true
obsessions and compulsions
   Rationale: Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder reflects a rigid personality style
centered on orderliness and control, unlike OCD, which involves intrusive obsessions and
compulsive rituals.

72. Conduct disorder is best characterized by:
   A. Persistent inattention only
   B. Repetitive violation of the rights of others and major age-appropriate norms
   C. Fear of separation
 D. Chronic depressed mood
       Answer: B. Repetitive violation of the rights of others and major age-appropriate norms
   Rationale: Conduct disorder involves repeated aggression, deceit, destruction, or serious rule
violations that infringe on others' rights or societal norms.

73. Oppositional defiant disorder is most defined by:
   A. Aggression causing serious harm only
   B. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, or vindictiveness
   C. Fire-setting for pleasure

 D. Recurrent stealing for monetary gain
       Answer: B. A pattern of angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, or
vindictiveness
   Rationale: Oppositional defiant disorder is characterized by persistent irritability, defiance, and
vindictive behavior toward authority figures.

74. Intermittent explosive disorder involves:
   A. Premeditated aggression for personal gain
   B. Recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts grossly out of proportion to provocation
   C. Chronic violation of rights since childhood

 D. Panic with derealization
       Answer: B. Recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts grossly out of proportion to
provocation
   Rationale: Intermittent explosive disorder is defined by repeated impulsive aggressive
episodes that are excessive relative to the trigger.

75. Pyromania is characterized by:
   A. Fire-setting exclusively for insurance fraud
   B. Deliberate fire-setting associated with tension before the act and fascination or pleasure

afterward
   C. Any accidental house fire

 D. Fire-setting during a manic episode only
       Answer: B. Deliberate fire-setting associated with tension before the act and fascination or
pleasure afterward
   Rationale: Pyromania involves intentional fire-setting driven by internal tension and followed
by relief, fascination, or gratification.

76. Kleptomania is best described as:
   A. Planned theft for financial need
   B. Recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal objects not needed for personal use or value
   C. Conduct disorder in all cases

 D. Delusional belief that one owns all objects
       Answer: B. Recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal objects not needed for personal
use or value
   Rationale: Kleptomania involves recurrent impulse-driven stealing of items that are not
needed for personal use or financial gain.

77. Which substance class is a depressant?
   A. Cocaine
   B. Alcohol
   C. Amphetamine

 D. LSD
       Answer: B. Alcohol
   Rationale: Alcohol is a central nervous system depressant that reduces neural activity and
slows physiological functioning.

78. Tolerance refers to:
   A. Withdrawal after stopping a substance
   B. Needing markedly increased amounts to achieve the desired effect or diminished effect

with continued use of the same amount
   C. Craving only

 D. Social approval of use
       Answer: B. Needing markedly increased amounts to achieve the desired effect or
diminished effect with continued use of the same amount
   Rationale: Tolerance occurs when repeated substance use produces reduced effects,
requiring more of the substance to achieve the original result.

79. Withdrawal is best defined as:
   A. Loss of interest in hobbies after stress
   B. A maladaptive behavioral pattern unrelated to substance cessation
