   C. A substance-specific syndrome following reduction or cessation after heavy prolonged use

 D. Any hangover
       Answer: C. A substance-specific syndrome following reduction or cessation after heavy
prolonged use
   Rationale: Withdrawal consists of characteristic physical or psychological symptoms that
emerge when a heavily used substance is reduced or stopped.

80. Which is classified as a behavioral addiction in DSM?
   A. Excessive shopping
   B. Gambling disorder
   C. Internet use disorder as an official diagnosis

 D. Workaholism
       Answer: B. Gambling disorder
   Rationale: Gambling disorder is the recognized behavioral addiction formally classified with
substance-related and addictive disorders.

81. Delirium is most accurately described as:
   A. A chronic psychotic disorder
   B. An acute disturbance in attention and awareness with fluctuating course
   C. A personality disorder of old age

 D. Normal aging
       Answer: B. An acute disturbance in attention and awareness with fluctuating course
   Rationale: Delirium is an acute, fluctuating disturbance in consciousness and cognition,
usually caused by a medical condition, intoxication, or withdrawal.

82. Major neurocognitive disorder is distinguished from mild neurocognitive disorder primarily
by:

   A. Presence of hallucinations
   B. Degree of cognitive decline and interference with independence in everyday activities
   C. Age of onset before 18

 D. Presence of depressed mood
       Answer: B. Degree of cognitive decline and interference with independence in everyday
activities
   Rationale: Major neurocognitive disorder causes significant cognitive decline that interferes
with independent functioning, unlike mild neurocognitive disorder.

83. A child has persistent deficits in social communication and restricted, repetitive patterns of
behavior. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Selective mutism
       Answer: B. Autism spectrum disorder
   Rationale: Autism spectrum disorder requires both social communication deficits and
restricted, repetitive behaviors.

84. ADHD is most strongly characterized by:
   A. Traumatic memory loss
   B. Persistent pattern of inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity that interferes with

functioning
   C. Severe conduct violation only

 D. Hallucinations and distractibility
       Answer: B. Persistent pattern of inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity that interferes
with functioning
   Rationale: ADHD is defined by enduring inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity severe
enough to impair functioning.

85. Specific learning disorder refers to:
   A. Low motivation in school only
   B. Difficulties learning academic skills such as reading, writing, or mathematics despite

appropriate opportunity
   C. Intellectual disability in all cases
 D. Autism spectrum disorder with language delay
       Answer: B. Difficulties learning academic skills such as reading, writing, or mathematics
despite appropriate opportunity
   Rationale: Specific learning disorder involves persistent problems in academic skill acquisition
that are not better explained by lack of opportunity or general intellectual disability.

86. Intellectual disability requires deficits in:
   A. Mood stability and appetite
   B. Intellectual and adaptive functioning, with onset during the developmental period
   C. Social confidence only

 D. Memory only after age 65
       Answer: B. Intellectual and adaptive functioning, with onset during the developmental
period
   Rationale: Intellectual disability requires impairments in both intellectual ability and adaptive
functioning beginning during development.

87. Which statement about paraphilic disorders is most accurate?
   A. Any unusual sexual interest automatically qualifies as a disorder
   B. A paraphilic disorder requires distress, impairment, or harm/risk of harm to others
   C. They are identical to gender dysphoria

 D. They are always psychotic in origin
       Answer: B. A paraphilic disorder requires distress, impairment, or harm/risk of harm to
others
   Rationale: An atypical sexual interest becomes a paraphilic disorder only when it causes
significant distress, impairment, or involves harm or risk to others.

88. Gender dysphoria refers to:
   A. Any nonconforming gender expression
   B. Distress associated with incongruence between experienced gender and assigned sex
   C. Delusional denial of biological sex

 D. Sexual dysfunction during adulthood only
       Answer: B. Distress associated with incongruence between experienced gender and
assigned sex
   Rationale: Gender dysphoria is defined by clinically significant distress resulting from
incongruence between one's experienced gender and assigned sex.

89. Under the PAP Code of Ethics and RA 10029-linked boundaries of competence, a
psychometrician should:

   A. Independently provide any psychological service as long as the client agrees
   B. Practice only within legal and competence boundaries and make referrals when needed
   C. Interpret obsolete tests if requested by a physician

 D. Delegate all testing to untrained staff
       Answer: B. Practice only within legal and competence boundaries and make referrals
when needed
   Rationale: Ethical and lawful practice requires psychometricians to work only within their
competence and legal scope, and to refer cases when services exceed those limits.

90. Which action is most ethical when a practitioner is asked to assess a client using a test for
which the practitioner has no adequate training?

   A. Proceed to avoid losing the referral
   B. Administer the test and interpret cautiously without disclosure
   C. Obtain proper supervision/training or refer to a qualified professional

 D. Use photocopied materials to practice
       Answer: C. Obtain proper supervision/training or refer to a qualified professional
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires competence, so the practitioner should first obtain proper
training or supervision or refer the client to someone qualified.

91. Which practice is most consistent with ethical assessment?
   A. Using photocopied test materials if the originals are unavailable
   B. Selecting only tests relevant to the referral question and appropriate for the client's

characteristics
   C. Releasing raw scores to any interested family member

 D. Reporting outdated test results without qualification
       Answer: B. Selecting only tests relevant to the referral question and appropriate for the
client's characteristics
   Rationale: Ethical assessment requires using appropriate, relevant, and properly selected
instruments suited to the referral question and client characteristics.

92. A psychometrician is asked by a school to send raw test data directly to a teacher without
client permission. The most ethical response is to:

   A. Send all materials because the teacher requested them
   B. Refuse because raw data and test responses are not released except under proper
authority or regulation
   C. Post the results in the class record

 D. Send only the answer sheet photo
       Answer: B. Refuse because raw data and test responses are not released except under
proper authority or regulation
   Rationale: Raw test data and test materials are protected, and disclosure requires proper
authorization, ethical justification, and adherence to confidentiality rules.

93. When explaining assessment results to nonpsychologists, the practitioner should:
   A. Use highly technical language to preserve authority
   B. Explain results in clear nontechnical language
   C. Avoid explaining limitations of the findings

 D. Release only percentile ranks without context
       Answer: B. Explain results in clear nontechnical language
   Rationale: Ethical communication requires that assessment findings be explained in a way
that authorized recipients can understand and use appropriately.
94. A practitioner delegates administration tasks to an assistant who has minimal training.
According to ethical standards, delegation is acceptable only when:

   A. The assistant is a relative of the client
   B. The assistant can reasonably be expected to perform competently with appropriate
supervision
   C. The client is not informed

 D. The task involves test security breaches
       Answer: B. The assistant can reasonably be expected to perform competently with
appropriate supervision
   Rationale: Delegation is ethical only when the person performing the task has sufficient
preparation and receives appropriate supervision to ensure competent service.

95. Which scenario best reflects a conflict of interest?
   A. Referring a client for emergency care
   B. Accepting a professional role when personal or financial interests could impair objectivity
   C. Using informed consent

 D. Consulting with another professional for the client's welfare
       Answer: B. Accepting a professional role when personal or financial interests could impair
objectivity
   Rationale: A conflict of interest exists when personal, financial, or other interests may
interfere with professional judgment or the welfare of the client.

96. A psychometrician is employed in a clinic and is asked to conduct independent
psychotherapy with a client. Under RA 10029-linked role boundaries, the best response is to:

   A. Accept because all mental health workers may provide psychotherapy
   B. Decline and clarify that this falls outside the psychometrician's lawful scope
   C. Proceed if the client signs a waiver

 D. Provide therapy only online
       Answer: B. Decline and clarify that this falls outside the psychometrician's lawful scope
   Rationale: A psychometrician must not perform services outside the legal scope of practice,
and client permission does not override professional licensing boundaries.

97. A client's parent asks for test results from an adolescent's assessment. The most ethical
initial response is to:

   A. Automatically refuse all disclosure
   B. Review the consent arrangement, referral source, and applicable confidentiality limits
before disclosure
   C. Postpone indefinitely

 D. Provide the raw data immediately
       Answer: B. Review the consent arrangement, referral source, and applicable
confidentiality limits before disclosure
   Rationale: Disclosure decisions must be guided by consent, confidentiality rules, legal
context, and clarification of who is entitled to receive the information.
98. Which principle is most directly violated when a practitioner knowingly uses obsolete or
culturally inappropriate tests and still issues firm conclusions?

   A. Beneficence and competence
   B. Naturalism
   C. Projective neutrality

 D. Free association
       Answer: A. Beneficence and competence
   Rationale: Using obsolete or inappropriate tests risks harm and demonstrates failure to
provide competent, responsible professional service.

99. In a third-party referral, ethical practice requires clarifying:
   A. Only the diagnosis
   B. The practitioner's role, who the client is, probable uses of the service, and limits of

confidentiality
   C. Only the fee

 D. Only the testing schedule
       Answer: B. The practitioner's role, who the client is, probable uses of the service, and
limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Third-party services require clear explanation at the outset regarding the
professional role, intended client, uses of the information, and confidentiality boundaries.

100. A board examinee is asked which statement best captures good diagnostic judgment in
abnormal psychology. The best answer is:

    A. Diagnosis is simply matching symptoms to a label as quickly as possible
    B. Clinical judgment should replace all structured diagnostic rules
    C. Sound diagnosis integrates evidence, differential diagnosis, context, impairment, and
ethical practice

 D. Only biological findings make diagnosis legitimate
        Answer: C. Sound diagnosis integrates evidence, differential diagnosis, context,
impairment, and ethical practice
    Rationale: Good diagnostic judgment is systematic and balanced, requiring evidence-based
reasoning, rule-outs, contextual understanding, evaluation of impairment, and ethical
responsibility.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 8
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 8

1. A clinician evaluates a 23-year-old man who reports low mood, poor concentration, insomnia,
and loss of appetite for 3 weeks after failing the psychometrician licensure exam. He remains
hopeful, continues reviewing, and still functions at home. Which is the best clinical judgment?

  A. Major depressive disorder
  B. Persistent depressive disorder
  C. No mental disorder if distress is proportionate and impairment is not clinically significant

 D. Bipolar II disorder
       Answer: C. No mental disorder if distress is proportionate and impairment is not clinically
significant
  Rationale: Not all distress after a stressor qualifies as a mental disorder. A DSM diagnosis
generally requires clinically significant distress or impairment, and proportionate emotional
reactions without marked dysfunction may fall outside disorder boundaries.

2. Which statement best reflects the current multidimensional view of psychopathology?
  A. Psychological disorders are caused primarily by unconscious conflict
  B. Psychological disorders usually result from the interaction of biological, psychological, and

social factors
  C. Psychological disorders are best explained only by genetic vulnerability

 D. Psychological disorders are caused mainly by faulty reinforcement histories
       Answer: B. Psychological disorders usually result from the interaction of biological,
psychological, and social factors
  Rationale: Contemporary abnormal psychology emphasizes an integrative model in which
biological, psychological, and social dimensions interact in the development and maintenance of
disorders.

3. A patient presents with auditory hallucinations after several days of methamphetamine use
and sleep deprivation. In differential diagnosis, the most appropriate immediate priority is to:

  A. Diagnose schizophrenia if hallucinations are bizarre
  B. Rule out substance-induced etiology first
  C. Diagnose brief psychotic disorder if duration is under 1 month

 D. Focus first on personality assessment
       Answer: B. Rule out substance-induced etiology first
  Rationale: Differential diagnosis prioritizes ruling out substance causes early, since
intoxication or withdrawal can mimic many psychiatric syndromes.

4. A psychometrician is asked to independently conduct psychotherapy for a client with panic
disorder in a private clinic. Under RA 10029 and ethical standards, the best response is:

  A. Accept, because panic disorder is a common condition
  B. Accept, if the client signs informed consent
  C. Decline, because psychometricians are prohibited from practicing therapy except in
emergencies
  D. Accept, provided the psychometrician has attended a seminar on CBT
  Answer: C. Decline, because psychometricians are prohibited from practicing therapy

except in emergencies
  Rationale: Ethical standards aligned with RA 10029 prohibit psychometricians from engaging

in psychotherapy except in emergency situations.

5. A woman repeatedly checks her stove for 2 hours each night because she fears the house
will burn down, although she recognizes the fear is excessive. The symptom pattern is most
consistent with:

  A. Generalized anxiety disorder
  B. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
  C. Delusional disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
  Rationale: The case shows obsessions about harm and compulsive checking performed to
reduce distress.

6. Which of the following is the best example of negative reinforcement?
  A. A child studies hard to receive praise
  B. A person avoids elevators to reduce panic sensations
  C. A student reads more because of curiosity

 D. A client is given tokens for adaptive behavior
       Answer: B. A person avoids elevators to reduce panic sensations
  Rationale: Avoidance is maintained by the removal or reduction of an aversive state, which is
negative reinforcement.

7. A man has experienced depressed mood for most of the day, more days than not, for 3 years,
with low self-esteem, hopelessness, fatigue, and poor concentration, but no history of mania.
The most likely diagnosis is:

  A. Cyclothymic disorder
  B. Persistent depressive disorder
  C. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood

 D. Bipolar II disorder
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
  Rationale: The depression is chronic, lasting at least 2 years without mania, which fits
persistent depressive disorder.

8. Which theorist is most strongly associated with classical conditioning?
  A. B. F. Skinner
  B. Ivan Pavlov
  C. Albert Bandura

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: B. Ivan Pavlov
  Rationale: Pavlov is the classic proponent of classical conditioning.
9. A client reports intense fear of embarrassment during recitations and avoids class reporting
despite adequate preparation. The most likely diagnosis is:

  A. Panic disorder
  B. Agoraphobia
  C. Social anxiety disorder

 D. Specific phobia
       Answer: C. Social anxiety disorder
  Rationale: The fear centers on negative evaluation and embarrassment in social or
performance situations.

10. A practitioner is unsure whether a supervisee has violated an ethical standard. Which is the
best initial action when appropriate and when confidentiality is not violated?

   A. Publicly warn others about the supervisee
   B. Immediately file a complaint without discussion
   C. Bring the concern informally to the supervisee's attention

 D. Ignore the matter unless a court order is issued
       Answer: C. Bring the concern informally to the supervisee's attention
   Rationale: Ethical codes support informal resolution first when appropriate and when doing so
does not violate confidentiality or create further harm.

11. Which defense mechanism involves attributing one's own unacceptable impulses to another
person?

   A. Sublimation
   B. Projection
   C. Reaction formation

 D. Displacement
       Answer: B. Projection
   Rationale: Projection involves attributing one's own unacceptable wishes or impulses to
someone else.

12. A patient develops sudden blindness after witnessing a traumatic event, but neurological
findings do not explain the symptom. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Conversion disorder

 D. Factitious disorder
       Answer: C. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: The patient has neurologic-like symptoms incompatible with recognized
neurological explanation and associated with psychological stress.

13. The diathesis-stress model proposes that:
   A. Stress alone causes all disorders
   B. Disorders result when vulnerability interacts with stress
   C. Genetics determines disorders regardless of environment
 D. Cognitive factors are irrelevant in etiology
       Answer: B. Disorders result when vulnerability interacts with stress
   Rationale: The diathesis-stress model posits that predisposition combines with environmental
stressors to increase disorder risk.

14. A 7-year-old boy has persistent deficits in social communication, limited eye contact,
repetitive behaviors, and insistence on sameness since early development. The best diagnosis
is:

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Autism spectrum disorder

 D. Reactive attachment disorder
       Answer: C. Autism spectrum disorder
   Rationale: Early-emerging deficits in social communication plus restricted and repetitive
behavior are defining features of autism spectrum disorder.

15. Which neurotransmitter has long been centrally implicated in schizophrenia because of the
effects of antipsychotic medications?

   A. GABA
   B. Dopamine
   C. Acetylcholine

 D. Endorphin
       Answer: B. Dopamine
   Rationale: Dopamine dysregulation has been centrally implicated in schizophrenia,
particularly given the action of many antipsychotic medications on dopamine pathways.

16. A college student has recurrent unexpected panic attacks and then worries for months about
additional attacks and their consequences. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Specific phobia
   B. Panic disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Acute stress disorder
       Answer: B. Panic disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent unexpected panic attacks followed by persistent concern or behavioral
change is the classic pattern of panic disorder.

17. A licensed psychometrician administers a psychological test using photocopied materials to
save costs. Ethically, this is:

   A. Acceptable if the test is widely used
   B. Acceptable if the client agrees
   C. Unethical because only original copies of test materials should be used

 D. Ethical if done in a school setting
       Answer: C. Unethical because only original copies of test materials should be used
   Rationale: Ethical standards require use of original test materials and prohibit use of
photocopied testing materials.

18. A client experiences alternating periods of inflated self-esteem, decreased need for sleep,
pressured speech, and risky spending severe enough to require hospitalization. The diagnosis
is most consistent with:

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: C. Bipolar I disorder
   Rationale: A manic episode severe enough to require hospitalization is sufficient for bipolar I
disorder.

19. In operant conditioning, behavior is strengthened by its consequences. This principle is most
associated with:

   A. Albert Ellis
   B. B. F. Skinner
   C. Sigmund Freud

 D. Carl Rogers
       Answer: B. B. F. Skinner
   Rationale: Skinner developed the operant conditioning framework emphasizing
consequences of behavior.

20. A woman believes she is infested with parasites despite repeated negative medical
workups. She is firmly convinced and not reassured by evidence. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Delusional disorder, somatic type
   C. Obsessive-compulsive disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Delusional disorder, somatic type
   Rationale: The belief is fixed, false, and not corrected by medical evidence, fitting a somatic
delusion.

21. Which is the hallmark feature of generalized anxiety disorder?
   A. Fear triggered only by specific objects
   B. Recurrent obsessions without worry
   C. Excessive anxiety and worry occurring more days than not about multiple events

 D. Brief intense fear lasting only during trauma exposure
       Answer: C. Excessive anxiety and worry occurring more days than not about multiple
events
   Rationale: Generalized anxiety disorder is defined by chronic, excessive, difficult-to-control
worry across domains.
22. A practitioner is asked by a school to release a student's raw test scores to a teacher for
classroom discussion. The most ethical response is:

   A. Release immediately because the teacher is part of the school
   B. Release only if the student verbally agrees
   C. Do not release raw test data to unauthorized persons except when legally required

 D. Release if the teacher promises confidentiality
       Answer: C. Do not release raw test data to unauthorized persons except when legally
required
   Rationale: Raw test data are protected and should not be released to unauthorized
individuals except under legal regulation such as court order.

23. Which is the best distinction between obsession and compulsion?
   A. Obsession is a behavior; compulsion is a belief
   B. Obsession is an intrusive thought; compulsion is a repetitive act meant to reduce distress
   C. Obsession is always psychotic; compulsion is always neurotic

 D. Obsession occurs in mood disorders only
       Answer: B. Obsession is an intrusive thought; compulsion is a repetitive act meant to
reduce distress
   Rationale: Obsessions are intrusive unwanted thoughts, urges, or images, whereas
compulsions are repetitive behaviors or mental acts performed to reduce anxiety or prevent
feared outcomes.

24. A 19-year-old man reports recurrent binge eating with compensatory self-induced vomiting
at least once a week for 4 months, with overvaluation of weight and shape. The most likely
diagnosis is:

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder

 D. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Recurrent binge eating plus compensatory vomiting and overvaluation of
shape/weight are classic for bulimia nervosa.

25. Which is most characteristic of anorexia nervosa?
   A. Recurrent binge eating without body image disturbance
   B. Restriction of energy intake leading to significantly low body weight with intense fear of

gaining weight
   C. Weight loss caused only by a medical illness

 D. Eating nonnutritive substances
       Answer: B. Restriction of energy intake leading to significantly low body weight with
intense fear of gaining weight
   Rationale: That is the core syndrome of anorexia nervosa.
26. A client worries constantly about having cancer despite minimal somatic symptoms and
repeated reassurance. The preoccupation itself is central. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Illness anxiety disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: The main problem is persistent fear of serious illness despite minimal somatic
symptoms.

27. Who is most associated with the concept of cognitive distortions in depression?
   A. Aaron Beck
   B. Carl Rogers
   C. Alfred Adler

 D. Erik Erikson
       Answer: A. Aaron Beck
   Rationale: Beck's cognitive theory of depression emphasizes negative automatic thoughts
and cognitive distortions.

28. Which sleep disorder is characterized by repeated episodes of irresistible sleep attacks,
cataplexy in some cases, and REM-related abnormalities?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Narcolepsy
   C. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder

 D. Nightmare disorder
       Answer: B. Narcolepsy
   Rationale: Narcolepsy is characterized by irresistible sleep episodes and may include
cataplexy and REM-related abnormalities.

29. A man drinks heavily every weekend despite recurrent arguments with his spouse, poor
work performance, and inability to cut down. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Alcohol intoxication
   B. Alcohol use disorder
   C. Social drinking

 D. Delirium tremens
       Answer: B. Alcohol use disorder
   Rationale: The pattern shows impaired control, continued use despite problems, and clinically
significant impairment.

30. Which term refers to the co-occurrence of two or more disorders in the same individual?
   A. Prodrome
   B. Comorbidity
   C. Catatonia
   D. Prognosis
  Answer: B. Comorbidity

   Rationale: Comorbidity is the co-occurrence of two or more disorders in one individual.

31. A patient presents with fluctuating consciousness, impaired attention, disorientation, and
visual illusions developing over one day after infection. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Major neurocognitive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Acute fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness with medical precipitants
strongly indicates delirium.

32. A psychometrician is asked to interpret test findings beyond their competence in a
specialized forensic case. The most ethical response is to:

   A. Proceed because test interpretation is always within psychometrician scope
   B. Refuse and make an appropriate referral or seek proper supervision within legal limits
   C. Interpret the results using internet sources

 D. Give only a verbal impression to avoid documentation
       Answer: B. Refuse and make an appropriate referral or seek proper supervision within
legal limits
   Rationale: Practitioners must remain within competence and legal scope, especially in
forensic contexts.

33. Which is the strongest clinical feature differentiating hallucination from illusion?
   A. Hallucinations are always visual
   B. Illusions occur without external stimuli
   C. Hallucinations occur without external stimuli

 D. Illusions occur only in psychotic disorders
       Answer: C. Hallucinations occur without external stimuli
   Rationale: Hallucinations are perceptions without external input, while illusions are
misinterpretations of real stimuli.

34. A person persistently violates the rights of others, deceives, acts impulsively, lacks remorse,
and had conduct problems before age 15. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Chronic disregard for and violation of others' rights, with conduct disorder before
age 15, fits antisocial personality disorder.
35. Which personality disorder is most associated with instability in relationships, self-image,
affect, and marked impulsivity?

   A. Avoidant personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: B. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Instability in affect, identity, relationships, and impulsivity is the hallmark profile of
borderline personality disorder.

36. A child frequently argues with adults, deliberately annoys others, and is angry and resentful,
but has not committed serious aggression or major rule violations. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   Rationale: The child is argumentative, defiant, and resentful without the severe aggression or
major rule-breaking typical of conduct disorder.

37. Which finding most strongly supports attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder rather than a
specific learning disorder alone?

   A. Difficulty only in reading comprehension
   B. Persistent inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity across settings
   C. Low math scores only

 D. Poor performance only in one academic subject
       Answer: B. Persistent inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity across settings
   Rationale: ADHD requires pervasive symptoms across settings, not just poor performance in
one academic area.

38. A client has severe memory gaps for personal information after a disaster and cannot recall
important autobiographical details, without evidence of ordinary forgetting. The most likely
diagnosis is:

   A. Delirium
   B. Dissociative amnesia
   C. Major depressive disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: B. Dissociative amnesia
   Rationale: Inability to recall important autobiographical information, often after trauma, is
characteristic of dissociative amnesia.

39. In the context of ethics, informed consent requires that the person understand the nature of
the service, risks, limits of confidentiality, and relevant conditions. Which element is essential?

   A. Blind agreement
   B. Coercion
   C. Comprehension

 D. Technical language only
       Answer: C. Comprehension
   Rationale: Informed consent is not valid unless the person understands the information being
provided.

40. A person reports hearing voices commenting on behavior, disorganized speech, and social
withdrawal for 8 months, with significant impairment. Substance and medical causes have been
ruled out. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Schizophrenia
   Rationale: Psychotic symptoms with impairment lasting more than 6 months are most
consistent with schizophrenia once substances and medical causes are ruled out.

41. Which disorder is characterized by recurrent pulling out of one's hair resulting in hair loss
and repeated attempts to decrease or stop?

   A. Excoriation disorder
   B. Trichotillomania
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: B. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Recurrent hair pulling causing hair loss with repeated attempts to stop defines
trichotillomania.

42. A client persistently believes a minor facial feature is hideous and repeatedly checks mirrors
for hours. The primary diagnosis is:

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Delusional disorder, grandiose type

 D. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: The person is preoccupied with a perceived defect and engages in repetitive
checking behavior.

43. Which is the best example of malingering?
   A. Producing symptoms to assume the sick role without clear external gain
   B. Feigning symptoms for financial compensation or to avoid legal responsibility
   C. Experiencing symptoms unconsciously after trauma

 D. Exaggerating distress due to catastrophic thinking
       Answer: B. Feigning symptoms for financial compensation or to avoid legal responsibility
   Rationale: Malingering involves intentional production or exaggeration of symptoms for clear
external gain.

44. A woman experiences recurrent intrusive trauma memories, nightmares, avoidance,
hypervigilance, and negative mood changes for 2 months after sexual assault. The most likely
diagnosis is:

   A. Acute stress disorder
   B. PTSD
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. PTSD
   Rationale: Trauma-related intrusion, avoidance, arousal, and negative mood/cognition
symptoms persisting beyond 1 month fit PTSD.

45. Which distinguishes acute stress disorder from PTSD most directly?
   A. Presence of anxiety
   B. Duration and timing of symptoms after trauma
   C. Presence of avoidance

 D. Presence of sleep disturbance
       Answer: B. Duration and timing of symptoms after trauma
   Rationale: Acute stress disorder and PTSD overlap symptomatically, but they are
distinguished chiefly by timing and duration.

46. A 15-year-old has severe recurrent temper outbursts grossly out of proportion to the
situation, with persistently irritable mood between outbursts for over a year. The best diagnosis
is:

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Bipolar I disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   Rationale: Chronic irritability plus recurrent severe temper outbursts in youth is the defining
profile of DMDD.

47. Which is most characteristic of delusional disorder?
   A. Prominent disorganized speech and grossly disorganized behavior
   B. Nonbizarre or bizarre delusions lasting at least 1 month with relatively preserved

functioning aside from the delusion's impact
   C. Recurrent panic attacks with insight

 D. Hallucinations occurring only during delirium
       Answer: B. Nonbizarre or bizarre delusions lasting at least 1 month with relatively
preserved functioning aside from the delusion's impact
   Rationale: Delusional disorder is defined by persistent delusions without the broad
deterioration typical of schizophrenia.
48. A practitioner is asked to provide teleassessment using a test for which no appropriate
norms exist for the client's language and background. The most ethical action is to:

   A. Administer anyway and ignore limitations
   B. Proceed and omit limitations from the report
   C. Use the tool cautiously only if justified, disclose limitations, and consider more appropriate
alternatives

 D. Translate test items informally and score normally
       Answer: C. Use the tool cautiously only if justified, disclose limitations, and consider more
appropriate alternatives
   Rationale: Assessment must use valid, appropriate tools and disclose significant limitations
when norms or language fit are inadequate.

49. Which term refers to repetitive behaviors or mental acts performed to reduce anxiety or
prevent a feared event?

   A. Delusions
   B. Compulsions
   C. Somatizations

 D. Dissociations
       Answer: B. Compulsions
   Rationale: Compulsions are repetitive acts or mental rituals used to reduce anxiety or prevent
a feared event.

50. A psychometrician notices that another practitioner's conduct may substantially harm a
client. Which is most ethical?

   A. Remain silent because professional courtesy comes first
   B. Report the concern to appropriate authorities when substantial harm is likely, while
respecting confidentiality
   C. Post a warning on social media

 D. Tell the client to sue immediately
       Answer: B. Report the concern to appropriate authorities when substantial harm is likely,
while respecting confidentiality
   Rationale: Ethical standards require further action when substantial harm is likely, while still
observing confidentiality requirements.

51. A man reports recurrent episodes of intense fear with palpitations, shortness of breath,
dizziness, and fear of dying that peak within minutes. Which feature would best distinguish
panic attacks from generalized anxiety?

   A. Panic attacks are always triggered by social situations
   B. Panic attacks involve an abrupt surge of intense fear reaching a peak within minutes
   C. Generalized anxiety always includes depersonalization

 D. Panic attacks occur only in panic disorder
       Answer: B. Panic attacks involve an abrupt surge of intense fear reaching a peak within
minutes
   Rationale: Panic attacks are defined by a sudden, intense surge of fear or discomfort that
peaks within minutes, unlike the more sustained and diffuse worry of generalized anxiety.

52. Which of the following is most characteristic of agoraphobia?
   A. Fear of contamination from dirty objects
   B. Fear of being negatively evaluated in social interactions
   C. Fear of being in situations where escape might be difficult or help unavailable if panic-like

symptoms occur

 D. Fear of thunderstorms and heights
       Answer: C. Fear of being in situations where escape might be difficult or help unavailable
if panic-like symptoms occur
   Rationale: Agoraphobia centers on fear and avoidance of situations where escape may be
hard or help unavailable if panic-like or incapacitating symptoms occur.

53. A woman repeatedly discards valuable possessions because she fears they are
contaminated, but she also becomes distressed when asked to throw away old newspapers and
broken appliances because she believes she might need them later. The latter behavior is most
consistent with:

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Hoarding disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Specific phobia
       Answer: B. Hoarding disorder
   Rationale: Difficulty discarding possessions due to a perceived need to save them is the
hallmark of hoarding disorder.

54. Which disorder is characterized by depersonalization, derealization, or both, with reality
testing remaining intact?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Bipolar I disorder
       Answer: B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: This disorder involves persistent or recurrent depersonalization, derealization, or
both, while reality testing remains intact.

55. A client persistently fabricates symptoms and even tampers with laboratory samples, without
obvious external incentives. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Malingering
   B. Factitious disorder
   C. Conversion disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Factitious disorder
   Rationale: Factitious disorder involves intentional falsification or induction of symptoms
without obvious external rewards.

56. In ethical decision-making, when the code of ethics conflicts with law or governing legal
authority, the practitioner should first:

   A. Ignore the law and follow the code exclusively
   B. Publicly criticize the law before acting
   C. Attempt to resolve the conflict while remaining committed to ethical principles

 D. Stop practicing permanently
       Answer: C. Attempt to resolve the conflict while remaining committed to ethical principles
   Rationale: When ethics and law conflict, the practitioner should first try to resolve the conflict
in a way that honors ethical obligations while complying with governing authority if unresolved.

57. Which is the best example of a specific phobia?
   A. Recurrent worry about grades, health, and finances
   B. Persistent fear of snakes that leads to immediate anxiety and avoidance
   C. Fear that others are plotting against you

 D. Intrusive doubts relieved by checking rituals
       Answer: B. Persistent fear of snakes that leads to immediate anxiety and avoidance
   Rationale: Specific phobia involves marked fear of a specific object or situation with
avoidance or intense distress.

58. A patient presents with a fixed belief that strangers are following him, along with
disorganized speech, flat affect, and marked social decline over 2 years. This presentation is
more consistent with:

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophrenia
   Rationale: The combination of delusions, disorganized speech, negative symptoms, and
long-term social decline strongly supports schizophrenia.

59. Which cognitive theorist proposed the ABC model in which beliefs mediate emotional
consequences?

   A. Albert Ellis
   B. Aaron Beck
   C. Carl Jung

 D. Joseph Wolpe
       Answer: A. Albert Ellis
   Rationale: Ellis proposed the ABC model in rational-emotive behavior therapy, emphasizing
that beliefs mediate emotional consequences.
60. A person drinks alcohol daily and develops tremors, autonomic hyperactivity, anxiety, and
insomnia when attempting to stop. These symptoms most strongly indicate:

   A. Alcohol intoxication
   B. Alcohol withdrawal
   C. Delirium due to Alzheimer's disease

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Alcohol withdrawal
   Rationale: Tremors, autonomic arousal, anxiety, and insomnia after reducing or stopping
alcohol are classic withdrawal signs.

61. Which eating disorder is characterized by recurrent binge eating without regular
compensatory behaviors?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Anorexia nervosa

 D. Rumination disorder
       Answer: B. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder involves recurrent binge eating without regular
compensatory behaviors like purging.

62. A client reports chronic feelings of emptiness, frantic efforts to avoid abandonment, recurrent
self-injury, and unstable intense relationships. Which additional diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: A. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Emptiness, abandonment fears, self-injury, and unstable relationships are central
features of borderline personality disorder.

63. A 6-year-old girl has persistent difficulty acquiring and using language, with reduced
vocabulary and problems in sentence structure, not due to hearing loss or intellectual disability.
The best diagnosis is:

   A. Autism spectrum disorder
   B. Language disorder
   C. Selective mutism

 D. Social anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Language disorder
   Rationale: Persistent impairment in language acquisition and use, including vocabulary and
sentence structure, fits language disorder.

64. Which term refers to the tendency for some disorders to be expressed differently across
cultural contexts while retaining a recognizable underlying syndrome?

   A. Cultural universality
   B. Culture-related diagnostic issues
   C. Random variation

 D. Forensic validity
       Answer: B. Culture-related diagnostic issues
   Rationale: Culture-related diagnostic issues refer to how disorders may vary in expression,
meaning, and presentation across cultural settings.

65. A practitioner accepts gifts of substantial monetary value from a current client and then
agrees to hire the client's sibling for a personal business. This raises primary concern about:

   A. Standardized testing
   B. Multiple relationships and conflict of interest
   C. Classical conditioning

 D. Neurocognitive decline
       Answer: B. Multiple relationships and conflict of interest
   Rationale: Substantial gifts and overlapping personal-business ties can impair objectivity and
risk exploitation.

66. A client persistently lies, steals, destroys property, and has physically harmed animals.
Which childhood diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Aggression, destruction, deceit, and serious violation of norms in childhood point
to conduct disorder.

67. Which symptom is most characteristic of mania rather than hypomania?
   A. Elevated mood with increased productivity for 4 days
   B. Decreased need for sleep without impairment
   C. Severe mood elevation causing marked impairment or hospitalization

 D. Increased talkativeness without psychosis
       Answer: C. Severe mood elevation causing marked impairment or hospitalization
   Rationale: Marked impairment, psychosis, or hospitalization distinguishes mania from
hypomania.

68. A patient has had numerous periods of hypomanic symptoms and depressive symptoms
that never met full episode criteria, lasting for more than 2 years. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Bipolar I disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Cyclothymic disorder
   Rationale: Cyclothymic disorder involves chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive
symptoms that do not meet full episode criteria.

69. Which of the following best describes a delusion?
   A. A recurrent intrusive image recognized as irrational
   B. A false fixed belief not ordinarily accepted by one's culture
   C. A perceptual experience without an external stimulus

 D. A transient misinterpretation of a real stimulus
       Answer: B. A false fixed belief not ordinarily accepted by one's culture
   Rationale: A delusion is a fixed false belief held despite contrary evidence and not better
explained by cultural norms.

70. A hospitalized patient becomes acutely disoriented at night, pulls at IV lines, and sees
insects on the wall. He had been oriented the previous day. Which is the best diagnosis?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Delirium
   C. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features

 D. Dissociative identity disorder
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: The abrupt fluctuation in attention, orientation, and visual misperceptions in a
medically ill patient strongly indicates delirium.

71. A psychometrician is asked to let an untrained school clerk administer a standardized
intelligence test because the office is busy. The most ethical response is:

   A. Allow it if instructions are written clearly
   B. Allow it if the clerk has observed testing before
   C. Do not allow it because assessment by unqualified persons is unethical

 D. Allow it only for screening cases
       Answer: C. Do not allow it because assessment by unqualified persons is unethical
   Rationale: Assessment tasks should not be delegated to unqualified individuals.

72. Which of the following is most associated with observational learning?
   A. Albert Bandura
   B. Ivan Pavlov
   C. Sigmund Freud

 D. Emil Kraepelin
       Answer: A. Albert Bandura
   Rationale: Bandura is most associated with observational learning and social learning theory.

73. A client feels detached from the self, as though observing one's body from outside, during
periods of severe stress. This experience is called:

   A. Derealization
   B. Depersonalization
   C. Delusion
 D. Thought insertion
       Answer: B. Depersonalization
   Rationale: Feeling detached from one's self or body is depersonalization.

74. A woman has a long-standing pattern of social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and
hypersensitivity to criticism, yet she desires relationships. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Dependent personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder involves social inhibition, inadequacy, and
hypersensitivity to criticism despite desire for connection.

75. Which personality disorder is most characterized by pervasive need to be taken care of,
submissive behavior, and fear of separation?

   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: A. Dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Dependent personality disorder is defined by excessive need to be cared for,
submissiveness, and fears of separation.

76. A man repeatedly exposes his genitals to unsuspecting strangers for sexual arousal. The
most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Fetishistic disorder
   B. Voyeuristic disorder
   C. Exhibitionistic disorder

 D. Sexual sadism disorder
       Answer: C. Exhibitionistic disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent sexual arousal from exposing one's genitals to unsuspecting persons
defines exhibitionistic disorder.

77. Which statement best reflects ethical practice in telepsychology?
   A. Ethical rules for face-to-face services do not apply online
   B. Online services are exempt from informed consent
   C. Ethical principles governing face-to-face services also apply to telepsychology

 D. Confidentiality cannot be maintained in online work, so ethics are suspended
       Answer: C. Ethical principles governing face-to-face services also apply to telepsychology
   Rationale: Telepsychology is governed by the same core ethical principles as in-person
practice, including competence, consent, and confidentiality.
78. A 10-year-old with ADHD continues to interrupt others, leave the seat in class, and fail to
complete tasks at home and school. The cross-setting nature of symptoms most directly
supports:

   A. A situational behavior problem only
   B. ADHD diagnosis
   C. Conduct disorder

 D. A specific phobia
       Answer: B. ADHD diagnosis
   Rationale: Symptoms across home and school support the cross-situational requirement for
ADHD.

79. Which is most characteristic of obsessive-compulsive personality disorder?
   A. Recurrent panic attacks
   B. Pervasive perfectionism, rigidity, and control
   C. Identity disturbance and self-harm

 D. Odd beliefs and perceptual distortions
       Answer: B. Pervasive perfectionism, rigidity, and control
   Rationale: Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder is characterized by overcontrol,
orderliness, and perfectionism.

80. A client states, "I washed my hands 40 times today because if I do not, my mother might
die." The repetitive washing is best understood as:

   A. A delusion
   B. A compulsion
   C. A negative symptom

 D. A conversion symptom
       Answer: B. A compulsion
   Rationale: The repetitive washing is a ritual intended to reduce anxiety or prevent a feared
outcome.

81. A person experiences depressed mood, insomnia, and anxiety within 2 months of job loss,
but the symptoms do not meet criteria for another disorder and are clearly linked to the stressor.
The best diagnosis is:

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Adjustment disorder
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: The symptoms arise in response to a clear stressor and do not meet criteria for
another specific disorder.

82. Which historical figure is most associated with describing dementia praecox, later
conceptualized as schizophrenia?

   A. Emil Kraepelin
   B. Jean Charcot
   C. Viktor Frankl

 D. Abraham Maslow
       Answer: A. Emil Kraepelin
   Rationale: Kraepelin described dementia praecox, an early concept related to what became
schizophrenia.

83. A patient has a history of repeated intoxication, risky driving while drunk, failed attempts to
cut down, and continued use despite liver problems. Which severity framework is most
appropriate?

   A. Alcohol use disorder conceptualized on a spectrum of severity
   B. Alcohol intoxication only
   C. Normal recreational drinking

 D. Dissociative disorder
       Answer: A. Alcohol use disorder conceptualized on a spectrum of severity
   Rationale: Substance use disorders are conceptualized dimensionally by severity based on
the number of criteria met.

84. Which of the following is a key feature of narcissistic personality disorder?
   A. Excessive emotionality and attention seeking
   B. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy
   C. Detachment from social relationships

 D. Extreme submissiveness
       Answer: B. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy
   Rationale: These are core features of narcissistic personality disorder.

85. A forensic evaluator must remember that DSM diagnoses:
   A. Directly determine legal conclusions in all cases
   B. Should be used cautiously in forensic settings and do not by themselves answer legal

questions
   C. Are irrelevant in any court-related matter

 D. Automatically establish criminal responsibility
       Answer: B. Should be used cautiously in forensic settings and do not by themselves
answer legal questions
   Rationale: DSM is a clinical diagnostic tool and must be applied cautiously in forensic
contexts; legal standards are not identical to clinical diagnoses.

86. A client complains of severe neurological symptoms that appear intentionally produced, but
the main goal is to obtain opioid medication. This is best classified as:

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Malingering

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: C. Malingering
   Rationale: The apparent intentional symptom production is motivated by a clear external
reward, obtaining opioids.

87. Which term refers to a psychological pattern in which individuals exposed to uncontrollable
aversive events may stop trying to change their situation?

   A. Reciprocal inhibition
   B. Learned helplessness
   C. Self-actualization

 D. Token economy
       Answer: B. Learned helplessness
   Rationale: Learned helplessness describes passivity and reduced problem-solving after
repeated uncontrollable aversive events.

88. A patient with major depressive disorder reports hearing accusatory voices only during
depressive episodes. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Schizoaffective disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   Rationale: The psychotic symptoms occur only during depressive episodes, supporting a
mood disorder with psychotic features rather than schizoaffective disorder.

89. A client seeks therapy from a practitioner who realizes the client is also a close relative of a
current business partner. Ethically, the clinician should primarily consider:

   A. Whether the situation creates a potentially harmful multiple relationship
   B. Whether the client is interesting to work with
   C. Whether the client can pay in cash

 D. Whether the partner approves informally
       Answer: A. Whether the situation creates a potentially harmful multiple relationship
   Rationale: Overlapping personal and professional roles may impair objectivity or risk
exploitation, making multiple relationship analysis central.

90. Which sleep disorder involves difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep despite adequate
opportunity for sleep, with daytime impairment?

   A. Narcolepsy
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Hypersomnolence disorder

 D. Sleep terror disorder
       Answer: B. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Insomnia disorder involves difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep despite
adequate opportunity, along with daytime impairment.
91. A child has repeated aggressive outbursts that are impulsive and disproportionate, but there
is no persistent pattern of violating others' rights between episodes. The best diagnosis is:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Oppositional defiant disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: IED involves impulsive aggressive outbursts that are disproportionate and not part
of a broader ongoing pattern of rights violations.

92. Which is the best definition of hallucination?
   A. A fixed false belief
   B. A misinterpretation of an external stimulus
   C. A sensory perception occurring without external stimulation

 D. A repetitive ritual meant to reduce anxiety
       Answer: C. A sensory perception occurring without external stimulation
   Rationale: Hallucinations are perceptions without an actual external stimulus.

93. A practitioner becomes aware that personal problems are interfering with competent work
performance. The most ethical course is to:

   A. Continue practicing unchanged to preserve income
   B. Take appropriate measures such as consultation, assistance, or limiting duties
   C. Hide the problem from all colleagues

 D. Immediately disclose all personal details to every client
       Answer: B. Take appropriate measures such as consultation, assistance, or limiting duties
   Rationale: Practitioners should address personal problems that impair competence by
seeking help and modifying work responsibilities as needed.

94. A patient has significant decline in memory and executive functioning that interferes with
independent living. The most appropriate broad diagnosis is:

   A. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Substantial cognitive decline interfering with independent functioning indicates
major neurocognitive disorder.

95. Which of the following most clearly differentiates schizotypal personality disorder from
schizophrenia?

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder never includes social anxiety
   B. Schizotypal personality disorder is a personality pattern with odd beliefs and interpersonal
deficits without sustained full psychosis
   C. Schizophrenia always begins in childhood
 D. Schizotypal personality disorder is primarily a mood disorder
       Answer: B. Schizotypal personality disorder is a personality pattern with odd beliefs and
interpersonal deficits without sustained full psychosis
   Rationale: Schizotypal personality disorder involves eccentricity, cognitive-perceptual
distortions, and social deficits, but not sustained schizophrenia-level psychosis.

96. A woman experiences recurrent, moderate depressive episodes every winter with remission
in spring. This specifier is most appropriate:

   A. With seasonal pattern
   B. With catatonia
   C. With rapid cycling

 D. With mixed features
       Answer: A. With seasonal pattern
   Rationale: Recurrent depressive episodes occurring in a seasonal pattern, such as winter
onset and spring remission, fit the seasonal pattern specifier.

97. A psychometrician receives a request from a parent to explain the results of an assessment
conducted for the school. Ethically, explaining assessment results should:

   A. Use language understandable to the recipient
   B. Be limited to technical psychometric language only
   C. Avoid any mention of limitations

 D. Be withheld automatically from all parents
       Answer: A. Use language understandable to the recipient
   Rationale: Ethical communication of assessment results should be clear and understandable
to the intended recipient.

98. Which of the following is the best example of positive reinforcement?
   A. Removing an aversive stimulus after a response
   B. Giving praise after a student completes an exposure exercise
   C. Avoiding a feared situation to reduce anxiety

 D. Ignoring a disruptive behavior until it stops
       Answer: B. Giving praise after a student completes an exposure exercise
   Rationale: Positive reinforcement involves adding a desirable consequence after a behavior
to increase its likelihood.

99. A client reports recurrent urges to set fires deliberately for pleasure and relief of tension,
without monetary or political motive. The most likely diagnosis is:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Pyromania
   C. Obsessive-compulsive disorder

 D. Malingering
       Answer: B. Pyromania
   Rationale: Pyromania involves deliberate fire-setting associated with tension before the act
and pleasure, gratification, or relief afterward, without external motive.
100. A newly licensed psychometrician is offered a role requiring neuropsychological
interpretation far beyond current training. Which response is most ethical and
board-appropriate?

    A. Accept immediately to gain experience
    B. Accept if the employer insists
    C. Decline or work only within lawful supervised boundaries after obtaining proper
competence

 D. Provide interpretations but label them tentative
        Answer: C. Decline or work only within lawful supervised boundaries after obtaining
proper competence
    Rationale: Practitioners must remain within competence and legal scope, and may only
expand responsibly through proper training and lawful supervision.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 9
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 9

1. A clinician begins the diagnostic process by first considering whether the client may be
intentionally producing symptoms for an obvious external gain, such as avoiding criminal liability
or obtaining compensation. Which condition should be ruled out first?

  A. Factitious disorder
  B. Malingering
  C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Malingering
  Rationale: Malingering involves intentional production or exaggeration of symptoms for clear
external gain, which must be ruled out early in differential diagnosis.

2. A patient presents with new-onset visual hallucinations that began during heavy stimulant use
and subside after intoxication resolves. Which is the most appropriate initial diagnostic
consideration?

  A. Schizophrenia
  B. Delusional disorder
  C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: C. Substance/medication-induced psychotic disorder
  Rationale: Psychotic symptoms temporally linked to substance use and resolving with
cessation indicate a substance/medication-induced condition.

3. A 10-year-old child has persistent deficits in social reciprocity, restricted interests, and
repetitive behaviors since early development. Which diagnosis is most consistent with this
presentation?

  A. Social anxiety disorder
  B. Autism spectrum disorder
  C. Reactive attachment disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Autism spectrum disorder
  Rationale: Core features include early-onset social communication deficits and restricted,
repetitive behaviors.

4. Which feature best distinguishes delusions from culturally sanctioned beliefs?
  A. Delusions are always bizarre
  B. Delusions are accompanied by hallucinations
  C. Delusions are idiosyncratic and not ordinarily accepted within the person's cultural context

 D. Delusions occur only in schizophrenia
       Answer: C. Delusions are idiosyncratic and not ordinarily accepted within the person's
cultural context
  Rationale: Cultural context determines whether a belief is considered pathological or
normative.
5. A client reports two weeks of depressed mood, anhedonia, insomnia, guilt, poor
concentration, and suicidal ideation, causing marked impairment. Which diagnosis is most
likely?

  A. Persistent depressive disorder
  B. Major depressive disorder
  C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder
  Rationale: The duration and symptom cluster meet criteria for a major depressive episode.

6. A patient has had a period of abnormally elevated mood, decreased need for sleep,
pressured speech, and increased goal-directed activity lasting 8 days, with marked impairment.
Which diagnosis is most strongly supported?

  A. Bipolar II disorder
  B. Cyclothymic disorder
  C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Bipolar I disorder
  Rationale: A manic episode lasting at least one week with impairment indicates bipolar I
disorder.

7. Which statement best differentiates hypomania from mania?
  A. Hypomania includes psychosis more often
  B. Hypomania lasts longer than mania
  C. Hypomania does not cause marked impairment or require hospitalization

 D. Hypomania includes more severe agitation
       Answer: C. Hypomania does not cause marked impairment or require hospitalization
  Rationale: Hypomania is less severe and lacks marked impairment, hospitalization, or
psychosis.

8. A client experiences sudden surges of intense fear with palpitations, shortness of breath,
trembling, and fear of dying. He then becomes preoccupied about future attacks. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Generalized anxiety disorder
  B. Panic disorder
  C. Specific phobia

 D. Acute stress disorder
       Answer: B. Panic disorder
  Rationale: Recurrent panic attacks with persistent concern about future attacks define panic
disorder.

9. A woman avoids malls, buses, and open public places because she fears being unable to
escape or obtain help if panic-like symptoms occur. Which diagnosis is most likely?
  A. Social anxiety disorder
  B. Specific phobia
  C. Agoraphobia

 D. Separation anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Agoraphobia
  Rationale: Avoidance of multiple situations due to fear of inability to escape or get help is
characteristic of agoraphobia.

10. A college student has excessive and difficult-to-control worry occurring more days than not
for months about finances, academics, and health, accompanied by muscle tension and
restlessness. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Panic disorder
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Chronic, excessive, and uncontrollable worry across multiple domains is central to
GAD.

11. A child becomes mute only in school despite speaking normally at home and with close
family. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Selective mutism
   C. Autism spectrum disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Selective mutism
   Rationale: Selective mutism involves failure to speak in specific settings despite normal
speech in others.

12. Which symptom pair is most central to obsessive-compulsive disorder?
   A. Depressed mood and fatigue
   B. Delusions and hallucinations
   C. Intrusive obsessions and repetitive compulsions

 D. Dissociation and amnesia
       Answer: C. Intrusive obsessions and repetitive compulsions
   Rationale: OCD is defined by intrusive thoughts (obsessions) and repetitive behaviors
(compulsions).

13. A client is preoccupied with a minor perceived defect in facial appearance and repeatedly
checks mirrors and seeks reassurance. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder
   D. Delusional disorder
  Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder

   Rationale: Persistent concern over perceived physical flaws with repetitive behaviors defines
BDD.

14. Which clinical feature most strongly distinguishes hoarding disorder from ordinary
collecting?

   A. Interest in valuable objects only
   B. Inability to discard possessions regardless of actual value, causing clutter and impairment
   C. Preference for neat organization of collections

 D. Collecting only one category of items
       Answer: B. Inability to discard possessions regardless of actual value, causing clutter and
impairment
   Rationale: Hoarding disorder involves difficulty discarding items leading to functional
impairment.

15. Recurrent hair pulling resulting in noticeable hair loss is most consistent with:
   A. Trichotillomania
   B. Excoriation disorder
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: A. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Repetitive hair pulling with hair loss defines trichotillomania.

16. A person develops intrusive memories, hypervigilance, nightmares, and avoidance one
month after a violent assault. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Adjustment disorder
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Posttraumatic stress disorder

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: C. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   Rationale: Trauma-related symptoms lasting over one month indicate PTSD.

17. A client develops anxiety, intrusive memories, and dissociative symptoms 3 days after a
serious accident. Symptoms have lasted 10 days. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Acute stress disorder
   B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   C. Panic disorder

 D. Dissociative identity disorder
       Answer: A. Acute stress disorder
   Rationale: Trauma-related symptoms lasting between 3 days and 1 month define acute stress
disorder.

18. Which feature best characterizes adjustment disorder?
   A. Symptoms always meet criteria for another specific disorder
   B. Emotional or behavioral symptoms occur in response to an identifiable stressor and are
out of proportion to the stressor

   C. It is always chronic for more than two years

 D. It necessarily includes psychosis
       Answer: B. Emotional or behavioral symptoms occur in response to an identifiable
stressor and are out of proportion to the stressor
   Rationale: Adjustment disorder involves disproportionate distress following an identifiable
stressor.

19. A patient has multiple distressing physical symptoms and devotes excessive time and
energy to health concerns. Medical findings do not fully explain the distress. Which diagnosis is
most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Factitious disorder

 D. Conversion disorder
       Answer: B. Somatic symptom disorder
   Rationale: Multiple somatic symptoms with excessive concern characterize somatic symptom
disorder.

20. A patient has minimal somatic symptoms but intense fear of having a serious illness and
repeatedly seeks reassurance despite negative workups. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Illness anxiety disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Preoccupation with illness despite minimal symptoms defines illness anxiety
disorder.

21. Sudden neurologic-like weakness after severe conflict, without compatible medical findings,
is most consistent with:

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Malingering

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Conversion disorder involves neurologic-like motor or sensory symptoms that are
incompatible with recognized medical conditions and are not better explained by intentional
feigning.

22. Which feature best differentiates factitious disorder from malingering?
   A. Factitious disorder involves obvious external rewards
   B. Malingering occurs only in medical settings
   C. Factitious disorder involves deception without clear external incentives

 D. Malingering is an official mental disorder diagnosis in all cases
       Answer: C. Factitious disorder involves deception without clear external incentives
   Rationale: Factitious disorder is characterized by falsification or induction of symptoms
without obvious external gain, unlike malingering, which is motivated by external incentives.

23. Recurrent episodes of inability to recall important autobiographical information, usually of a
traumatic nature, are most consistent with:

   A. Dissociative amnesia
   B. Delirium
   C. Major neurocognitive disorder

 D. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
       Answer: A. Dissociative amnesia
   Rationale: Dissociative amnesia specifically involves inability to recall important personal
information, often related to trauma or stress, beyond ordinary forgetting.

24. A client reports feeling detached from her body and as if the world is unreal, while reality
testing remains intact. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Psychotic disorder
   B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   C. Dissociative identity disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: This disorder involves persistent or recurrent experiences of detachment from self
or surroundings while the person still knows these experiences are not literally real.

25. Which feature is most characteristic of dissociative identity disorder?
   A. Persistent cognitive decline due to neurodegeneration
   B. Two or more distinct personality states with discontinuity in sense of self
   C. Delusions of control only

 D. Fear of social scrutiny
       Answer: B. Two or more distinct personality states with discontinuity in sense of self
   Rationale: Dissociative identity disorder is defined by identity disruption involving two or more
distinct personality states and marked discontinuity in sense of self.

26. Which diagnosis is characterized by restriction of energy intake leading to significantly low
body weight, intense fear of gaining weight, and disturbance in body image?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Anorexia nervosa

 D. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: C. Anorexia nervosa
   Rationale: Anorexia nervosa is marked by significantly low body weight, persistent fear of
weight gain, and distorted evaluation of body shape or weight.
27. Recurrent binge eating followed by self-induced vomiting or laxative misuse is most
consistent with:

   A. Binge-eating disorder
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Anorexia nervosa, restricting type

 D. Pica
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Bulimia nervosa involves recurrent binge eating episodes followed by
compensatory behaviors such as vomiting or laxative misuse to prevent weight gain.

28. Recurrent binge eating without regular compensatory behavior is most consistent with:
   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Binge-eating disorder
   C. Rumination disorder

 D. Anorexia nervosa
       Answer: B. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder is defined by recurrent binge eating accompanied by
distress but without regular compensatory behaviors.

29. A child shows persistent failure to meet nutritional needs due to avoidance of food based on
sensory characteristics, without body image disturbance. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   B. Anorexia nervosa
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: A. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   Rationale: ARFID involves restricted intake leading to nutritional problems without the weight
and shape concerns seen in anorexia nervosa.

30. Difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep despite adequate opportunity, with daytime
impairment, is most consistent with:

   A. Hypersomnolence disorder
   B. Insomnia disorder
   C. Narcolepsy

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Insomnia disorder involves persistent difficulty falling asleep, staying asleep, or
getting restorative sleep despite adequate opportunity, with significant daytime consequences.

31. Excessive sleepiness despite a main sleep period of at least 7 hours is most consistent with:
   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Nightmare disorder
 D. Delirium
       Answer: B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   Rationale: Hypersomnolence disorder is characterized by excessive sleepiness despite
apparently sufficient sleep duration.

32. A male client has marked delay in ejaculation during partnered sexual activity, causing
distress. Which category does this belong to?

   A. Gender dysphoria
   B. Sexual dysfunction
   C. Paraphilic disorder

 D. Personality disorder
       Answer: B. Sexual dysfunction
   Rationale: Delayed ejaculation is classified as a sexual dysfunction because it involves
impairment in normal sexual response causing distress.

33. Which feature best differentiates a paraphilic disorder from an atypical sexual interest
alone?

   A. Any unusual sexual preference automatically qualifies as a disorder
   B. The atypical interest must involve distress, impairment, or harm/risk of harm to others
   C. The person must be male

 D. The interest must be lifelong
       Answer: B. The atypical interest must involve distress, impairment, or harm/risk of harm to
others
   Rationale: Atypical sexual interests alone are not sufficient for diagnosis; they become
paraphilic disorders when they cause significant distress, impairment, or harm/risk to others.

34. Clinically significant distress due to incongruence between experienced gender and
assigned gender is most consistent with:

   A. Sexual masochism disorder
   B. Gender dysphoria
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Histrionic personality disorder
       Answer: B. Gender dysphoria
   Rationale: Gender dysphoria is defined by distress or impairment related to incongruence
between experienced gender and assigned gender.

35. Recurrent verbal outbursts and physical aggression grossly out of proportion to provocation
are most consistent with:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Antisocial personality disorder
       Answer: C. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: Intermittent explosive disorder involves recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts
that are disproportionate to the provocation.

36. A child frequently loses temper, argues with authority figures, and is spiteful, but has not
engaged in serious aggression toward people or animals. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   Rationale: Oppositional defiant disorder is characterized by angry/irritable mood,
argumentative/defiant behavior, and vindictiveness without the more severe rule violations of
conduct disorder.

37. Repetitive violation of others' rights through aggression, deceitfulness, property destruction,
and serious rule violations is most consistent with:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. ADHD

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: A. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Conduct disorder involves a persistent pattern of behavior violating others' rights
and major age-appropriate social norms.

38. Which diagnosis requires the person to be at least 18 years old and to have evidence of
conduct disorder before age 15?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Intermittent explosive disorder
       Answer: C. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Antisocial personality disorder requires age 18 or older and a prior history of
conduct disorder symptoms before age 15.
