39. Persistent pattern of disregard for and violation of the rights of others, with deceitfulness,
impulsivity, and lack of remorse, is most characteristic of:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Schizotypal personality disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
       Answer: B. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: Antisocial personality disorder is defined by chronic disregard for others' rights,
deceit, impulsivity, irresponsibility, and lack of remorse.
40. Instability in relationships, self-image, affect, and marked impulsivity is most characteristic
of:

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Histrionic personality disorder
   C. Dependent personality disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: A. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Borderline personality disorder is marked by pervasive instability in interpersonal
relationships, identity, affect regulation, and impulse control.

41. Excessive emotionality and attention seeking are most characteristic of:
   A. Narcissistic personality disorder
   B. Histrionic personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Histrionic personality disorder is defined by excessive emotionality, suggestibility,
and a strong need to be the center of attention.

42. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy are most characteristic of:
   A. Narcissistic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: A. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Narcissistic personality disorder involves grandiosity, entitlement, and diminished
empathy toward others.

43. Social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy, and hypersensitivity to criticism are most
characteristic of:

   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: B. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Avoidant personality disorder is marked by social inhibition and fear of criticism
despite a desire for relationships.

44. Excessive need to be taken care of, leading to submissive and clinging behavior, is most
characteristic of:

   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Borderline personality disorder
 D. Histrionic personality disorder
       Answer: A. Dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Dependent personality disorder involves excessive reliance on others for
emotional and decision-making support.

45. Preoccupation with orderliness, perfectionism, and control at the expense of flexibility is
most characteristic of:

   A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. Hoarding disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   Rationale: OCPD involves rigid perfectionism and control that interferes with efficiency and
flexibility.

46. Detachment from social relationships and restricted emotional expression are most
characteristic of:

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizoid personality disorder features emotional detachment and lack of desire for
close relationships.

47. Cognitive or perceptual distortions and eccentric behavior with interpersonal deficits are
most characteristic of:

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Paranoid personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Schizotypal personality disorder includes eccentric behavior and unusual beliefs or
perceptual experiences.

48. Pervasive distrust and suspiciousness such that others' motives are interpreted as
malevolent are most characteristic of:

   A. Paranoid personality disorder
   B. Schizotypal personality disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Paranoid personality disorder is defined by persistent distrust and suspicion of
others.
49. Delusions, hallucinations, disorganized speech, grossly disorganized or catatonic behavior,
and negative symptoms are classically associated with:

   A. Schizophrenia spectrum disorders
   B. Dissociative disorders
   C. Somatic symptom disorders

 D. Anxiety disorders
       Answer: A. Schizophrenia spectrum disorders
   Rationale: These symptom domains define schizophrenia spectrum and other psychotic
disorders.

50. Continuous signs of disturbance for at least 6 months, with at least 1 month of active-phase
psychotic symptoms, most strongly support:

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Schizophrenia
   Rationale: Schizophrenia requires at least 6 months of disturbance including 1 month of
active symptoms.

51. Schizophreniform disorder differs from schizophrenia primarily in:
   A. Presence of negative symptoms
   B. Duration of illness
   C. Presence of hallucinations

 D. Need for hospitalization
       Answer: B. Duration of illness
   Rationale: Schizophreniform disorder has similar symptoms but lasts less than 6 months.

52. One or more delusions lasting at least one month with relatively preserved functioning
outside the impact of the delusion is most consistent with:

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Brief psychotic disorder
   C. Schizoaffective disorder

 D. Schizophreniform disorder
       Answer: A. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: Delusional disorder involves persistent delusions with relatively preserved
functioning.

53. Psychotic symptoms lasting more than 1 day but less than 1 month, with eventual full return
to premorbid functioning, are most consistent with:

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Delusional disorder
   C. Schizophrenia
 D. Bipolar I disorder
       Answer: A. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Brief psychotic disorder is defined by short duration and full recovery.

54. An uninterrupted period of illness during which there is a major mood episode concurrent
with schizophrenia symptoms, plus delusions or hallucinations for at least 2 weeks without
mood symptoms, most strongly suggests:

   A. Bipolar I disorder with psychotic features
   B. Schizoaffective disorder
   C. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Schizoaffective disorder
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires psychotic symptoms independent of mood
episodes.

55. Which symptom is considered a negative symptom of schizophrenia?
   A. Hallucinations
   B. Delusions
   C. Avolition

 D. Flight of ideas
       Answer: C. Avolition
   Rationale: Avolition reflects decreased motivation and is a core negative symptom.

56. A fluctuating disturbance in attention and awareness that develops over a short period and
is caused by a medical condition is most consistent with:

   A. Delirium
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Dissociative amnesia

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: A. Delirium
   Rationale: Delirium is characterized by acute onset and fluctuating attention and awareness.

57. Significant decline in one or more cognitive domains that interferes with independence is
most consistent with:

   A. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
       Answer: B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Major neurocognitive disorder involves substantial cognitive decline affecting
independence.

58. Modest cognitive decline that does not interfere with capacity for independence is most
consistent with:
   A. Delirium
   B. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   C. Major neurocognitive disorder

 D. Dissociative disorder
       Answer: B. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Mild neurocognitive disorder involves cognitive decline without loss of
independence.

59. A child persistently fails to give close attention to details, is easily distracted, and often loses
things across settings. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Specific learning disorder
   B. Attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   C. Oppositional defiant disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder
   Rationale: ADHD includes persistent inattention symptoms across settings that impair
functioning.

60. Which diagnosis involves persistent difficulties in reading, writing, or mathematics despite
targeted intervention and adequate opportunity to learn?

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. ADHD
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: C. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Specific learning disorder involves persistent academic skill deficits despite
adequate instruction.

61. Deficits in intellectual functions and adaptive functioning with onset during the
developmental period are most consistent with:

   A. Specific learning disorder
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. Intellectual disability

 D. ADHD
       Answer: C. Intellectual disability
   Rationale: Intellectual disability requires impairments in both intellectual functioning and
adaptive functioning beginning during development.

62. Multiple motor tics and at least one vocal tic present for more than one year are most
consistent with:

   A. Stereotypic movement disorder
   B. Provisional tic disorder
   C. Tourette's disorder
   D. Functional neurological symptom disorder
  Answer: C. Tourette's disorder

   Rationale: Tourette's disorder is defined by both motor and vocal tics persisting for more than
one year.

63. Which presentation most strongly suggests separation anxiety disorder?
   A. Fear of public embarrassment in social situations
   B. Persistent fear or anxiety concerning separation from attachment figures
   C. Fear of contamination

 D. Fear of enclosed spaces only
       Answer: B. Persistent fear or anxiety concerning separation from attachment figures
   Rationale: Separation anxiety disorder centers on excessive fear or anxiety about separation
from attachment figures.

64. Which of the following most strongly suggests social anxiety disorder rather than panic
disorder?

   A. Unexpected panic attacks during sleep
   B. Fear of negative evaluation in social or performance situations
   C. Excessive worry about many domains

 D. Intrusive unwanted thoughts
       Answer: B. Fear of negative evaluation in social or performance situations
   Rationale: Social anxiety disorder specifically involves fear of scrutiny and negative
evaluation by others.

65. A person fears flying specifically because of possible crashing, but functions well otherwise.
Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Generalized anxiety disorder
   B. Agoraphobia
   C. Specific phobia

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: C. Specific phobia
   Rationale: Specific phobia involves marked fear of a specific object or situation such as flying.

66. Which diagnosis is characterized by chronic fluctuating periods of hypomanic symptoms and
depressive symptoms that do not meet full episode criteria for at least 2 years?

   A. Bipolar I disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Cyclothymic disorder
   Rationale: Cyclothymic disorder involves long-term subthreshold mood fluctuations.

67. A person has been depressed most of the day, more days than not, for at least 2 years, but
never met criteria for mania. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Persistent depressive disorder
   C. Major depressive disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
   Rationale: Persistent depressive disorder involves chronic depressed mood for at least two
years without manic episodes.

68. Which feature best differentiates bereavement from major depressive disorder in a
diagnostic assessment?

   A. Bereavement never includes sadness
   B. Major depressive disorder is impossible after loss
   C. Assessment should consider duration, severity, functional impairment, hopelessness, and
associated syndrome rather than assuming all grief is normal or pathological

 D. Bereavement always includes psychosis
       Answer: C. Assessment should consider duration, severity, functional impairment,
hopelessness, and associated syndrome rather than assuming all grief is normal or pathological
   Rationale: Careful clinical evaluation is required to distinguish normal grief from major
depressive disorder.

69. The tendency for several disorders to occur in the same individual is referred to as:
   A. Catatonia
   B. Comorbidity
   C. Conversion

 D. Somatization
       Answer: B. Comorbidity
   Rationale: Comorbidity refers to the co-occurrence of multiple disorders in the same
individual.

70. In differential diagnosis, what is a major reason substance etiology must be considered
early?

   A. Substance-related explanations are rare in clinical practice
   B. Missing a substance cause can lead to incorrect diagnosis and inappropriate treatment
   C. Substances only cause mood symptoms

 D. DSM prohibits diagnosing primary disorders in people who use substances
       Answer: B. Missing a substance cause can lead to incorrect diagnosis and inappropriate
treatment
   Rationale: Substance effects can mimic psychiatric disorders, leading to misdiagnosis if not
ruled out early.

71. According to ethical principles for psychologists and psychometricians, which action best
reflects maintaining boundaries of competence?

   A. Offering any service requested as long as the client agrees
   B. Practicing only within areas supported by education, training, supervised experience,
consultation, or professional experience
   C. Refusing all emergency services

 D. Delegating all testing to untrained staff
       Answer: B. Practicing only within areas supported by education, training, supervised
experience, consultation, or professional experience
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires professionals to work within their established
competencies.

72. Which ethical principle is most directly involved when a practitioner avoids exploiting a client
for personal, professional, or financial gain?

   A. Integrity
   B. Justice only
   C. Autonomy only

 D. Utility only
       Answer: A. Integrity
   Rationale: Integrity involves honesty and avoidance of exploitation or conflicts of interest.

73. A psychologist is asked by a school administrator to assess a student. The parents assume
the school will receive the full report. Ethically, the psychologist should first:

   A. Send results directly to the school without discussion
   B. Clarify roles, probable uses of information, and limits of confidentiality with all involved
parties
   C. Refuse the case automatically

 D. Give the child the raw test scores only
       Answer: B. Clarify roles, probable uses of information, and limits of confidentiality with all
involved parties
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires clear explanation of roles and confidentiality in third-party
situations.

74. A practitioner recognizes that fatigue and unresolved personal distress are affecting
judgment in sessions. What is the most ethical response?

   A. Continue practicing without change because clients need continuity
   B. Ignore the problem unless clients complain
   C. Obtain consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or terminate
affected duties

 D. Transfer all clients immediately without explanation
       Answer: C. Obtain consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or
terminate affected duties
   Rationale: Practitioners must address personal issues that impair professional functioning.

75. Which action is most consistent with the ethical requirement to maintain confidentiality?
   A. Sharing case material casually with friends for support
   B. Disclosing identifying information whenever a colleague is curious
   C. Protecting client information and disclosing only with proper consent or recognized

legal/ethical justification
 D. Posting anonymized-looking but recognizable case details on social media
       Answer: C. Protecting client information and disclosing only with proper consent or
recognized legal/ethical justification
   Rationale: Confidentiality requires safeguarding information and limiting disclosure to
appropriate circumstances.

76. Which situation most clearly reflects a potentially harmful multiple relationship?
   A. A clinician attends a public seminar with a former classmate
   B. A therapist enters a business partnership with a current client
   C. A psychologist consults a peer about a difficult case while protecting confidentiality

 D. A psychometrician refers a client to a physician
       Answer: B. A therapist enters a business partnership with a current client
   Rationale: Dual relationships can impair objectivity and increase risk of exploitation.

77. Under ethical standards, delegated work should be assigned only to persons who:
   A. Are available, regardless of training
   B. Can be expected to perform competently based on education, training, or experience, with

appropriate supervision if needed
   C. Promise to do their best

 D. Have known the practitioner for many years
       Answer: B. Can be expected to perform competently based on education, training, or
experience, with appropriate supervision if needed
   Rationale: Delegation must consider competence and proper supervision.

78. In an emergency where no qualified specialist is immediately available, a psychology
practitioner may ethically:

   A. Provide cautious, limited emergency assistance and discontinue when the emergency
ends or appropriate services become available

   B. Offer long-term services indefinitely outside competence
   C. Ignore the emergency to avoid liability

 D. Use experimental procedures without consent
       Answer: A. Provide cautious, limited emergency assistance and discontinue when the
emergency ends or appropriate services become available
   Rationale: Ethical standards allow limited emergency intervention when necessary.

79. Which conduct best reflects informed consent in assessment or therapy?
   A. Using technical language so clients appreciate the practitioner's expertise
   B. Obtaining consent in reasonably understandable language, including relevant limits and

conditions
   C. Avoiding discussion of risks or alternatives

 D. Relying only on implied consent in all situations
       Answer: B. Obtaining consent in reasonably understandable language, including relevant
limits and conditions
   Rationale: Informed consent requires clear, understandable explanation of services and
conditions.

80. A practitioner becomes aware that another professional has likely committed a serious
ethical violation that may substantially harm clients. What is the most appropriate action?

   A. Gossip about the matter with colleagues
   B. Take further action by reporting to appropriate authorities when informal resolution is
insufficient and confidentiality rights are not violated
   C. Ignore it because professionals protect one another

 D. Post the allegation online
       Answer: B. Take further action by reporting to appropriate authorities when informal
resolution is insufficient and confidentiality rights are not violated
   Rationale: Ethical responsibility includes reporting serious violations to protect clients when
appropriate.

81. Republic Act No. 10029 is most directly relevant to psychometric practice because it:
   A. Abolished licensure in psychology
   B. Regulates the professional practice of psychology and psychometrics in the Philippines
   C. Applies only to physicians

 D. Eliminated ethical requirements for assessment
       Answer: B. Regulates the professional practice of psychology and psychometrics in the
Philippines
   Rationale: RA 10029 provides the legal framework governing licensure, scope of practice,
and regulation of psychology and psychometrics in the Philippines.

82. In relation to RA 10029, a psychometrician should be most careful about which activity?
   A. Administering and scoring tests within lawful and ethical boundaries
   B. Independently presenting oneself as authorized to perform functions beyond legal scope
   C. Protecting test materials

 D. Observing confidentiality
       Answer: B. Independently presenting oneself as authorized to perform functions beyond
legal scope
   Rationale: Practicing beyond legal scope violates RA 10029 and professional ethics.

83. A psychometrician is asked to interpret highly complex forensic findings beyond his
documented competence and legal scope. The best response is to:

   A. Accept because experience can be improvised
   B. Decline or refer, and work only within legal scope and competence
   C. Provide the report but omit the signature

 D. Ask the client to waive all complaints
       Answer: B. Decline or refer, and work only within legal scope and competence
   Rationale: Ethical and legal standards require practitioners to work within their competence
and scope.
84. Which practice is most consistent with ethical test security and professional conduct?
   A. Publicly posting secure test items online for transparency
   B. Giving raw test materials to unqualified persons on request
   C. Safeguarding test materials, administering them properly, and limiting access to qualified

persons

 D. Letting untrained assistants improvise administration procedures
       Answer: C. Safeguarding test materials, administering them properly, and limiting access
to qualified persons
   Rationale: Ethical testing requires protection of test materials and proper administration by
qualified individuals.

85. A teacher asks a psychometrician to send a student's test results through an unsecured
group chat. The best response is to:

   A. Send immediately because it is convenient
   B. Decline and use a secure, ethically appropriate method that protects confidentiality
   C. Post only the final diagnosis in the group chat

 D. Ask another teacher to send it instead
       Answer: B. Decline and use a secure, ethically appropriate method that protects
confidentiality
   Rationale: Confidential information must be transmitted through secure channels to protect
client privacy.

86. A supervisee is asked to conduct an unfamiliar assessment procedure for the first time.
Ethically, the supervisor should:

   A. Allow independent administration without oversight
   B. Ensure training and appropriate supervision before delegation
   C. Tell the supervisee to watch online videos only

 D. Skip consent because it is for training purposes
       Answer: B. Ensure training and appropriate supervision before delegation
   Rationale: Supervisors must ensure competence and provide adequate supervision before
assigning tasks.

87. Which psychologist is most closely associated with psychoanalytic theory?
   A. B. F. Skinner
   B. Sigmund Freud
   C. Aaron Beck

 D. Ivan Pavlov
       Answer: B. Sigmund Freud
   Rationale: Freud developed psychoanalytic theory focusing on unconscious processes and
early experiences.

88. Which figure is most strongly associated with classical conditioning?
   A. Carl Rogers
   B. Ivan Pavlov
   C. Albert Ellis

 D. Jean Piaget
       Answer: B. Ivan Pavlov
   Rationale: Pavlov demonstrated classical conditioning through associative learning
experiments.

89. Which psychologist is most closely associated with operant conditioning?
   A. B. F. Skinner
   B. Alfred Adler
   C. Carl Jung

 D. Noam Chomsky
       Answer: A. B. F. Skinner
   Rationale: Skinner developed operant conditioning, emphasizing reinforcement and
punishment in behavior.

90. Which theorist is most strongly associated with the cognitive model emphasizing
maladaptive automatic thoughts in depression?

   A. Aaron Beck
   B. Sigmund Freud
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. John Watson
       Answer: A. Aaron Beck
   Rationale: Beck's cognitive theory highlights negative automatic thoughts and cognitive
distortions in depression.

91. Which pioneer is most associated with client-centered or person-centered therapy?
   A. Carl Rogers
   B. Albert Bandura
   C. Emil Kraepelin

 D. Joseph Wolpe
       Answer: A. Carl Rogers
   Rationale: Rogers developed person-centered therapy emphasizing empathy and
unconditional positive regard.

92. Emil Kraepelin is especially remembered for his contribution to:
   A. Systematic classification of mental disorders
   B. Classical conditioning of fear
   C. Client-centered therapy

 D. Token economy
       Answer: A. Systematic classification of mental disorders
   Rationale: Kraepelin is known for organizing mental disorders into systematic diagnostic
categories.

93. Which concept is most closely associated with Albert Bandura?
   A. Free association
   B. Social learning through modeling
   C. Dream interpretation

 D. Electroconvulsive therapy
       Answer: B. Social learning through modeling
   Rationale: Bandura emphasized observational learning and modeling in behavior acquisition.

94. Joseph Wolpe is most closely associated with:
   A. Systematic desensitization
   B. Moral therapy
   C. Electroconvulsive therapy

 D. Dream analysis
       Answer: A. Systematic desensitization
   Rationale: Wolpe developed systematic desensitization for treating anxiety through gradual
exposure.

95. A patient with severe depression says, "Nothing will ever improve; I fail at everything." This
statement most directly reflects which cognitive feature?

   A. Loose associations
   B. Cognitive distortion involving overgeneralization and hopeless automatic thinking
   C. Thought insertion

 D. Confabulation
       Answer: B. Cognitive distortion involving overgeneralization and hopeless automatic
thinking
   Rationale: The statement reflects negative automatic thoughts and overgeneralization typical
in cognitive models of depression.

96. Which feature most strongly suggests a diagnosis of delirium rather than schizophrenia in
an older adult with acute confusion?

   A. Presence of hallucinations
   B. Chronic social withdrawal
   C. Fluctuating attention and awareness with sudden onset

 D. Flat affect
       Answer: C. Fluctuating attention and awareness with sudden onset
   Rationale: Delirium is characterized by acute onset and fluctuating levels of consciousness
and attention.

97. A patient hears accusatory voices only during a severe depressive episode and has no
psychotic symptoms outside the episode. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Schizoaffective disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   Rationale: Psychotic symptoms occurring exclusively during mood episodes indicate mood
disorder with psychotic features.

98. A client presents with low mood after job loss. Symptoms began within one month, do not
meet full criteria for major depressive disorder, and cause distress and impaired functioning.
Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood
   Rationale: Symptoms are linked to a stressor and do not meet full criteria for major
depressive disorder.

99. A forensic evaluator notices clear external incentives for symptom exaggeration, including
compensation claims and avoidance of prosecution. Which formulation is most appropriate to
consider first?

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Malingering
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: B. Malingering
   Rationale: External incentives strongly suggest malingering.

100. A clinician assessing a complex case uses a structured approach that rules out feigning,
substances, medical causes, primary disorders, stress-related residual categories, and finally
considers whether no mental disorder is present. This approach best reflects:

    A. A purely psychoanalytic assessment
    B. A differential diagnosis framework
    C. A projective testing procedure

 D. A behavioral activation protocol
        Answer: B. A differential diagnosis framework
    Rationale: Systematic elimination of alternative explanations reflects a structured differential
diagnosis process.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 10
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 10

1. A 23-year-old woman reports that for the past 7 months she has worried excessively about
her grades, her parents' health, and minor mistakes at work. She finds it difficult to control the
worry and reports muscle tension, irritability, and poor sleep. Which diagnosis is most consistent
with the presentation?

  A. Panic disorder
  B. Generalized anxiety disorder
  C. Adjustment disorder with anxiety

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Generalized anxiety disorder
  Rationale: The presentation involves excessive, difficult-to-control worry across multiple
domains for more than 6 months accompanied by physical and cognitive symptoms such as
muscle tension and sleep disturbance, which defines generalized anxiety disorder.

2. A client says he has sudden attacks of intense fear accompanied by palpitations, dizziness,
trembling, and fear of dying. He has begun avoiding buses, malls, and bridges because escape
may be difficult if another attack occurs. Which diagnosis best accounts for both the attacks and
the avoidance?

  A. Specific phobia
  B. Social anxiety disorder
  C. Panic disorder with agoraphobia

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Panic disorder with agoraphobia
  Rationale: The combination of recurrent panic attacks and avoidance of situations due to fear
of difficulty escaping or getting help is characteristic of panic disorder with agoraphobic
avoidance.

3. A 9-year-old child speaks freely at home but remains silent in school despite understanding
the language used there. This pattern has persisted for several months and interferes with
classroom participation. Which diagnosis is most likely?

  A. Autism spectrum disorder
  B. Social anxiety disorder
  C. Selective mutism

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: C. Selective mutism
  Rationale: The consistent failure to speak in specific social settings despite speaking in
others, with functional impairment, is the hallmark of selective mutism.

4. A college student experiences intense fear only when required to speak in front of the class
because she believes others will judge her negatively. She is otherwise socially comfortable with
close friends. Which diagnosis is most appropriate?

  A. Agoraphobia
  B. Social anxiety disorder
  C. Panic disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: B. Social anxiety disorder
  Rationale: The fear is specific to situations involving possible negative evaluation, particularly
performance situations, which is characteristic of social anxiety disorder.

5. A man avoids dogs because he becomes immediately fearful on seeing one, even when he
knows the dog is harmless. His fear is persistent, excessive, and restricted to that object. Which
diagnosis is most consistent?

  A. Specific phobia
  B. Generalized anxiety disorder
  C. Separation anxiety disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: A. Specific phobia
  Rationale: The excessive, persistent fear triggered by a specific object and resulting in
avoidance is characteristic of specific phobia.

6. A 34-year-old repeatedly checks whether the stove is off for over 2 hours each night because
he fears causing a fire. He recognizes the behavior is excessive but feels unable to resist.
Which feature best distinguishes this condition from generalized worry?

  A. Symptoms are always ego-syntonic
  B. The fear is limited to social humiliation
  C. Repetitive compulsive rituals are present

 D. Insight is absent in all cases
       Answer: C. Repetitive compulsive rituals are present
  Rationale: The presence of repetitive behaviors performed to reduce anxiety distinguishes
obsessive-compulsive disorder from generalized anxiety.

7. A woman is preoccupied with the belief that her nose is deformed despite minimal observable
irregularity. She repeatedly checks mirrors and seeks cosmetic procedures. Which diagnosis is
most likely?

  A. Somatic symptom disorder
  B. Illness anxiety disorder
  C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Delusional disorder, grandiose type
       Answer: C. Body dysmorphic disorder
  Rationale: Preoccupation with perceived defects in appearance along with repetitive checking
behaviors is characteristic of body dysmorphic disorder.

8. A patient persistently has difficulty discarding old newspapers, broken appliances, and empty
containers because she feels a need to save them. Her apartment has become unusable.
Which diagnosis is most appropriate?

  A. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
  B. Hoarding disorder
  C. Major neurocognitive disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Hoarding disorder
  Rationale: Persistent difficulty discarding possessions regardless of value leading to clutter
and impairment is diagnostic of hoarding disorder.

9. A teenager repeatedly pulls out her hair when tense and feels relief afterward. She has
noticeable hair loss and has tried unsuccessfully to stop. Which diagnosis best fits?

  A. Excoriation disorder
  B. Trichotillomania
  C. Tic disorder

 D. Nonsuicidal self-injury
       Answer: B. Trichotillomania
  Rationale: Recurrent hair pulling with attempts to stop and associated tension and relief is
characteristic of trichotillomania.

10. A man repeatedly picks at minor skin irregularities until lesions develop. He spends
considerable time doing this and feels increasing tension before the act. Which diagnosis is
most likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Factitious disorder
   C. Excoriation disorder

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: C. Excoriation disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent skin picking resulting in lesions and distress defines excoriation
disorder.

11. A survivor of a typhoon has intrusive memories, nightmares, exaggerated startle response,
and avoidance of reminders for 3 weeks after the event. Which diagnosis is most appropriate?

   A. Adjustment disorder
   B. Acute stress disorder
   C. Posttraumatic stress disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Acute stress disorder
   Rationale: Trauma-related symptoms lasting less than one month are consistent with acute
stress disorder.

12. A woman continues to experience intrusive recollections, emotional numbing,
hypervigilance, and avoidance 5 months after a violent assault. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Acute stress disorder
   B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   C. Panic disorder

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Posttraumatic stress disorder
   Rationale: Persistent trauma-related symptoms beyond one month support a diagnosis of
PTSD.

13. A employee develops low mood and anxiety 1 month after job loss. The symptoms cause
distress but do not meet full criteria for a depressive or anxiety disorder and are clearly linked to
the stressor. Which diagnosis is most fitting?

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. Persistent depressive disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: C. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: Emotional or behavioral symptoms in response to an identifiable stressor that do
not meet criteria for another disorder define adjustment disorder.

14. A client presents with paralysis of one arm after a heated family conflict. Neurological
evaluation does not support a medical explanation, and the symptom is incompatible with
recognized neurological disease. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Conversion disorder

 D. Factitious disorder imposed on self
       Answer: C. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Neurological symptoms incompatible with medical findings following psychological
stress indicate conversion disorder.

15. A man repeatedly seeks medical consultation for fears of having cancer despite minimal
symptoms and repeated reassurance. His main problem is fear of illness rather than distress
about actual symptoms. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Panic disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: A. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Preoccupation with having a serious illness despite minimal symptoms and
reassurance is characteristic of illness anxiety disorder.

16. A patient reports chronic pain and gastrointestinal discomfort. She spends much of the day
catastrophizing these symptoms and frequently seeks reassurance, although the medical
findings are limited. Which diagnosis best fits?

   A. Conversion disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Factitious disorder
       Answer: B. Somatic symptom disorder
   Rationale: Excessive thoughts, feelings, or behaviors related to distressing physical
symptoms define somatic symptom disorder.

17. A woman intentionally contaminates her urine sample so that she will be admitted for further
treatment and receive attention from medical staff, but there is no obvious external gain. Which
diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Malingering
   B. Factitious disorder imposed on self
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Factitious disorder imposed on self
   Rationale: Intentional falsification of symptoms without external reward to assume a sick role
is characteristic of factitious disorder.

18. A defendant exaggerates auditory hallucinations during a court-ordered evaluation in hopes
of being found unfit to stand trial. Which is the best classification?

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Malingering

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: C. Malingering
   Rationale: Intentional exaggeration of symptoms for external gain such as avoiding legal
consequences defines malingering.

19. A woman cannot recall important autobiographical information surrounding a traumatic
event, but there is no evidence of a neurological disorder. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Dissociative identity disorder
   B. Dissociative amnesia
   C. Delirium

 D. Posttraumatic stress disorder
       Answer: B. Dissociative amnesia
   Rationale: Inability to recall important personal information, usually trauma-related, without
neurological cause defines dissociative amnesia.

20. A man says, "Sometimes I feel detached from myself, as if I am observing my life from
outside my body, and the world looks unreal." Reality testing remains intact. Which diagnosis
best fits?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: Persistent experiences of detachment from self or surroundings with intact reality
testing define depersonalization/derealization disorder.
21. A client reports hearing two voices conversing about him, has disorganized speech,
diminished emotional expression, and marked functional decline for 8 months. Which diagnosis
is most likely?

   A. Schizophreniform disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophrenia
   Rationale: The presence of multiple psychotic symptoms with functional decline lasting more
than 6 months supports schizophrenia.

22. A previously healthy adult develops hallucinations, delusions, and disorganized speech
lasting 3 weeks following a severe stressor, then returns to premorbid functioning. Which
diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Delusional disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: A. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Sudden onset of psychosis lasting less than one month with full return to baseline
is characteristic of brief psychotic disorder.

23. A patient has delusions and hallucinations for 2 months, but the disturbance has not yet
lasted 6 months. Which diagnosis is most appropriate at this time?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Delusional disorder
   C. Schizophreniform disorder

 D. Brief psychotic disorder
       Answer: C. Schizophreniform disorder
   Rationale: Psychotic symptoms lasting more than 1 month but less than 6 months meet
criteria for schizophreniform disorder.

24. A man has fixed beliefs that neighbors are spying on him, but his behavior and functioning
are otherwise relatively preserved, and no other prominent psychotic symptoms are present.
Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Schizoaffective disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: A. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: Presence of persistent delusions with relatively preserved functioning and minimal
additional symptoms defines delusional disorder.
25. A patient has a major depressive episode concurrent with active psychotic symptoms, and
there is also a documented period of delusions without prominent mood symptoms. Which
diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Schizoaffective disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Schizoaffective disorder
   Rationale: The presence of mood episodes with psychosis plus a period of psychosis without
mood symptoms defines schizoaffective disorder.

26. A 28-year-old has elevated mood, decreased need for sleep, pressured speech, grandiosity,
and major impairment requiring hospitalization. Which diagnosis is most directly supported by
this episode?

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Bipolar I disorder
   Rationale: A single manic episode causing marked impairment or hospitalization is sufficient
for bipolar I disorder.

27. A patient reports episodes of depression and periods of increased energy, talkativeness,
and decreased need for sleep that do not cause marked impairment or hospitalization. He has
never had a full manic episode. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Bipolar I disorder

 D. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: B. Bipolar II disorder
   Rationale: Bipolar II disorder involves hypomanic episodes and major depressive episodes
without full manic episodes.

28. For the past 3 years, a client has had numerous periods of subclinical depressive symptoms
and hypomanic symptoms, but never meets full criteria for a major depressive, manic, or
hypomanic episode. Which diagnosis best fits?

   A. Cyclothymic disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Persistent depressive disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: A. Cyclothymic disorder
   Rationale: Chronic fluctuating subthreshold mood symptoms without full episodes define
cyclothymic disorder.
29. A woman reports a 3-week period of depressed mood, anhedonia, insomnia, guilt, poor
concentration, and suicidal ideation. Substance use and medical causes have been ruled out.
Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Major depressive disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder with depressed mood

 D. Bipolar II disorder
       Answer: B. Major depressive disorder
   Rationale: A cluster of depressive symptoms lasting at least 2 weeks with impairment meets
criteria for major depressive disorder.

30. A man describes being "down" most days for the last 4 years, with low self-esteem, poor
appetite, hopelessness, and low energy, but he has never been symptom-free for more than 2
months. Which diagnosis is most appropriate?

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. Persistent depressive disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Persistent depressive disorder
   Rationale: Chronic depressive symptoms lasting at least 2 years with minimal remission
define persistent depressive disorder.

31. A child has severe recurrent temper outbursts grossly out of proportion to the situation and
persistent irritability between outbursts across home and school for over a year. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Pediatric bipolar disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. Intermittent explosive disorder
       Answer: C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   Rationale: Severe temper outbursts with chronic irritability across settings define disruptive
mood dysregulation disorder.

32. A woman experiences marked affective lability, irritability, depressed mood, and tension in
the week before menses, with remission shortly after onset of menstruation. Which diagnosis is
most consistent?

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Premenstrual dysphoric disorder
   C. Bipolar II disorder

 D. Cyclothymic disorder
       Answer: B. Premenstrual dysphoric disorder
   Rationale: Cyclical mood symptoms tied to the menstrual cycle characterize premenstrual
dysphoric disorder.
33. Which feature most strongly supports mania rather than hypomania?
   A. Increased talkativeness
   B. Elevated self-esteem
   C. Marked impairment or hospitalization

 D. Decreased need for sleep
       Answer: C. Marked impairment or hospitalization
   Rationale: Mania is distinguished from hypomania by significant impairment, hospitalization,
or psychosis.

34. A clinician initially considers major depressive disorder in a patient with recurrent depressive
episodes. Which additional history would most strongly shift the diagnosis toward bipolar
disorder?

   A. Family history of dementia
   B. Past episode of increased energy with decreased need for sleep and grandiosity
   C. Past bereavement after a parent's death

 D. Chronic feelings of emptiness
       Answer: B. Past episode of increased energy with decreased need for sleep and
grandiosity
   Rationale: A history of hypomanic or manic symptoms indicates bipolar spectrum disorder.

35. A woman with anorexia nervosa has intense fear of gaining weight, severe restriction of food
intake, and significantly low body weight. Which cognitive feature is especially characteristic?

   A. Indifference to body shape
   B. Disturbance in body image evaluation
   C. Fear of vomiting only

 D. Loss of appetite due to depression
       Answer: B. Disturbance in body image evaluation
   Rationale: Distorted perception of body weight or shape is central to anorexia nervosa.

36. A normal-weight college student has recurrent episodes of binge eating followed by
self-induced vomiting and undue influence of body shape on self-evaluation. Which diagnosis is
most likely?

   A. Binge-eating disorder
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder

 D. Anorexia nervosa, restricting type
       Answer: B. Bulimia nervosa
   Rationale: Binge eating with compensatory behaviors and normal weight defines bulimia
nervosa.

37. A patient repeatedly consumes very large amounts of food in a discrete period while feeling
out of control, but does not regularly use compensatory behaviors. Which diagnosis best fits?

   A. Bulimia nervosa
   B. Anorexia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder

 D. Pica
       Answer: C. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent binge eating without compensatory behaviors defines binge-eating
disorder.

38. A child refuses many foods because of texture and smell, resulting in nutritional deficiency
and weight loss, but there is no body image disturbance. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
   Rationale: Restrictive eating without body image disturbance leading to nutritional problems
characterizes ARFID.

39. A woman reports dissatisfaction with sleep, trouble falling asleep, and daytime fatigue
occurring at least 3 nights a week for several months despite adequate opportunity for sleep.
Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder
   C. Hypersomnolence disorder

 D. Narcolepsy
       Answer: A. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Persistent difficulty initiating or maintaining sleep despite adequate opportunity
defines insomnia disorder.

40. A client complains of excessive sleepiness despite sleeping at least 9 hours per night and
still having difficulty being fully awake. This pattern has persisted for months. Which diagnosis is
most appropriate?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Nightmare disorder

 D. Sleep terror disorder
       Answer: B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   Rationale: Excessive sleepiness despite adequate sleep duration is characteristic of
hypersomnolence disorder.

41. Sudden bilateral loss of muscle tone triggered by laughter in a sleepy patient would most
strongly suggest:

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Narcolepsy
   C. REM sleep behavior disorder
   D. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder
  Answer: B. Narcolepsy

   Rationale: Cataplexy, or sudden loss of muscle tone triggered by emotion, is a hallmark
feature of narcolepsy.

42. A man with alcohol use disorder continues drinking despite liver disease, has repeatedly
failed to cut down, and spends much time obtaining alcohol. Which core concept does this
illustrate?

   A. Substance intoxication only
   B. Problematic pattern with impaired control
   C. Social use without impairment

 D. Factitious behavior
       Answer: B. Problematic pattern with impaired control
   Rationale: Continued use despite harm, failed attempts to stop, and excessive time spent
reflect impaired control in substance use disorder.

43. A patient develops tremors, autonomic hyperactivity, anxiety, and insomnia several hours
after abruptly reducing heavy alcohol intake. This presentation is most consistent with:

   A. Alcohol intoxication
   B. Alcohol withdrawal
   C. Panic disorder

 D. Sedative intoxication
       Answer: B. Alcohol withdrawal
   Rationale: Symptoms following reduction of heavy alcohol use indicate withdrawal syndrome.

44. Which substance class is most associated with euphoria, pupillary constriction, and
respiratory depression in intoxication?

   A. Stimulants
   B. Hallucinogens
   C. Opioids

 D. Cannabis
       Answer: C. Opioids
   Rationale: Opioid intoxication typically presents with euphoria, pinpoint pupils, and respiratory
depression.

45. A student uses cocaine and shortly afterward becomes euphoric, grandiose, and later
paranoid. Which is the best explanation?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Cocaine intoxication can produce psychotic symptoms
   C. Persistent depressive disorder

 D. Conversion disorder
       Answer: B. Cocaine intoxication can produce psychotic symptoms
   Rationale: Stimulant intoxication, especially cocaine, can induce transient psychotic
symptoms such as paranoia and grandiosity.
46. A client cannot stop gambling despite debt, lying to family members, and repeated
unsuccessful efforts to cut back. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   B. Gambling disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Manic episode
       Answer: B. Gambling disorder
   Rationale: Persistent problematic gambling behavior with distress and impairment defines
gambling disorder.

47. A person repeatedly fails to resist aggressive impulses and assaults others, with episodes
grossly out of proportion to provocation and not premeditated for gain. Which diagnosis best
fits?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: C. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: Recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts disproportionate to provocation
characterize intermittent explosive disorder.

48. Deliberate fire setting for fascination, curiosity, or gratification, without external motive, is
most characteristic of:

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Pyromania
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Pyromania
   Rationale: Fire setting driven by fascination and gratification without external gain defines
pyromania.

49. Recurrent failure to resist impulses to steal items not needed for personal use or monetary
value is most consistent with:

   A. Malingering
   B. Kleptomania
   C. Conduct disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Kleptomania
   Rationale: Impulse-driven theft without need or value defines kleptomania.

50. A 7-year-old often loses school materials, is easily distracted, avoids sustained mental effort,
and interrupts classmates across multiple settings. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Specific learning disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. ADHD

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: C. ADHD
   Rationale: Inattention, distractibility, and impulsivity across settings are core features of
ADHD.

51. A child has persistent deficits in social communication and restricted, repetitive behaviors
beginning early in development. Which diagnosis is most appropriate?

   A. ADHD
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. Selective mutism

 D. Social anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Autism spectrum disorder
   Rationale: Core features include social communication deficits and restricted, repetitive
patterns of behavior.

52. A student of average intelligence shows persistent difficulty in word reading accuracy and
spelling that began during school years and is not better explained by sensory deficit. Which
diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Intellectual disability
   B. ADHD
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: C. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Persistent academic skill deficits despite normal intelligence indicate specific
learning disorder.

53. The diagnosis of intellectual disability requires deficits in intellectual functions and:
   A. a history of psychosis
   B. deficits in adaptive functioning
   C. persistent depressed mood

 D. onset after age 30
       Answer: B. deficits in adaptive functioning
   Rationale: Intellectual disability requires both intellectual and adaptive functioning deficits with
developmental onset.

54. A child argues with adults, is touchy, and deliberately annoys others, but there is no pattern
of serious aggression, theft, or property destruction. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   Rationale: ODD involves irritability, defiance, and argumentative behavior without severe rule
violations.

55. A teenager has repeatedly bullied peers, stolen from others, and deliberately destroyed
property. Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Conduct disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: C. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Persistent violation of others' rights and social norms defines conduct disorder.

56. A person shows a pervasive disregard for and violation of the rights of others since
adolescence, including deceitfulness, irresponsibility, and lack of remorse. Which diagnosis is
most likely?

   A. Narcissistic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: C. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: A pattern of disregard for others and lack of remorse since adolescence
characterizes antisocial personality disorder.

57. A woman has unstable relationships, identity disturbance, chronic emptiness, and recurrent
self-harm in response to fears of abandonment. Which diagnosis best fits?

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Borderline personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: C. Borderline personality disorder
   Rationale: Emotional instability, identity disturbance, and fear of abandonment define
borderline personality disorder.

58. A man consistently interprets others' motives as malevolent, bears grudges, and is unwilling
to confide in others because of suspiciousness. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Paranoid personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: B. Paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Pervasive distrust and suspiciousness without psychosis define paranoid
personality disorder.
59. A person is detached from social relationships, prefers solitary activities, and shows limited
emotional expression, but does not display cognitive-perceptual distortions. Which diagnosis is
most appropriate?

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Autism spectrum disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: A. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Social detachment and restricted emotional expression without eccentric beliefs
define schizoid personality disorder.

60. Social anxiety accompanied by eccentric behavior, odd beliefs, and unusual perceptual
experiences most strongly suggests:

   A. Avoidant personality disorder
   B. Schizotypal personality disorder
   C. Schizoid personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Odd beliefs and perceptual experiences alongside social anxiety characterize
schizotypal personality disorder.

61. A patient is uncomfortable unless others take responsibility for major areas of life and
urgently seeks another relationship when one ends. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Dependent personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: A. Dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Excessive need to be cared for, difficulty making independent decisions, and
urgent seeking of new relationships are defining features of dependent personality disorder.

62. A person is preoccupied with orderliness, perfectionism, and control at the expense of
flexibility and efficiency. Which diagnosis best fits?

   A. OCD
   B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   Rationale: A pervasive pattern of perfectionism, rigidity, and control interfering with
functioning characterizes OCPD.

63. A socially inhibited adult avoids occupational activities involving interpersonal contact
because of fears of criticism and feelings of inadequacy, yet desires relationships. Which
diagnosis is most likely?
   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Social anxiety disorder only
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: C. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Social inhibition with feelings of inadequacy and hypersensitivity to criticism,
alongside desire for relationships, defines avoidant personality disorder.

64. A theatrical, attention-seeking interpersonal style with rapidly shifting but shallow expression
of emotion is most characteristic of:

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Borderline personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Bipolar II disorder
       Answer: A. Histrionic personality disorder
   Rationale: Excessive emotionality and attention-seeking behavior with shallow affect
characterize histrionic personality disorder.

65. Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy are core features of:
   A. Antisocial personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Narcissistic personality disorder is defined by grandiosity, need for admiration, and
lack of empathy.

66. An elderly hospitalized patient develops acute fluctuating confusion, impaired attention, and
disorganized thinking over 2 days after an infection. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Major neurocognitive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Dissociative disorder
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Acute onset, fluctuating course, and impaired attention in the context of medical
illness indicate delirium.

67. A patient shows gradual decline in memory and other cognitive domains that interferes with
independence in everyday activities. Which diagnosis is most appropriate?

   A. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Major neurocognitive disorder

 D. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
       Answer: C. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Significant cognitive decline that interferes with independence defines major
neurocognitive disorder.

68. Which feature best distinguishes delirium from major neurocognitive disorder?
   A. Delusions are never present in delirium
   B. Delirium has an acute, fluctuating course with impaired attention
   C. Memory loss occurs only in neurocognitive disorders

 D. Delirium lasts at least 6 months
       Answer: B. Delirium has an acute, fluctuating course with impaired attention
   Rationale: Delirium is distinguished by its acute onset, fluctuating course, and impaired
attention.

69. Visual hallucinations, cognitive fluctuations, and parkinsonian features would raise suspicion
for:

   A. Neurocognitive disorder due to Alzheimer's disease only
   B. Delirium only
   C. Neurocognitive disorder with Lewy bodies

 D. Dissociative identity disorder
       Answer: C. Neurocognitive disorder with Lewy bodies
   Rationale: Lewy body neurocognitive disorder commonly presents with visual hallucinations,
fluctuations, and parkinsonism.

70. A woman reports markedly reduced interest in sexual activity that causes personal distress.
Which diagnosis is most consistent?

   A. Female sexual interest/arousal disorder
   B. Gender dysphoria
   C. Histrionic personality disorder

 D. Paraphilic disorder
       Answer: A. Female sexual interest/arousal disorder
   Rationale: Reduced sexual interest accompanied by distress defines female sexual
interest/arousal disorder.

71. Recurrent inability to attain or maintain an erection during partnered sexual activity, causing
distress, is most consistent with:

   A. Premature ejaculation
   B. Male hypoactive sexual desire disorder
   C. Erectile disorder

 D. Gender dysphoria
       Answer: C. Erectile disorder
   Rationale: Persistent difficulty achieving or maintaining erection during sexual activity defines
erectile disorder.

72. A man is distressed because his experienced gender is incongruent with his assigned sex
and he has a persistent desire to be treated as another gender. Which diagnosis is most likely?
   A. Sexual masochism disorder
   B. Gender dysphoria
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Transvestic disorder
       Answer: B. Gender dysphoria
   Rationale: Distress due to incongruence between experienced gender and assigned sex
defines gender dysphoria.

73. Recurrent sexual arousal from observing an unsuspecting person who is naked or engaging
in sexual activity, when acted upon or causing distress, is most consistent with:

   A. Fetishistic disorder
   B. Voyeuristic disorder
   C. Exhibitionistic disorder

 D. Sexual sadism disorder
       Answer: B. Voyeuristic disorder
   Rationale: Sexual arousal from observing unsuspecting individuals defines voyeuristic
disorder.

74. A patient reports recurrent intense sexual arousal from exposing his genitals to
unsuspecting strangers and has acted on these urges. Which diagnosis is most likely?

   A. Voyeuristic disorder
   B. Fetishistic disorder
   C. Exhibitionistic disorder

 D. Transvestic disorder
       Answer: C. Exhibitionistic disorder
   Rationale: Exposing one's genitals to unsuspecting others for sexual arousal defines
exhibitionistic disorder.

75. A man experiences intense sexual arousal from nonliving objects or a highly specific
nongenital body part, and the pattern causes significant distress. Which diagnosis is most
appropriate?

   A. Fetishistic disorder
   B. Pedophilic disorder
   C. Sexual masochism disorder

 D. Gender dysphoria
       Answer: A. Fetishistic disorder
   Rationale: Sexual arousal focused on nonliving objects or specific body parts with distress
defines fetishistic disorder.

76. Which pioneer is most strongly associated with the psychoanalytic model and the role of
unconscious conflict?

   A. Ivan Pavlov
   B. Sigmund Freud
   C. Emil Kraepelin
 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: B. Sigmund Freud
   Rationale: Freud developed psychoanalysis emphasizing unconscious conflict in behavior.

77. The classification system most strongly associated with the early descriptive differentiation
of dementia praecox and manic-depressive illness is linked to:

   A. Philippe Pinel
   B. Emil Kraepelin
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. B. F. Skinner
       Answer: B. Emil Kraepelin
   Rationale: Kraepelin is known for early diagnostic classification distinguishing major
psychiatric syndromes.

78. The concept of moral therapy is historically associated most closely with:
   A. humane treatment and structured, respectful care
   B. electroconvulsive treatment for psychosis
   C. classical conditioning of fear

 D. neurotransmitter imbalance models
       Answer: A. humane treatment and structured, respectful care
   Rationale: Moral therapy emphasized humane, respectful, and structured care for individuals
with mental illness.

79. Which theorist is most closely associated with classical conditioning?
   A. Albert Bandura
   B. Ivan Pavlov
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: B. Ivan Pavlov
   Rationale: Pavlov's experiments on conditioned reflexes established classical conditioning.

80. The emphasis on reinforcement and consequences in explaining behavior is most
associated with:

   A. B. F. Skinner
   B. Sigmund Freud
   C. Hippocrates

 D. Jean Piaget
       Answer: A. B. F. Skinner
   Rationale: Skinner developed operant conditioning focusing on reinforcement and
consequences.

81. The proposal that abnormal behavior should be understood through interacting biological,
psychological, emotional, and social influences best reflects:

   A. the supernatural model
   B. the moral model
   C. a multidimensional integrative approach

 D. strict biological reductionism
       Answer: C. a multidimensional integrative approach
   Rationale: Modern abnormal psychology emphasizes that behavior results from the
interaction of multiple domains rather than a single cause.

82. A clinician is deciding whether a patient's depressive symptoms are primary or
substance-induced. Which question is most critical?

   A. Whether the patient believes in psychotherapy
   B. Whether symptoms have a close temporal relationship to substance use
   C. Whether the patient prefers medication

 D. Whether family members agree with the diagnosis
       Answer: B. Whether symptoms have a close temporal relationship to substance use
   Rationale: Establishing timing between substance use and symptom onset is crucial in
determining substance-induced conditions.

83. Which is the best example of a compulsion?
   A. Recurrent intrusive thought of contamination
   B. Persistent depressed mood
   C. Repeated handwashing to reduce anxiety

 D. Fear of public embarrassment
       Answer: C. Repeated handwashing to reduce anxiety
   Rationale: Compulsions are repetitive behaviors performed to reduce distress caused by
obsessions.

84. In schizophrenia, diminished emotional expression and avolition are examples of:
   A. positive symptoms
   B. negative symptoms
   C. dissociative symptoms

 D. manic symptoms
       Answer: B. negative symptoms
   Rationale: Negative symptoms reflect deficits or loss of normal functions such as emotional
expression and motivation.

85. Which finding would most strongly suggest delirium rather than schizophrenia in an older
adult with new-onset psychosis?

   A. Long history of social withdrawal
   B. Acute fluctuating disturbance in attention after a medical illness
   C. Presence of bizarre delusions

 D. Auditory hallucinations alone
       Answer: B. Acute fluctuating disturbance in attention after a medical illness
   Rationale: Delirium is characterized by acute onset, fluctuating course, and impaired attention
often due to a medical condition.
86. A psychometrician is asked by a physician to independently interpret complex
psychopathology and make a formal treatment plan without supervision. Under RA 10029, the
most appropriate response is:

   A. Accept because any licensed psychometrician may independently practice all
psychological services

   B. Decline or clarify limits because work must remain within lawful scope and competence
   C. Accept if the client signs consent

 D. Accept only if no psychologist is available anywhere
       Answer: B. Decline or clarify limits because work must remain within lawful scope and
competence
   Rationale: RA 10029 requires practitioners to work within their scope and competence;
psychometricians cannot independently perform functions beyond their legal role.

87. A psychometrician is newly assigned to administer an instrument unfamiliar to her.
According to ethical standards on competence, the best course is to:

   A. Proceed immediately because licensure alone is sufficient
   B. Refuse all future assessment work
   C. Obtain training, supervision, consultation, or make an appropriate referral

 D. Let the client interpret the test personally
       Answer: C. Obtain training, supervision, consultation, or make an appropriate referral
   Rationale: Ethical standards require practitioners to ensure competence before using
unfamiliar tools or to refer appropriately.

88. A practitioner providing telepsychology services should ethically assume that:
   A. ethical obligations are waived online
   B. only face-to-face services require informed consent
   C. the same ethical principles governing confidentiality and informed consent still apply

 D. telepsychology is prohibited for all psychometricians
       Answer: C. the same ethical principles governing confidentiality and informed consent still
apply
   Rationale: Ethical principles such as confidentiality and informed consent apply equally to
telepsychology.

89. A psychologist receives a third-party referral from an employer for assessment of an
employee. What should be clarified at the outset?

   A. Only the employee's favorite treatment
   B. The probable uses of the information, role expectations, and limits of confidentiality
   C. That no records will be kept

 D. That the employee must waive all rights
       Answer: B. The probable uses of the information, role expectations, and limits of
confidentiality
   Rationale: In third-party referrals, roles, use of information, and confidentiality limits must be
clearly explained.
90. A practitioner becomes aware that another psychology professional may have committed an
ethical violation causing likely substantial harm. The most appropriate general response is to:

   A. Ignore it to avoid conflict
   B. Publicly shame the colleague on social media
   C. Take appropriate further action or report to proper authorities consistent with ethics and
confidentiality

 D. Destroy relevant records
       Answer: C. Take appropriate further action or report to proper authorities consistent with
ethics and confidentiality
   Rationale: Ethical standards require appropriate action when substantial harm may occur,
while respecting confidentiality and due process.

91. A practitioner notices that personal stress is impairing judgment during sessions. Which
ethical principle is most directly relevant?

   A. Maintain competence and take measures such as consultation, limiting, suspending, or
terminating duties if needed

   B. Continue working unchanged to avoid disappointing clients
   C. Transfer all files to friends

 D. Diagnose all clients quickly and end sessions early
       Answer: A. Maintain competence and take measures such as consultation, limiting,
suspending, or terminating duties if needed
   Rationale: Practitioners must monitor their functioning and take action if impairment affects
competence.

92. A client reveals intent to seriously harm an identifiable person. Which legal-ethical concept
is most relevant?

   A. Duty to warn/protect
   B. Absolute confidentiality without exception
   C. Barter

 D. Multiple inheritance
       Answer: A. Duty to warn/protect
   Rationale: Threats of serious harm to identifiable individuals may require breaching
confidentiality to protect others.

93. A supervisor asks an intern to administer tests for which the intern has no training and
provides no supervision. Which ethical concern is most central?

   A. Delegation beyond competence
   B. Positive reinforcement
   C. Cultural formulation

 D. Countertransference only
       Answer: A. Delegation beyond competence
   Rationale: Assigning tasks without ensuring competence and supervision violates ethical
standards.
94. A clinician begins treating a close relative and also enters into a business arrangement with
that person. Which ethical risk is most clearly raised?

   A. Multiple relationship impairing objectivity and increasing risk of exploitation
   B. Improved validity of diagnosis
   C. Reduction of conflicts of interest

 D. Automatic informed consent
       Answer: A. Multiple relationship impairing objectivity and increasing risk of exploitation
   Rationale: Multiple relationships can impair professional judgment and increase risk of harm
or exploitation.

95. Which statement best reflects a proper principle of confidentiality?
   A. Confidentiality never has any limit
   B. Confidentiality may have limits that should be clarified, especially in third-party and risk

situations
   C. Confidentiality applies only to written records

 D. Confidentiality is optional if the clinician is curious
       Answer: B. Confidentiality may have limits that should be clarified, especially in third-party
and risk situations
   Rationale: Confidentiality is fundamental but has limits that must be communicated clearly.

96. A psychometrician says, "I can treat all severe psychiatric disorders independently because
I am licensed." This statement is ethically problematic primarily because:

   A. all self-statements are unethical
   B. it may misrepresent competence and lawful scope of practice
   C. treatment is never part of psychology

 D. psychometricians may not interact with clients
       Answer: B. it may misrepresent competence and lawful scope of practice
   Rationale: Misrepresenting scope of practice and competence violates ethical and legal
standards.

97. A practitioner is asked to provide emergency psychological assistance in a disaster area
outside her usual specialty because no other service is available. Ethically, she should:

   A. never help under any circumstance
   B. provide appropriate limited emergency assistance cautiously, then discontinue once
emergency ends and arrange competent follow-up
   C. permanently practice outside competence without training

 D. offer services only for cash
       Answer: B. provide appropriate limited emergency assistance cautiously, then discontinue
once emergency ends and arrange competent follow-up
   Rationale: Ethical standards allow limited emergency services when no alternatives exist, with
appropriate safeguards and follow-up.
98. In differential diagnosis, which sequence is most defensible when a patient presents with
new psychiatric symptoms?

   A. Diagnose personality disorder first, then consider medical issues
   B. Rule out malingering/factitious behavior, substance causes, and medical etiologies before
finalizing the primary psychiatric diagnosis
   C. Begin with projective testing only

 D. Ignore timeline and context
       Answer: B. Rule out malingering/factitious behavior, substance causes, and medical
etiologies before finalizing the primary psychiatric diagnosis
   Rationale: Proper differential diagnosis requires ruling out non-psychiatric and secondary
causes before assigning a primary diagnosis.

99. A clinician evaluating sudden-onset hallucinations in a patient taking high-dose
corticosteroids should first consider:

   A. schizophrenia spectrum disorder
   B. medication/substance-induced etiology
   C. schizoid personality disorder

 D. specific phobia
       Answer: B. medication/substance-induced etiology
   Rationale: Medications like corticosteroids can induce psychiatric symptoms and must be
considered first.

100. Which principle best captures high-quality board-style clinical reasoning in abnormal
psychology?

    A. Choose the most dramatic diagnosis immediately
    B. Focus on one symptom and ignore impairment, timing, and context
    C. Integrate symptom pattern, duration, differential diagnoses, functional impairment, and
etiological possibilities

 D. Base diagnosis only on the client's preferred label
        Answer: C. Integrate symptom pattern, duration, differential diagnoses, functional
impairment, and etiological possibilities
    Rationale: Accurate diagnosis requires integrating multiple clinical factors including symptom
pattern, duration, impairment, and possible causes.
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL
PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 11
MOCK EXAM- ABNORMAL PSYCHOLOGY EXAM 11

1. A 17-year-old student has become increasingly withdrawn, reports hearing a male voice
commenting on his actions, and shows flat affect. He has no history of substance use, and
medical workup is unremarkable. Which diagnosis is MOST strongly suggested?

  A. Social anxiety disorder
  B. Schizophrenia spectrum disorder
  C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophrenia spectrum disorder
  Rationale: Auditory hallucinations, flat affect, and social withdrawal strongly suggest a
schizophrenia-spectrum presentation after substance and medical causes are excluded.

2. A client reports recurrent panic attacks and now refuses to ride buses, enter malls, or stand in
long lines because escape might be difficult if panic occurs. Which diagnosis BEST fits the
avoidance pattern?

  A. Panic disorder with agoraphobia-type avoidance
  B. Specific phobia
  C. Separation anxiety disorder

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: A. Panic disorder with agoraphobia-type avoidance
  Rationale: The client has recurrent panic attacks followed by avoidance of places where
escape may be difficult, a classic panic-agoraphobic pattern.

3. A woman has had 3 years of fluctuating hypomanic symptoms and periods of depressive
symptoms that never met full criteria for a major depressive episode. Which diagnosis is MOST
likely?

  A. Bipolar I disorder
  B. Bipolar II disorder
  C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: C. Cyclothymic disorder
  Rationale: Cyclothymic disorder involves chronic fluctuating hypomanic and depressive
