symptoms that do not meet full episode criteria for at least 2 years in adults.

4. A 9-year-old child persistently fails to speak in school despite speaking normally at home and
with siblings. Which diagnosis is MOST appropriate?

  A. Autism spectrum disorder
  B. Selective mutism
  C. Social anxiety disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Selective mutism
  Rationale: Selective mutism is characterized by consistent failure to speak in specific social
situations despite speaking normally in others.

5. A man repeatedly checks his stove for hours each night because of intrusive fears of causing
a fire, despite recognizing the fear as excessive. Which feature MOST clearly supports
obsessive-compulsive disorder?

  A. Checking is ego-syntonic and pleasurable
  B. Checking is done to neutralize distress from intrusive thoughts
  C. Checking occurs only during intoxication

 D. Checking is motivated by financial gain
       Answer: B. Checking is done to neutralize distress from intrusive thoughts
  Rationale: Compulsions are repetitive behaviors performed to reduce distress or prevent
feared outcomes linked to obsessions.

6. A 24-year-old develops intrusive memories, hypervigilance, and nightmares 2 weeks after
surviving a severe car crash. Which diagnosis is MOST appropriate at this time?

  A. Adjustment disorder
  B. Acute stress disorder
  C. Posttraumatic stress disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Acute stress disorder
  Rationale: Trauma-related symptoms occurring from 3 days to 1 month after trauma fit acute
stress disorder rather than PTSD.

7. A client presents with depressed mood and fatigue. According to sound differential diagnosis
practice, which should be ruled out FIRST after considering feigning?

  A. Personality disorder
  B. Substance etiology
  C. Specific phobia

 D. Adjustment disorder
       Answer: B. Substance etiology
  Rationale: A core differential diagnosis principle is to rule out substance effects early because
substances can mimic many psychiatric presentations.

8. A patient intentionally falsifies symptoms to obtain disability benefits. Which is the BEST
classification?

  A. Conversion disorder
  B. Factitious disorder
  C. Malingering

 D. Somatic symptom disorder
       Answer: C. Malingering
  Rationale: Intentional symptom production for clear external incentives such as disability
benefits indicates malingering.
9. A patient intentionally produces symptoms without obvious external reward and repeatedly
seeks hospitalization. Which diagnosis is MOST consistent?

  A. Illness anxiety disorder
  B. Factitious disorder
  C. Malingering

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Factitious disorder
  Rationale: Factitious disorder involves falsification or induction of symptoms in the absence of
obvious external rewards.

10. A 28-year-old reports persistent sadness, anhedonia, early morning awakening, poor
concentration, guilt, and suicidal ideation for 3 weeks. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. Cyclothymic disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
       Answer: A. Major depressive disorder
   Rationale: The cluster of depressive symptoms over weeks with impairment and suicidal
ideation strongly supports a major depressive episode.

11. A client fears developing cancer despite repeated normal medical evaluations and has
minimal somatic symptoms. Which diagnosis BEST fits?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Illness anxiety disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Generalized anxiety disorder
       Answer: B. Illness anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Illness anxiety disorder features high health anxiety with minimal or absent somatic
symptoms despite reassurance.

12. A patient develops paralysis of the right arm after a family conflict. Neurological findings are
inconsistent with known disease processes, and there is no evidence of intentional feigning.
Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Factitious disorder
   B. Conversion disorder
   C. Somatic symptom disorder

 D. Dissociative amnesia
       Answer: B. Conversion disorder
   Rationale: Neurological-like symptoms incompatible with recognized disease and not
intentionally produced suggest conversion disorder.

13. A client experiences recurrent depersonalization episodes but reality testing remains intact.
Which diagnosis is MOST appropriate?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Bipolar I disorder
       Answer: B. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   Rationale: Persistent depersonalization with intact reality testing is the hallmark of
depersonalization/derealization disorder.

14. A 14-year-old repeatedly pulls out hair from the scalp, feels tension before doing so, and
has made unsuccessful attempts to stop. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   B. Trichotillomania
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Excoriation disorder
       Answer: B. Trichotillomania
   Rationale: Recurrent hair pulling with failed attempts to stop is characteristic of
trichotillomania.

15. A 19-year-old persistently picks at skin lesions, causing tissue damage, and has repeatedly
tried to stop. Which diagnosis is MOST appropriate?

   A. Excoriation disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Factitious disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: A. Excoriation disorder
   Rationale: Repeated skin picking causing lesions and unsuccessful efforts to stop fit
excoriation disorder.

16. A person binge eats large amounts of food while feeling out of control, but does not regularly
engage in purging or compensatory behavior. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Anorexia nervosa
   B. Bulimia nervosa
   C. Binge-eating disorder

 D. Avoidant/restrictive food intake disorder
       Answer: C. Binge-eating disorder
   Rationale: Binge-eating disorder involves recurrent binge episodes with loss of control and no
regular compensatory behavior.

17. Which feature MOST clearly distinguishes anorexia nervosa from bulimia nervosa?
   A. Episodes of eating in secret
   B. Significant restriction leading to low body weight
   C. Shape and weight overvaluation

 D. Fear of gaining weight
       Answer: B. Significant restriction leading to low body weight
   Rationale: Low body weight due to restriction is central to anorexia nervosa and distinguishes
it from bulimia nervosa.

18. A client reports normal appetite but persistent difficulty initiating sleep for months, leading to
fatigue and occupational impairment. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Insomnia disorder
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Circadian rhythm sleep-wake disorder

 D. Narcolepsy
       Answer: A. Insomnia disorder
   Rationale: Chronic difficulty initiating sleep with daytime impairment is classic insomnia
disorder.

19. A patient has excessive daytime sleepiness despite adequate main sleep duration and no
cataplexy. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Narcolepsy
   B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   C. Insomnia disorder

 D. Nightmare disorder
       Answer: B. Hypersomnolence disorder
   Rationale: Excessive daytime sleepiness despite adequate main sleep duration supports
hypersomnolence disorder.

20. A 32-year-old has repeated episodes of intense fear with palpitations, dizziness, chest
discomfort, and fear of dying that peak within minutes. Which is the BEST term for these
episodes?

   A. Obsessions
   B. Panic attacks
   C. Dissociative episodes

 D. Delusions
       Answer: B. Panic attacks
   Rationale: Abrupt surges of intense fear peaking within minutes with autonomic symptoms
define panic attacks.

21. A man persistently avoids parties because he fears scrutiny and embarrassment if others
notice his shaking voice. Which diagnosis BEST fits?

   A. Agoraphobia
   B. Social anxiety disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Panic disorder
       Answer: B. Social anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Fear of negative evaluation and embarrassment in social situations is the defining
pattern of social anxiety disorder.
22. A woman has marked fear of dogs that is out of proportion to actual danger and avoids
parks because of this fear. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Specific phobia
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Panic disorder

 D. Separation anxiety disorder
       Answer: A. Specific phobia
   Rationale: Marked, excessive fear tied to a specific object such as dogs is consistent with
specific phobia.

23. A child becomes extremely distressed whenever separated from a parent, worries that harm
will befall the parent, and refuses sleepovers. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Selective mutism
   B. Separation anxiety disorder
   C. Social anxiety disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: B. Separation anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Excessive distress and worry about separation from attachment figures define
separation anxiety disorder.

24. A woman worries excessively for months about finances, health, work, and family, and finds
the worry difficult to control. Which diagnosis is MOST appropriate?

   A. Panic disorder
   B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   C. Illness anxiety disorder

 D. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
       Answer: B. Generalized anxiety disorder
   Rationale: Uncontrollable, excessive worry across multiple domains for months is the
hallmark of GAD.

25. Which statement BEST reflects the relationship between panic disorder and agoraphobia?
   A. They are always diagnosed together
   B. Agoraphobia refers only to fear of open spaces
   C. Panic symptoms may lead to avoidance of situations where escape seems difficult

 D. Panic disorder requires psychosis
       Answer: C. Panic symptoms may lead to avoidance of situations where escape seems
difficult
   Rationale: That statement captures the core functional link between panic symptoms and
agoraphobic avoidance.

26. A client hoards newspapers, broken appliances, and containers because discarding them
causes marked distress. Her home is no longer usable. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   B. Hoarding disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Major depressive disorder
       Answer: B. Hoarding disorder
   Rationale: Persistent difficulty discarding possessions with resulting clutter and distress
supports hoarding disorder.

27. A man is preoccupied with a slight facial blemish that others barely notice and repeatedly
seeks cosmetic procedures. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Delusional disorder, grandiose type
       Answer: B. Body dysmorphic disorder
   Rationale: Preoccupation with perceived appearance defects plus repetitive
reassurance-seeking or procedures supports BDD.

28. A survivor of workplace dismissal becomes tearful, anxious, and socially withdrawn within 2
months of losing the job. Symptoms do not meet criteria for another disorder. Which diagnosis is
MOST likely?

   A. Major depressive disorder
   B. Adjustment disorder
   C. Persistent depressive disorder

 D. Acute stress disorder
       Answer: B. Adjustment disorder
   Rationale: Emotional and behavioral symptoms in response to an identifiable stressor that do
not meet full criteria for another disorder fit adjustment disorder.

29. Which feature MOST strongly differentiates PTSD from adjustment disorder?
   A. Symptoms begin after a stressor
   B. Presence of intrusive trauma-related symptoms after exposure to traumatic stress
   C. Depressed mood

 D. Functional impairment
       Answer: B. Presence of intrusive trauma-related symptoms after exposure to traumatic
stress
   Rationale: PTSD specifically requires exposure to traumatic stress plus intrusion, avoidance,
negative mood/cognition changes, and arousal alterations.

30. A client cannot recall important autobiographical information following a traumatic event, but
neurological workup is negative. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Dissociative amnesia
   B. Major neurocognitive disorder
   C. Delirium

 D. Conversion disorder
       Answer: A. Dissociative amnesia
   Rationale: Important autobiographical memory loss after trauma without neurological
explanation is most consistent with dissociative amnesia.

31. A patient reports two distinct identity states associated with memory gaps for daily events.
Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Depersonalization/derealization disorder
   B. Dissociative identity disorder
   C. Schizoaffective disorder

 D. Borderline personality disorder
       Answer: B. Dissociative identity disorder
   Rationale: Distinct identity states plus recurrent amnesia for daily events strongly suggest
dissociative identity disorder.

32. A patient has multiple physical complaints and devotes excessive time, worry, and behavior
to them, even when medical findings are mild. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Illness anxiety disorder
   B. Somatic symptom disorder
   C. Factitious disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: B. Somatic symptom disorder
   Rationale: The key feature is disproportionate thoughts, feelings, and behaviors about
somatic symptoms, regardless of medical explanation.

33. A person with angina repeatedly triggers episodes when enraged and chronically ignores
medical advice because of maladaptive psychological patterns. Which diagnosis BEST fits?

   A. Somatic symptom disorder
   B. Adjustment disorder
   C. Psychological factors affecting other medical conditions

 D. Illness anxiety disorder
       Answer: C. Psychological factors affecting other medical conditions
   Rationale: Psychological or behavioral factors that worsen a medical condition are central to
this diagnosis.

34. A client with schizophrenia has prominent delusions, hallucinations, disorganized speech,
and avolition. Which symptom is considered a negative symptom?

   A. Delusion of persecution
   B. Auditory hallucination
   C. Avolition

 D. Disorganized speech
       Answer: C. Avolition
   Rationale: Avolition is a negative symptom reflecting decreased motivation and goal-directed
behavior.
35. A patient has psychotic symptoms for 3 weeks following a major stressor and then fully
returns to baseline functioning. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Schizophrenia
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Brief psychotic disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Brief psychotic disorder
   Rationale: Psychotic symptoms lasting more than a day but less than a month with full return
to premorbid functioning suggest brief psychotic disorder.

36. A client has one month of psychotic symptoms but duration is still under 6 months. Which
diagnosis is MOST appropriate if other criteria are met?

   A. Brief psychotic disorder
   B. Schizophreniform disorder
   C. Schizophrenia

 D. Schizoaffective disorder
       Answer: B. Schizophreniform disorder
   Rationale: Schizophreniform disorder is diagnosed when schizophrenia-like symptoms last at
least 1 month but less than 6 months.

37. A person has a fixed false belief that neighbors are poisoning his food, but speech, affect,
and functioning are otherwise relatively preserved. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Delusional disorder
   B. Schizophrenia
   C. Obsessive-compulsive disorder

 D. Bipolar II disorder
       Answer: A. Delusional disorder
   Rationale: A nonbizarre or bizarre fixed delusion with relatively preserved functioning outside
the delusional theme fits delusional disorder.

38. Which diagnosis requires a major mood episode concurrent with psychotic symptoms, along
with a period of psychosis without mood symptoms?

   A. Major depressive disorder with psychotic features
   B. Bipolar I disorder
   C. Schizoaffective disorder

 D. Delusional disorder
       Answer: C. Schizoaffective disorder
   Rationale: Schizoaffective disorder requires both mood episodes and periods of psychosis
occurring without mood symptoms.

39. A client has decreased need for sleep, pressured speech, inflated self-esteem, risky
spending, and marked functional impairment for 8 days. Which diagnosis is MOST strongly
suggested?

   A. Hypomanic episode
   B. Manic episode
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: B. Manic episode
   Rationale: The duration, severity, and marked functional impairment indicate mania rather
than hypomania.

40. A client reports recurrent depressive episodes and at least one hypomanic episode, but
never a full manic episode. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Bipolar I disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Cyclothymic disorder

 D. Persistent depressive disorder
       Answer: B. Bipolar II disorder
   Rationale: Bipolar II requires at least one hypomanic episode and one major depressive
episode without a history of mania.

41. Which feature MOST strongly distinguishes a manic episode from a hypomanic episode?
   A. Elevated mood
   B. Increased energy
   C. Marked impairment or hospitalization

 D. Decreased need for sleep
       Answer: C. Marked impairment or hospitalization
   Rationale: Functional severity is a major distinguishing feature: mania causes marked
impairment, psychosis, or hospitalization.

42. A 10-year-old has severe recurrent temper outbursts grossly out of proportion to
provocation, plus persistent irritability between outbursts. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Bipolar I disorder
   C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder

 D. Conduct disorder
       Answer: C. Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder
   Rationale: DMDD involves severe recurrent temper outbursts plus persistent irritability
between outbursts in youth.

43. Which psychologist is most closely associated with the concept of learned helplessness
relevant to depression?

   A. Albert Bandura
   B. Martin Seligman
   C. Carl Rogers

 D. Ivan Pavlov
       Answer: B. Martin Seligman
   Rationale: Martin Seligman is closely associated with learned helplessness, a concept
relevant to depression.

44. Which pioneer is MOST closely associated with moral therapy?
   A. Philippe Pinel
   B. B. F. Skinner
   C. Emil Kraepelin

 D. Aaron Beck
       Answer: A. Philippe Pinel
   Rationale: Philippe Pinel is classically associated with moral treatment and more humane
care of the mentally ill.

45. Which historical figure is BEST known for classifying mental disorders and helping
distinguish dementia praecox from manic-depressive illness?

   A. Sigmund Freud
   B. Emil Kraepelin
   C. Carl Jung

 D. John Watson
       Answer: B. Emil Kraepelin
   Rationale: Kraepelin is known for classification work distinguishing major psychotic and mood
syndromes.

46. Which approach is MOST associated with Aaron Beck?
   A. Classical conditioning
   B. Cognitive therapy emphasizing maladaptive beliefs
   C. Free association

 D. Aversion therapy only
       Answer: B. Cognitive therapy emphasizing maladaptive beliefs
   Rationale: Aaron Beck developed cognitive therapy focused on identifying and restructuring
maladaptive cognitions.

47. Which theorist is MOST associated with client-centered or person-centered therapy?
   A. Carl Rogers
   B. Albert Ellis
   C. Joseph Wolpe

 D. Hans Selye
       Answer: A. Carl Rogers
   Rationale: Carl Rogers is identified with person-centered therapy emphasizing empathy,
congruence, and unconditional positive regard.

48. Which concept is MOST associated with Hans Selye?
   A. Operant conditioning
   B. General adaptation syndrome
   C. Reciprocal inhibition
 D. Modeling
       Answer: B. General adaptation syndrome
   Rationale: Hans Selye proposed the general adaptation syndrome describing stages of stress
response.

49. A child shows persistent inattention across home and school, frequently loses materials, is
forgetful, and is easily distracted. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Specific learning disorder
   B. ADHD
   C. Autism spectrum disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. ADHD
   Rationale: Cross-situational inattention, distractibility, forgetfulness, and disorganization
support ADHD.

50. A student has normal intelligence and opportunity to learn but shows persistent deficits in
word reading accuracy and spelling. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. ADHD
   B. Intellectual disability
   C. Specific learning disorder

 D. Communication disorder
       Answer: C. Specific learning disorder
   Rationale: Persistent academic skill deficits despite adequate instruction and opportunity fit
specific learning disorder.

51. A child has deficits in social reciprocity, limited eye contact, and restricted repetitive
interests. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Social anxiety disorder
   B. Autism spectrum disorder
   C. Selective mutism

 D. Reactive attachment disorder
       Answer: B. Autism spectrum disorder
   Rationale: Core deficits in social reciprocity plus restricted repetitive interests strongly support
ASD.

52. Intellectual disability is defined primarily by deficits in:
   A. Mood regulation and social anxiety
   B. Intellectual and adaptive functioning
   C. Reading and writing only

 D. Attention and memory only
       Answer: B. Intellectual and adaptive functioning
   Rationale: Intellectual disability requires deficits in both intellectual functioning and adaptive
functioning.
53. A child argues with adults, loses temper, and is spiteful but has not engaged in serious
aggression, theft, or rights violations. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. ADHD
       Answer: B. Oppositional defiant disorder
   Rationale: ODD is characterized by angry/irritable mood, argumentative/defiant behavior, and
vindictiveness without severe rights violations.

54. A 15-year-old has repeatedly bullied younger peers, stolen items, destroyed property, and
violated rules. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Oppositional defiant disorder
   B. Conduct disorder
   C. Adjustment disorder

 D. Bipolar II disorder
       Answer: B. Conduct disorder
   Rationale: Bullying, theft, property destruction, and serious rule violations are classic conduct
disorder features.

55. A 24-year-old has recurrent impulsive verbal and physical outbursts grossly out of proportion
to provocation and later feels remorse. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Antisocial personality disorder
   B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   C. Conduct disorder

 D. Oppositional defiant disorder
       Answer: B. Intermittent explosive disorder
   Rationale: IED features recurrent impulsive aggressive outbursts disproportionate to
provocation.

56. Which disorder is classified under substance-related and addictive disorders without
involving ingestion of a psychoactive substance?

   A. Pyromania
   B. Kleptomania
   C. Gambling disorder

 D. Trichotillomania
       Answer: C. Gambling disorder
   Rationale: Gambling disorder is the notable non-substance behavioral addiction classified
with substance-related and addictive disorders.

57. Which statement BEST describes substance use disorder in DSM-style diagnosis?
   A. It is diagnosed solely by quantity consumed
   B. It is based on maladaptive pattern causing impairment or distress
   C. It requires tolerance and withdrawal in all cases
 D. It excludes behavioral criteria
       Answer: B. It is based on maladaptive pattern causing impairment or distress
   Rationale: Substance use disorder is diagnosed from a maladaptive pattern with clinically
significant impairment or distress across criteria.

58. A patient becomes disoriented and has fluctuating attention over hours after a severe
infection. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Major neurocognitive disorder
   B. Delirium
   C. Dissociative amnesia

 D. Schizophrenia
       Answer: B. Delirium
   Rationale: Acute onset, fluctuating course, and disturbed attention following infection strongly
indicate delirium.

59. A client has gradual decline in memory and executive function that interferes with
independence. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Delirium
   B. Mild neurocognitive disorder
   C. Major neurocognitive disorder

 D. Dissociative disorder
       Answer: C. Major neurocognitive disorder
   Rationale: Cognitive decline severe enough to interfere with independence indicates major
neurocognitive disorder.

60. Which feature BEST distinguishes delirium from major neurocognitive disorder?
   A. Presence of memory loss
   B. Acute onset and fluctuating course of disturbed attention
   C. Age of onset over 65

 D. Need for medical assessment
       Answer: B. Acute onset and fluctuating course of disturbed attention
   Rationale: That combination is the classic distinguishing feature of delirium.

61. A person with borderline personality disorder is MOST likely to show which pattern?
   A. Restricted emotional expression and detachment
   B. Grandiosity without instability
   C. Instability in relationships, self-image, and affect with impulsivity

 D. Chronic rule violation without remorse only
       Answer: C. Instability in relationships, self-image, and affect with impulsivity
   Rationale: That cluster is central to borderline personality disorder.

62. Which personality disorder is MOST associated with disregard for and violation of the rights
of others?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Dependent personality disorder
       Answer: B. Antisocial personality disorder
   Rationale: ASPD is defined by disregard for and violation of others' rights.

63. A man is socially detached, prefers solitary activities, and appears indifferent to praise or
criticism. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Schizotypal personality disorder

 D. Major depressive disorder
       Answer: A. Schizoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Detachment from social relationships and restricted emotional expression suggest
schizoid personality disorder.

64. A client has odd beliefs, eccentric behavior, and social discomfort but not sustained
psychosis. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Autism spectrum disorder
       Answer: A. Schizotypal personality disorder
   Rationale: Odd beliefs, eccentricity, and interpersonal discomfort without persistent psychosis
are characteristic of schizotypal personality disorder.

65. A woman avoids relationships because of fear of criticism and rejection despite wanting
closeness. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Schizoid personality disorder
   B. Dependent personality disorder
   C. Avoidant personality disorder

 D. Social anxiety disorder only
       Answer: C. Avoidant personality disorder
   Rationale: Desire for relationships combined with avoidance due to fear of criticism supports
avoidant personality disorder.

66. A client is submissive, has difficulty making everyday decisions without reassurance, and
fears being left to care for self. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Avoidant personality disorder
   C. Dependent personality disorder

 D. Histrionic personality disorder
       Answer: C. Dependent personality disorder
   Rationale: Excessive need to be taken care of, reassurance-seeking, and fear of separation
characterize dependent personality disorder.

67. Which personality disorder is MOST characterized by preoccupation with orderliness,
perfectionism, and control at the expense of flexibility?

   A. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   B. Obsessive-compulsive disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Paranoid personality disorder
       Answer: A. Obsessive-compulsive personality disorder
   Rationale: OCPD is a personality pattern of perfectionism, rigidity, and control.

68. A client has recurrent intense sexual arousal from exposing genitals to unsuspecting
strangers. Which diagnosis is MOST likely if it causes distress or has been acted upon with a
nonconsenting person?

   A. Fetishistic disorder
   B. Exhibitionistic disorder
   C. Voyeuristic disorder

 D. Transvestic disorder
       Answer: B. Exhibitionistic disorder
   Rationale: Exposing one's genitals to unsuspecting strangers is the core exhibitionistic
pattern when disorder criteria are met.

69. A client experiences recurrent sexual arousal from observing unsuspecting persons who are
naked or engaging in sexual activity. Which diagnosis is MOST likely if disorder criteria are met?

   A. Voyeuristic disorder
   B. Sexual masochism disorder
   C. Fetishistic disorder

 D. Pedophilic disorder
       Answer: A. Voyeuristic disorder
   Rationale: Secret observation of unsuspecting nude or sexually active persons defines
voyeuristic disorder when criteria are met.

70. Which statement BEST reflects the distinction between a paraphilia and a paraphilic
disorder?

   A. They are identical terms
   B. A paraphilic disorder requires distress, impairment, or harm/risk to others
   C. A paraphilia always involves criminal behavior

 D. A paraphilic disorder is diagnosed only in women
       Answer: B. A paraphilic disorder requires distress, impairment, or harm/risk to others
   Rationale: The distinction is that atypical sexual interest alone is not enough; clinically
significant distress, impairment, or harm/risk is required for disorder.
71. A child assigned male at birth persistently insists "I am a girl," is distressed by male sex
characteristics, and wants to be treated as female. Which diagnosis is MOST relevant if
clinically significant distress is present?

   A. Transvestic disorder
   B. Gender dysphoria
   C. Body dysmorphic disorder

 D. Histrionic personality disorder
       Answer: B. Gender dysphoria
   Rationale: Marked incongruence between experienced gender and assigned sex with
clinically significant distress indicates gender dysphoria.

72. Which of the following BEST exemplifies a multidimensional or integrative approach to
psychopathology?

   A. Explaining depression solely by one neurotransmitter deficit
   B. Explaining anxiety only by parenting style
   C. Viewing disorder as arising from interacting biological, psychological, and social influences

 D. Rejecting diagnosis entirely
       Answer: C. Viewing disorder as arising from interacting biological, psychological, and
social influences
   Rationale: That is the essence of an integrative, multidimensional model of psychopathology.

73. Which research method is MOST appropriate for examining whether childhood trauma
predicts later depression without manipulating trauma exposure?

   A. Experimental design
   B. Correlational longitudinal study
   C. Case report only

 D. Single blind drug trial
       Answer: B. Correlational longitudinal study
   Rationale: A longitudinal correlational design can examine prediction over time when
manipulation would be unethical.

74. In research, the ethical principle of informed consent MOST directly requires that
participants:

   A. Receive payment
   B. Agree only after understandable disclosure of relevant information
   C. Be randomly assigned

 D. Know the study hypothesis in full detail always
       Answer: B. Agree only after understandable disclosure of relevant information
   Rationale: Informed consent requires understandable disclosure and voluntary agreement by
competent participants.

75. Which assessment method is MOST useful for obtaining detailed symptom history, onset,
and psychosocial context?

   A. Clinical interview
   B. EEG
   C. MRI

 D. Projective drawing only
       Answer: A. Clinical interview
   Rationale: The clinical interview is central for gathering symptom history, onset, course, and
context.

76. Which statement about diagnosis is MOST accurate?
   A. Diagnosis should ignore impairment if symptoms are unusual
   B. Diagnosis relies only on laboratory tests
   C. Clinical significance and differential diagnosis are both important

 D. Diagnosis is unnecessary when treatment is available
       Answer: C. Clinical significance and differential diagnosis are both important
   Rationale: Accurate diagnosis requires both symptom fit and determination that symptoms
are clinically significant while ruling out alternatives.

77. A psychometrician is asked to independently provide psychotherapy for severe PTSD
without training or license for such work. Under RA 10029-aligned ethical principles, the BEST
action is to:

   A. Proceed because the client is in distress
   B. Provide treatment and learn during sessions
   C. Decline beyond competence and make an appropriate referral

 D. Ask a friend for informal tips and continue
       Answer: C. Decline beyond competence and make an appropriate referral
   Rationale: Ethical practice requires working within competence and referring when services
exceed training or legal scope.

78. Which ethical principle is MOST directly violated when a practitioner shares a client's trauma
disclosure with coworkers for casual conversation?

   A. Beneficence
   B. Confidentiality
   C. Test standardization

 D. Debriefing
       Answer: B. Confidentiality
   Rationale: Casually sharing private client information violates the obligation to protect
confidentiality.

79. A court orders psychological services. Before proceeding, the practitioner should MOST
importantly:

   A. Promise absolute confidentiality
   B. Explain the nature of services and limits of confidentiality
   C. Refuse all services

 D. Begin therapy immediately without discussion
       Answer: B. Explain the nature of services and limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: When services are court-ordered, the individual should be informed of the nature
of services and confidentiality limits.

80. A practitioner agrees to evaluate an employee at the request of a company. Ethically, the
practitioner should clarify at the outset:

   A. Only the fee
   B. Who the client is, the role of the evaluator, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
   C. Only the diagnosis

 D. Only whether treatment will be free
       Answer: B. Who the client is, the role of the evaluator, probable uses of information, and
limits of confidentiality
   Rationale: Third-party requests require clear role clarification at the outset.

81. Which action BEST reflects ethical management of competence?
   A. Accepting all referrals to build experience
   B. Practicing only within education, training, supervision, and experience
   C. Using internet summaries instead of formal training

 D. Delegating all difficult cases to students without supervision
       Answer: B. Practicing only within education, training, supervision, and experience
   Rationale: Boundaries of competence are fundamental to ethical practice.

82. A practitioner develops strong personal attraction toward a current therapy client and begins
pursuing a romantic relationship. This is BEST described as:

   A. Harmless boundary crossing
   B. Ethical because both are consenting adults
   C. Exploitative and unethical multiple relationship

 D. Acceptable if therapy is going well
       Answer: C. Exploitative and unethical multiple relationship
   Rationale: Romantic involvement with a current therapy client is exploitative because of the
power imbalance and risk of harm.

83. A licensed practitioner's personal problems are seriously impairing judgment in sessions.
The BEST ethical response is to:

   A. Ignore the issue to avoid stigma
   B. Continue practice as usual
   C. Seek consultation/assistance and limit, suspend, or terminate affected duties as needed

 D. Transfer all records to friends
       Answer: C. Seek consultation/assistance and limit, suspend, or terminate affected duties
as needed
   Rationale: Practitioners must address impairing personal problems to protect clients and
maintain competence.

84. Which statement BEST reflects an ethical approach to delegated work?
   A. Any assistant may perform any task if convenient
   B. Only tasks matched to the assistant's competence and supervision should be delegated
   C. Delegation eliminates responsibility of the psychologist

 D. Delegation requires no client knowledge
       Answer: B. Only tasks matched to the assistant's competence and supervision should be
delegated
   Rationale: Delegation must match the individual's training and the level of supervision
provided.

85. A psychologist receives a referral involving telepsychology services in an area new to her.
The MOST ethical step is to:

   A. Proceed because online work is informal
   B. Obtain relevant training, consultation, or supervised experience first
   C. Refuse all future online work permanently

 D. Ask the client to teach her
       Answer: B. Obtain relevant training, consultation, or supervised experience first
   Rationale: New modalities require efforts to build competence before practice.

86. Which diagnosis is MOST associated with pervasive suspiciousness such that others'
motives are interpreted as malevolent?

   A. Paranoid personality disorder
   B. Schizoid personality disorder
   C. Narcissistic personality disorder

 D. Avoidant personality disorder
       Answer: A. Paranoid personality disorder
   Rationale: Pervasive distrust and interpreting motives as malevolent are core paranoid
personality features.

87. A client displays grandiosity, needs admiration, and lacks empathy. Which diagnosis is
MOST likely?

   A. Borderline personality disorder
   B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   C. Dependent personality disorder

 D. Schizotypal personality disorder
       Answer: B. Narcissistic personality disorder
   Rationale: Grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy define narcissistic
personality disorder.

88. Which personality disorder is MOST associated with excessive emotionality and attention
seeking?

   A. Histrionic personality disorder
   B. Antisocial personality disorder
   C. OCPD
   D. Paranoid personality disorder
  Answer: A. Histrionic personality disorder

   Rationale: Excessive emotionality and attention seeking are classic histrionic personality
features.

89. A patient with depression also reports brief periods of unusually elevated mood, reduced
need for sleep, and increased goal-directed activity that never caused marked impairment.
Which diagnosis should be carefully considered?

   A. Persistent depressive disorder
   B. Bipolar II disorder
   C. Delusional disorder

 D. Schizoid personality disorder
       Answer: B. Bipolar II disorder
   Rationale: Depression with clear hypomanic periods should prompt careful consideration of
bipolar II disorder rather than unipolar depression alone.

90. A client presents with first-onset psychosis at age 68. Which differential diagnosis issue is
ESPECIALLY important?

   A. Rule out another medical condition
   B. Assume schizophrenia immediately
   C. Ignore medication effects

 D. Diagnose delusional disorder first without assessment
       Answer: A. Rule out another medical condition
   Rationale: Late-onset psychosis raises strong concern for medical or neurological causes and
requires careful medical differential diagnosis.

91. A patient with severe alcohol intoxication reports hallucinations during heavy use. Which is
the BEST diagnostic principle?

   A. Primary psychotic disorder is always diagnosed first
   B. Consider substance-induced etiology before concluding a primary psychotic disorder
   C. Hallucinations rule out substance effects

 D. Alcohol cannot produce psychotic symptoms
       Answer: B. Consider substance-induced etiology before concluding a primary psychotic
disorder
   Rationale: Heavy substance use can directly produce hallucinations and psychotic symptoms,
so substance-induced causes must be evaluated first.

92. A client with panic symptoms also has hyperthyroidism. Which differential diagnosis
question is MOST crucial?

   A. Whether the client has a personality disorder
   B. Whether the medical condition directly accounts for the anxiety symptoms
   C. Whether the client likes treatment

 D. Whether the client has a sleep disorder
       Answer: B. Whether the medical condition directly accounts for the anxiety symptoms
   Rationale: A key differential diagnosis step is determining whether a medical condition directly
causes the psychiatric presentation.

93. Which diagnosis would BEST fit a person whose grief reaction remains severe, prolonged,
and maladaptive far beyond expected cultural norms?

   A. Uncomplicated bereavement only
   B. Prolonged grief disorder
   C. Specific phobia

 D. Delirium
       Answer: B. Prolonged grief disorder
   Rationale: Persistent, impairing, maladaptive grief beyond expected cultural norms points
toward prolonged grief disorder.

94. Which symptom is MOST characteristic of catatonia?
   A. Flight of ideas
   B. Waxy flexibility or mutism
   C. Fear of contamination

 D. Grandiosity
       Answer: B. Waxy flexibility or mutism
   Rationale: Catatonia is associated with psychomotor abnormalities such as mutism, stupor,
negativism, posturing, or waxy flexibility.

95. A person repeatedly steals unneeded items and experiences tension before the theft and
relief afterward. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Kleptomania
   C. Antisocial personality disorder

 D. Malingering
       Answer: B. Kleptomania
   Rationale: Recurrent failure to resist stealing unneeded objects with tension before and relief
after is characteristic of kleptomania.

96. A person deliberately sets fires on multiple occasions and feels fascination and tension
related to fire, without external gain. Which diagnosis is MOST likely?

   A. Conduct disorder
   B. Pyromania
   C. Intermittent explosive disorder

 D. Mania
       Answer: B. Pyromania
   Rationale: Deliberate fire-setting driven by fascination, tension, and relief without external
reward indicates pyromania.

97. Which statement BEST distinguishes obsessions from delusions?
   A. Obsessions are always culturally sanctioned
   B. Obsessions are intrusive recurrent thoughts often recognized as one's own and excessive
   C. Delusions are always brief

 D. Obsessions never lead to rituals
       Answer: B. Obsessions are intrusive recurrent thoughts often recognized as one's own
and excessive
   Rationale: Obsessions are experienced as intrusive, unwanted thoughts, urges, or images,
unlike delusions, which are fixed false beliefs.

98. Which statement BEST reflects the boundary between disorder and no mental disorder?
   A. Any unusual behavior is a disorder
   B. A symptom becomes a disorder only when it causes clinically significant distress or

impairment and fits diagnostic criteria
   C. Distress is irrelevant if family members are worried

 D. Diagnosis should be given whenever possible
       Answer: B. A symptom becomes a disorder only when it causes clinically significant
distress or impairment and fits diagnostic criteria
   Rationale: Diagnosis requires more than unusuality; symptoms must meet criteria and be
clinically significant.

99. A psychometrician notices that an unlicensed coworker is administering psychological
services beyond legal scope. The MOST appropriate response is to:

   A. Ignore it to protect workplace harmony
   B. Join the practice to help
   C. Address or report the ethical/legal concern through appropriate channels

 D. Publicly shame the coworker online
       Answer: C. Address or report the ethical/legal concern through appropriate channels
   Rationale: Ethical responsibility includes taking appropriate action when substantial harm or
unlawful practice may occur.

100. A clinician is evaluating self-injury. Which question BEST helps distinguish nonsuicidal
self-injury from a suicide attempt?

    A. Whether the person used a sharp object
    B. Whether there was intent to die
    C. Whether the person is female

 D. Whether the injury required stitches
        Answer: B. Whether there was intent to die
    Rationale: Suicidal intent is the key factor distinguishing a suicide attempt from nonsuicidal
self-injury.
